url,title,category,contenthttps://www.coinbureau.com/Analysis/is-monero-anonymous/,Is Monero Anonymous? How Untraceable is XMR? ,Analysis,"<p>In blockchain design, anonymity and pseudonymity are analogous principles. The Bitcoin network is a pseudonymous blockchain, meaning the transactions are recorded in an open ledger that anyone can view, but personal information about the sender and receiver is not readily transparent. However, advancements in blockchain analysis have led to Bitcoin transactions being easily traceable, with blockchain analytics companies being able to figure out which addresses belong to which people, making Bitcoin Pseudonymous, but not anonymous.</p><p>A couple of prominent techniques involve revealing the real identities of Bitcoin users by connecting the dots between publicly available transaction metadata such as addresses, timestamps and amounts with the user’s IP address. Even when they use separate addresses for every transaction, one can backtrack the transfers to their root with metadata.</p><div class=""raw-html-embed""><style>\n.code-block-important {\n    background: var(--binance-card-background-color);\n}\n.code-block-important blockquote {\n    margin-left: 0;\n    font-size: 14px;\n    font-weight: 500;\n    padding-left: 30px;\n    line-height: 1.75rem;\n    margin-block-end: 2em;\n    letter-spacing: 0.04em;\n    word-break: break-word;\n    margin-block-start: 0em;\n    border-left: 3px solid orange;\n}\n.code-block-important-description-div{\n    font-weignt:800px;\n    padding: 8px 8px 8px 0px;\n}\n</style>\n<div class=""code-block-important"">\n    <blockquote>\n        <div class=""code-block-important-description-div""><b>Important: </b>IP address tracing is the process of identifying the origin and location of an internet user by analyzing their unique IP address. It has been around since the early days of the internet, dating back to the 1970s and 1980s, and is used in network diagnostics, cybersecurity, and law enforcement.</div>\n    </blockquote>\n</div> </div><p>In light of such loopholes, the Monero network was born as a fork of a project known as “Bytecoin” in April 2014. Monero is one of the earliest blockchains to advocate complete anonymity, which entailed addressing the anonymity weaknesses plaguing networks like Bitcoin.</p><p><a href=""/deals/wallet/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg"" alt=""Crypto-Wallets-Design Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>This article is a primer on understanding Monero’s Anonymity and learning how to use it efficiently. If you are curious about the nuances between Monero and Bitcoin, we explore those granular differences in an article&nbsp;in our <a href=""/analysis/monero-vs-bitcoin/"">Bitcoin vs Monero</a>. I suggest checking out Coin Bureau’s&nbsp;learner on the <a href=""/education/what-is-monero/"">Monero Protocol</a> to refresh your concepts. However, here’s a <strong>TLDR of Monero:</strong></p><h2>What is Monero?</h2><p>Monero is the first privacy-focused and&nbsp;<a href=""https://www.bitdegree.org/crypto/learn/crypto-terms/what-is-censorship-resistance"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">censorship-resistant</a> blockchain. Every Monero blockchain user and their transactions are anonymous by default. Two essential characteristics are the cornerstone of the Monero Protocol:</p><ul><li><strong>Untraceability&nbsp;</strong>- All possible senders are equiprobable for each incoming transaction.</li><li><strong>Unlinkability&nbsp;</strong>- It is impossible to prove any two transactions were sent to the same person.</li></ul><p>Despite such anonymity, anyone can cryptographically verify the correct execution of a transaction on the Monero blockchain with transaction proofs recorded in the&nbsp;<a href=""https://localmonero.co/blocks/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">public database</a>.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Monero_Transactions_are_Private_4fcf988698.jpg"" alt=""Monero Transactions are Private.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Monero_Transactions_are_Private_4fcf988698.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Monero_Transactions_are_Private_4fcf988698.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Monero_Transactions_are_Private_4fcf988698.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Monero_Transactions_are_Private_4fcf988698.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>A Monero Explorer transaction snapshot. The blockchain hides sensitive details.</figcaption></figure><p><strong>Key features of the Monero blockchain include:</strong></p><h3>Privacy</h3><p>Monero is the strongest proponent of privacy. The network anonymizes transaction amounts and obfuscates sender and receiver identities with cryptographic techniques like <a href=""https://serhack.me/articles/what-is-stealth-address-technology-monero/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">stealth addresses</a> and <a href=""https://www.getmonero.org/resources/moneropedia/ringsignatures.html"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">ring signatures</a>.</p><h3>Security</h3><p>Monero is a permissionless and decentralized&nbsp;<a href=""/analysis/proof-of-work-vs-proof-of-stake/"">Proof-of-Work</a> protocol. Therefore, it benefits from the security properties of similar networks, like no central authority and no control over transaction data or user’s personal information.</p><h3>Equitable Mining</h3><p>Monero uses a unique POW mining algorithm called&nbsp;<strong>RandomX&nbsp;</strong>that is ASIC-resistant. Here is what it means -&nbsp;</p><p>The Bitcoin network follows a “one CPU - one vote” policy in its mining protocol. This logic proved sufficiently equitable in the early days of the network when the hashing power required to run the network was shallow and affordable. However, as the network grew in adoption, specialized hardware called <a href=""https://en.bitcoin.it/wiki/ASIC"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">ASICs</a> emerged. ASICs are custom-built for mining and solving hash functions efficiently. Bitcoin mining has since become a race to acquire the most potent ASICs, where every CPU is undoubtedly not equitable, leading to the centralization of mining activity in pools and places with cheap electricity.</p><h4>Monero ASIC-Resistant Mining</h4><p>The RandomX mining algorithm constantly updates its code to maintain ASIC resistance. RandomX deploys RAM-heavy techniques to make mining memory intensive. Adding RAM to ASICs is expensive and complex. The memory-hard nature of RandomX outweighs the benefits of deploying expensive ASICs over conventional CPUs, democratizing its consensus process.</p><h3>Adaptive Block Size</h3><p>Monero’s adaptive block size adjusts based on transaction volume, ensuring that mining remains efficient and the network can scale with demand. This feature ensures that transactions are processed on time, even during high demand, benefiting all network participants.</p><h3>IP Address Privacy (Under Development)</h3><p><a href=""https://web.getmonero.org/resources/moneropedia/kovri.html"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Kovri</a> is a decentralized anonymity technology designed to help hide the IP addresses of participants of the Monero blockchain. IP addresses can reveal the user’s location and real-world identity. Therefore, Kovri enhances the privacy of Monero. Kovri hides IP by encrypting user internet traffic.&nbsp;</p><p>Another subtle design aspect of Monero is its 2-minute transaction confirmation time, which takes about ten minutes to achieve finality. The Monero development team frequently forks the network to add new privacy features. Let’s discuss how Monero works:</p><h2>How Monero Works</h2><p>Monero is a peer-to-peer digital cash network with use cases adjacent to Bitcoin with enhanced privacy techniques. Monero tracks XMR exchanges like Bitcoin as Unspent Transaction Outputs (<a href=""/blockchain/unspent-transaction-output-utxo/"">UTXOs</a>). However, the process of sending and receiving UTXOs is designed to preserve the anonymity of the involved parties. There are three major components at work to achieve this:</p><h3>Ring Signatures: Anonymizing Senders</h3><p>A traditional transaction involves the sender signing the transaction with their private key. Ring signature is an upgraded digital signature on Monero where the actual signature mixes with a bunch of decoy signatures for obfuscation. The decoys are picked from past signed outputs on Monero. The idea behind the setup is that since the actual signer is indistinguishable from the decoys, all pose an equiprobable chance of being real, so no one can know which one is real with absolute certainty.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/How_Monero_hides_sender_s_identity_1201d0074f.jpg"" alt=""How Monero is anonymous"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_How_Monero_hides_sender_s_identity_1201d0074f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_How_Monero_hides_sender_s_identity_1201d0074f.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_How_Monero_hides_sender_s_identity_1201d0074f.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_How_Monero_hides_sender_s_identity_1201d0074f.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Ring signature design as illustrated by&nbsp;<a href=""https://messari.io/report/on-chain-privacy"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Messari</a></figcaption></figure><h3>Stealth Address: Anonymizing Receivers</h3><p>Transaction linkability and address reuse are among the most exploited aspects in denonymizing users of Bitcoin. Even if a new public address is used to send every transaction, the links between them can be traced back to the original owner.</p><p>Monero proposes a solution where users may publicize a single public address and receive unconditional unlinkable payments on the address. It achieves this by sending every transaction output to a public address derived from the sender’s data and the recipient’s public address, called a&nbsp;<strong>stealth address.</strong></p><p>To send a transaction output, the sender first creates a one-time destination key using a part of the recipient’s public address and other critical cryptographic primitives. The sender publishes the output publicly. Now, users constantly scan all new transaction outputs with their public key.&nbsp;</p><p>The cryptographic primitives are designed such that the rightful recipient can claim their outputs in the network, effectively unlinking the transactions on Menoro.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Monero_Stealth_Transaction_Model_c85869d364.jpg"" alt=""Monero Stealth Transactions"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Monero_Stealth_Transaction_Model_c85869d364.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Monero_Stealth_Transaction_Model_c85869d364.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Monero_Stealth_Transaction_Model_c85869d364.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Monero_Stealth_Transaction_Model_c85869d364.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Monero stealth transaction model | Image via&nbsp;<a href=""https://github.com/monero-project/research-lab/blob/master/whitepaper/whitepaper.pdf"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">CryptoNote Whitepaper</a></figcaption></figure><h3>Ring Confidential Transactions (RingCT)</h3><p>Monero uses a cryptographic tool called&nbsp;<strong>confidential transactions</strong> to hide the amount of XMR transferred in each transaction. Confidentiality is achieved by encrypting the transaction amounts; only the sender and receiver, who hold the necessary keys, can view the actual amounts.</p><p>RingCT combines the concepts of ring signatures and confidential transactions to hide both the sender’s identity and the transaction amount simultaneously. This enhancement ensures that transactions are verified and recorded on the blockchain while the sender, receiver, and amount remain private.</p><p>Feel free to check out our other resources on Monero if you want to get into the weeds of everything Monero-related:</p><ul><li><a href=""/guides/how-to-use-monero/"">How to Use Monero Guide</a></li><li><a href=""/mining/monero-home/"">How to Mine Monero</a></li><li><a href=""/education/mining-monero/"">Is Mining Monero Still Profitable?</a></li><li><a href=""/mining/best-monero-pools/"">Best Monero Mining Pools</a></li><li><a href=""/analysis/best-monero-wallets/"">Top Monero Wallets</a></li></ul><p>If you want Guy's take on Monero, that can be found in the video below:</p><figure class=""media""><div data-oembed-url=""https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=b7BP6hU7AQw""><div style=""position: relative; padding-bottom: 100%; height: 0; padding-bottom: 56.2493%;""><iframe src=""https://www.youtube.com/embed/b7BP6hU7AQw"" style=""position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; top: 0; left: 0;"" frameborder=""0"" allow=""autoplay; encrypted-media"" allowfullscreen=""""></iframe></div></div></figure><h2>Monero vs. Other Networks</h2><p>Blockchain designs are a game of tradeoffs. There is no “<a href=""/analysis/solving-blockchain-trilemma/"">have it all</a>” blockchain perfect for every use case while adhering to all ideal design principles. Monero is no exception. The privacy features it offers are at a cost; let us compare Monero, Bitcoin, and Ethereum for a deeper look.</p><h3>Transaction Speed</h3><p>Transactions on Monero are relatively fast. The average block time (time required to produce a new block) is two minutes. Monero reduces the likelihood of congestion and delayed transactions with its variable block size, which can accommodate more transactions if needed.</p><p>The block time of Bitcoin and Ethereum is 10 minutes and about 13 seconds on average. Bitcoin owes its slow block time to its power-hungry but robust consensus. While Ethereum transactions are faster, they are also more in number due to smart contract support.</p><h3>Fees</h3><p>Transaction fees on Monero may vary with demand but are generally reasonable. The protocol can regulate fees by altering its block size to fit more or fewer transactions. The lack of smart contract support means only XMR transfers are possible on the chain, which helps keep fees down.</p><p>Bitcoin and Ethereum are known to have periods of escalated fees during high demand. Unlike Monero, Bitcoin operates within a limited block capacity, making fees a direct function of demand. The fees on Ethereum are gas-dependent, meaning the fee is regulated based on the processing power spent by the network in producing blocks. Bitcoin and Ethereum have a history of exorbitant fee spikes.</p><h3>Scalability</h3><p>Monero features an adaptive block size that adjusts to transaction volume, offering flexible scalability. Monero’s privacy design requires the address to be twice as large as Bitcoin's, and ring signatures combine multiple signatures into one.&nbsp;</p><p>The privacy features on Monero impose heavy storage requirements on Monero. While a variable block size helps with scalability, each transaction on Monero is significantly bulkier than in Ethereum or Bitcoin.</p><p>Ethereum and Bitcoin have transcended their monolithic design to improve scalability. <a href=""/technology/lightning-network/"">Lightning Network</a> on Bitcoin and the <a href=""/analysis/what-is-the-best-layer-2/"">layer-2 ecosystem</a> of Ethereum are some scalability solutions available today.</p><h3>Privacy</h3><p>Monero transactions are private by default. Ring signatures and stealth addresses are so great at obfuscating transactions a user needs to publicize their transactions to dilute privacy intentionally.</p><p>Bitcoin and Ethereum are pseudonymous, meaning transactions are traceable and public. However, Ethereum has the potential for programmed privacy with smart contracts, which Bitcoin lacks.</p><p><i><strong><u>Fun Fact:</u></strong></i> Monero has been so successful at remaining untraceable that the IRS <a href=""https://www.forbes.com/sites/kellyphillipserb/2020/09/14/irs-will-pay-up-to-625000-if-you-can-crack-monero-other-privacy-coins/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">offered a $625,000 reward</a> in 2020 to anyone who could crack the anonymity features of XMR. To date, nobody has.</p><h3>Mining</h3><p>Monero is a POW blockchain like Bitcoin. The former deploys the RandomX mining algorithm, while the latter uses a SHA-256 algorithm. RandomX facilitates memory-based mining, which is not resource-intensive. In contrast, mining Bitcoin entails solving hash functions, best done with expensive and resource-hungry ASICs. Ethereum is a POS blockchain that replaces computational power with steep monetary requirements.</p><p>The variable block capacity and signature design make Monero a memory-heavy chain, imposing heavy resource requirements on nodes and potentially leading to centralization with time.</p><h2>How to Use Monero Anonymously&nbsp;</h2><p>Achieving absolute digital anonymity is a monumental feat. Everyday users like you and I cannot even begin to realize the traces we leave behind on the internet, even when we are confident about our anonymity.&nbsp;</p><p>Therefore, iterating the speculativeness of anonymity is essential to discuss before delving into this section. The steps and precautions described in the following text must not be considered absolute or infallible. I encourage users to perceive it more like a set of guidelines to help you conduct self-due diligence that achieves reliable anonymity in your setting. Let’s explore what it takes to be anonymous in Web3.</p><p>A general practice for anonymity and general online security is using a VPN to mask your identity and encrypt your internet communication. <a href=""https://go.coinbureau.com/expressvpn"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener nofollow"">Sign up for a good VPN</a> service before exploring the steps described below. A VPN will help you hide your IP address, which is essential for hiding your location and personal identity.</p><h3>Creating an Anonymous XMR Wallet</h3><p>You first need an anonymous XMR wallet to obtain, store, and transact XMR. Look for a wallet that respects user privacy and demands little or no personal information. Avoid online wallets and privately controlled wallets like the ones offered by centralized exchanges.</p><p>Cold hardware wallets are effective at maintaining anonymity. Many prominent wallet providers like&nbsp;<a href=""/analysis/ledger-nano-x-trezor-model-t/"">Ledger and Trezor</a> support XMR. You can also consider using Monero GUI or CLI from GetMonero.org. Explore our detailed&nbsp;guide on <a href=""/analysis/best-monero-wallets/"">Monero wallets</a> for more details.</p><p>Remember that when you buy a hardware wallet online, any identity you provide, like your name, email, address, or fiat payment channels, breaches anonymity to some extent, which is why I believe achieving absolute anonymity is extraordinarily difficult in the digital age.</p><h3>Obtaining XMR</h3><p>Cryptocurrency exchanges are the most convenient platforms for acquiring cryptocurrencies. The general practice involves registering with an exchange and buying crypto with fiat. Then, most exchanges allow withdrawals to on-chain wallets.&nbsp;</p><p>This centralized exchange (CEX) approach is a no-go for us. Most exchanges impose KYC requirements and AML (Anti Money Laundering) verifications, breaking anonymity. You could look for CEXs that do not demand KYC. Consider verifying the legitimacy of any KYC-less exchange you may find.</p><p>P2P exchanges connect buyers and sellers without offering exchange and custodial services themselves. Therefore, they can circumvent imposing KYC requirements on their users.&nbsp;<a href=""https://localmonero.co/?language=en"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Localmonero</a> is a well-known P2P exchange where you can buy XMR with various fiat and crypto options. Avoid fiat to protect anonymity; crypto options like BTC and ETH are ideal.&nbsp;</p><p>Once you have some XMR, transfer it to a new address. Transferring to a new stealth address will break the link with our external purchase using stealth transactions. The process of sending XMR to yourself multiple times to obfuscate identity is called&nbsp;‘churning.’ You could also consider <a href=""/education/mining-monero/"">mining XMR</a> so that you never leave the Monero ecosystem and potentially leave digital traces following you.&nbsp;</p><h2>Risks of Using Monero</h2><p>Privacy-focused blockchain projects deal with considerable heat from regulatory authorities. They also have a history of facilitating illicit exchanges of money and goods worldwide. Some risks you should consider before using Monero are as follows:</p><h3>Regulatory Risk</h3><p>Given its privacy-centric nature, Monero has been associated with illicit activities such as money laundering and illegal transactions on the dark web, leading to increased scrutiny from regulatory bodies worldwide. In some countries, the use of privacy coins like Monero is heavily regulated or even banned. This regulatory risk could impact the value and usability of Monero.&nbsp;</p><h3>Market Volatility</h3><p>Like all cryptocurrencies, Monero is subject to high market volatility. The value of XMR can fluctuate wildly in a short period, which can lead to significant financial losses for investors who are not prepared for such volatility.</p><h3>Technological Risks</h3><p>Monero's privacy features rely on complex cryptographic techniques. If these techniques were to be compromised, they could expose user transaction data. Additionally, as with any digital asset, there's the risk of loss due to hacking, phishing, or other cyber attacks.</p><h3>Liquidity Risk</h3><p>Monero's controversial reputation may limit its adoption by mainstream businesses and consumers, affecting the coin's liquidity and making it harder to buy or sell without impacting the market price.</p><h3>Others Risks</h3><p>Using Monero requires a certain level of technical knowledge. Mistakes in handling wallet keys or transaction details can lead to irreversible loss of funds. Furthermore, as a POW protocol, Monero consumes energy, leading to environmental stress in running the network.</p><p><a href=""https://hub.coinbureau.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg"" alt=""Join-The-CoinBureau-Club-Inline-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Final Thoughts</h2><blockquote><p>""I don't want to live in a world where everything that I say, everything I do, everyone I talk to, every expression of creativity, love, or friendship is recorded"" - <a href=""https://www.theguardian.com/world/2013/jul/08/edward-snowden-surveillance-excess-interview"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Edward Snowden.</a></p></blockquote><p>Edward Snowden, a former NSA contractor, famously highlighted the importance of privacy and anonymity in a world increasingly under surveillance.&nbsp;</p><p>Monero, a blockchain protocol fundamentally anchored to the principle of privacy, is a testament to Edward’s remarks. It is designed to obscure transactions to make them confidential and untraceable with cryptography. Monero provides a space for financial transactions without the intrusion of surveillance. The freedom from constant regulatory overwatch is an essential defense against conformity, obedience, and submission.&nbsp;</p><p>While it is impossible to predict the prospects of Monero with certainty, we can ponder the factors that may shape its near and distant future. As a cryptocurrency, it is subject to macroeconomic uncertainty, regulatory crackdowns, and forces of supply and demand.&nbsp;</p><p>As a privacy-focused technology, it has a few trends going its way. Digital privacy is a growing concern, and demand for robust privacy-focused financial networks could increase. I also see Monero’s potential in privacy-focused industries, where the networks concern a specific class of individuals. For instance, corporations may use Monero as a private network of intra-department transfers. Legal services and healthcare might find Monero’s privacy appealing for personal connectivity of sensitive data that may not concern the general public. Monero's future is a balance between its prospects as a leading privacy coin and the challenges it faces from regulatory, environmental, and technological perspectives.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Review/render-network-review/,Render Network Review: Next-Level Decentralized Computing,Review,"<p>I own a PlayStation VR 2 headset. As I slip into the virtual realm, I'm transported to fantastical worlds where I embark on thrilling adventures, slaying robots and battling formidable foes. The adrenaline rush that comes with each encounter, the sharp focus required to solve intricate puzzles, and the immersive feeling of paddling down virtual rivers while kayaking, are thrilling.</p><p>But behind my experiences of exhilaration and delight lie certain challenges faced by the thousands of people creating these virtual worlds. The demand for more intricate visuals in animations and VR experiences necessitates external servers and additional resources, leading to increased rendering complexity. Despite this demand, the centralized GPU cloud faces limitations due to high upfront investments and rapid hardware depreciation, resulting in high costs and limited availability.</p><p>This puts independent creators in a conundrum — shell out for expensive GPU cloud rendering services or set up their own GPU server infrastructure, which incurs a heavy cost as well. Enter Render Network!</p><p><a href=""/deals/trading/bitget-crypto-exchange/""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg"" alt=""Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>This Render Network review will give you the lowdown on everything you need to know, exploring its features, benefits, use cases and potential risks.</p><p><strong>Render Network Review Summary</strong></p><p>The Render Network provides decentralized GPU computing power for tasks ranging from basic <a href=""https://processing.org/tutorials/rendering"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">rendering</a> to <a href=""https://mitsloan.mit.edu/ideas-made-to-matter/machine-learning-explained"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">machine learning</a> training to complex calculations and Artificial Intelligence, which are in a blockchain-based peer-to-peer network.</p><figure class=""table""><table><tbody><tr><td>Headquarters</td><td>California</td></tr><tr><td>Year Founded</td><td>2017</td></tr><tr><td>Founder</td><td>Jules Urbach</td></tr><tr><td>Native Token</td><td>RNDR</td></tr><tr><td>Total Funding</td><td><a href=""https://www.crunchbase.com/organization/rndr-token"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">$30 million</a></td></tr></tbody></table></figure><h2>What is Render Network?</h2><p><a href=""https://rendernetwork.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Render Network</a> lets people monetize their otherwise dormant GPU resources by performing renders in return for its native RNDR token. The platform allocates idle GPU power from across the globe for 3D rendering tasks, creating a scalable peer-to-peer GPU cloud computing network. Through this process, Render Network not only minimizes GPU wastage but also offers creators cost-effective, on-demand rendering abilities.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Render_Network_Review_767dc64c37.jpg"" alt=""Render Network Review.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Render_Network_Review_767dc64c37.jpg 204w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Render_Network_Review_767dc64c37.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Render_Network_Review_767dc64c37.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Render Network Provides Decentralized GPU Computing Power For a Variety of Tasks. Image via <a href=""https://rendernetwork.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Render Network</a></figcaption></figure><p>The underlying technology of Render Network is rooted in <a href=""/education/what-is-blockchain-technology/"">blockchain technology</a>. It not only stores, validates, and time-stamps intricate technical specifications, schedules, accounts, regulations, protocols, standards, and property rights, but also manages digital rights crucial for assets that are otherwise prone to routine copying.</p><p>The integration of the <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a> blockchain enables the seamless execution of more complex transactions using smart contracts, providing a robust framework for transactions backed by ORBX packages. ORBX is an open-source file format designed to encode all elements of 3D scenes and transfer them between platforms.</p><p>As node operators successfully complete scenes on the network, their reputation score increases. Render Network refers to this process as Proof-of-Render where trustworthiness is built on rendering 3D scenes rather than the proof-of-work mining used by other blockchain protocols such as <a href=""/education/what-is-bitcoin/"">Bitcoin</a>.</p><p>The company focuses on virtual reality, mixed reality and augmented reality experiences.</p><p>Recently, OTOY (the parent company of Render) was featured in an article by the <a href=""https://hbr.org/2023/09/web3-could-change-the-business-model-of-creative-work"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Harvard Business Review</a>, which explored how Web3 could change the business model of creative work.</p><p>Render Network has implemented a MATIC (<a href=""/education/polygon-2023-beginners-guide-to-matic/"">Polygon</a>) <a href=""/analysis/proof-of-work-vs-proof-of-stake/"">proof-of-stake</a> cross-chain bridge in order to alleviate the long transaction times and high gas prices. The <a href=""/education/cross-chain-bridges/"">cross-chain bridge</a> allows for easy asset movement between ETH and Matic, where an RNDR and escrow contract has been set up on the Layer 2 system.</p><h2>Who Founded Render Network?</h2><p>Jules Urbach is the founder of Render and OTOY. He sets the strategic vision for OTOY and is the chief architect of the company’s technology roadmap.</p><p>He made his first game at the age of 18 and went on to make the web's first 3D video game platform and licensed the software to a number of major companies including Disney, Warner Brothers, Nickelodeon and Microsoft.</p><p>In addition, Ari Emanuel, the CEO of sports and entertainment company Endeavor, and movie director JJ Abrams are advisers to the company.</p><h2>What's the Role of the Render Network Foundation?</h2><p>As the Render Network has evolved into one of the largest decentralized GPU computing and GPU cloud rendering networks in the world, it has introduced a decentralized governance framework, led by the <a href=""https://renderfoundation.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Render Network Foundation</a>.</p><p>The foundation considers it important that active and engaged network participants are rewarded with ownership of the network in order to ensure that the network continues to evolve in the direction that serves its users most effectively.</p><figure class=""image""><a href=""https://vimeo.com/231572056"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_fb33c3171b.png""></a><figcaption>Source: <a href=""https://rendernetwork.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Rendernetwork.com</a></figcaption></figure><p>Every member of the Render Network community is considered a part of the foundation, as long as they are active participants.</p><h2>How to Join Render Network?</h2><p>If you're looking to join Render Network, there are two ways you can go about it. You can either join as a node operator (lend GPU power) or as a creator. Let's explore the two!</p><h3>Node Operators</h3><p>Perhaps you bought the shiny new GPU to play games, but haven't been able to find any free time. If you have unused GPU power, you could rent it out via Render Network and earn some RNDR tokens for time spent rendering.</p><p>Once a creator confirms that the renders were successfully processed, you will receive your RNDR tokens. Payouts are made every 7 to 10 days in a consolidated transaction to save on transaction fees required to make payments on the Ethereum blockchain.</p><p>The network scores users based on their success rate and past performance. If node operators do not successfully process work, their reputation will take a hit. Node operators with higher reputation scores are assigned work faster than those with low scores, incentivizing them to maintain high success rates.</p><p>Render Network says you should only connect your node to the network when you are able to commit most of your GPU, RAM and CPU resources. If you have a lot of GPU-intensive background tasks running while processing renders on the Render Network, it may lead to job failures that will hurt your reputation score and may lead to a potential quarantining of your node.</p><h3>Creators</h3><p>If you're someone who makes digital visuals, you're a consumer or a ""creator"" in Render Network parlance.</p><p>Just like node operators, creators have to be cognizant of their reputation score as well. If creators reject work that is properly rendered, their reputation score is reduced. For creators, reputation scores are used to determine the amount of concurrent mining nodes a user can access at any given time. As a result, creators with higher reputation scores are able to process work faster.</p><p>If you have insufficient funds to process a job, you will have to add tokens to your account in order to submit the job. Also, if you run out of RNDR tokens in your account while your rendering is in progress, your job will be paused until more tokens are added to your account. There are two ways of adding funds:</p><ul><li><strong>RNDR Token:</strong> RNDR is Render Network's native token. These can be purchased and sold on exchanges.</li><li><strong>RNDR Credits:</strong> Unlike the token, RNDR credits can be purchased using PayPal and Stripe, directly through the Render Network portal on rndr.x.io. When a user purchases RNDR credits, they are backed by RNDR tokens that have been purchased off of an exchange by Render Network. This means that when a creator pays for a job using RNDR credits, node operators are paid out in RNDR tokens for their work.</li></ul><h2>How to Get Started as a Node Operator</h2><p>To become a node operator, there are certain hardware requirements you must meet:</p><ul><li>A CUDA-enabled NVIDIA GPU and a minimum of CUDA 10.1 drivers with support for compute capability 3.0 or higher (the minimum driver version is 419). Render recommends at least 6GB of VRAM, and over 8GB VRAM.</li><li>RAM helps your node process more complex scenes, which means the higher your RAM, the more computing power your node can take on. Render recommends more than 32GB RAM.</li><li>Strong network connectivity is required to download and upload assets.</li><li>100 GB of free disk space is recommended.</li></ul><h3>Connecting your Node to the Render Network</h3><p>To join the network as a node operator, you must first complete a form, and you will be added to the onboarding queue.</p><p>Once your node is ready to start mining, the Render Network team will detail everything in an email, but here's a top-level view:</p><ul><li>Download and install the application sent to you by the Render Network team. Information for setting up your node will be included in the email.</li><li>Once you're all set, open and run the Render Network client. At this point, you will have to add your Ethereum wallet. It's important that you link the same wallet you shared previously with the Render Network team. Once you copy your ETH Wallet ID, click ""Set wallet ID."" If you do not see this popup in your taskbar, check your security and firewall settings.</li></ul><h2>How to Get Started as a Creator</h2><p>To get started on the creator portal, you must have an active OctaneRender license or a subscription, which is currently €23.95 per month (billed annually) or €239.88 annually, which comes out to €19.99 per month. If you own a subscription or have a license, you can start rendering at rndr.x.io, where you log in with your OTOY account.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/OTOY_Login_704c1c4ded.jpg"" alt=""OTOY Login.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_OTOY_Login_704c1c4ded.jpg 160w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_OTOY_Login_704c1c4ded.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>OTOY is Render Network's Parent Company. Image via Render Network</figcaption></figure><p>This is what a creator's journey looks like on Render Network:</p><ul><li><strong>Checking Octane Version:</strong> The Render Network supports the most stable versions of OctaneRender.</li><li><strong>Exporting to ORBX file format:</strong> To upload a scene to the Render Network, the scene needs to be exported as an ORBX file, using OctaneRender Standalone or any of the supported OctaneRender plugin integrations. Checking a scene and optimizing it in Octane Standalone before it is uploaded to the Render Network is recommended to avoid errors, re-renders or unnecessary costs.</li><li><strong>Create Job Parameters for Rendering:</strong> When you have a scene to render, you can create a job. To begin this process click the “Create a Job” button on your scene. You will be redirected to the “Create a Job” page, where you will have several options.</li><li><strong>Estimate Job Costs:</strong> The final step before rendering is generating a cost estimate. This is to avoid the final job cost exceeding the number of tokens that were temporarily held for rendering. If the amount of work exceeds the number of tokens/credits in your account, the render will be paused and you will be prompted to add more tokens/credits to your account to resume the render.</li></ul><h2>How Much Does RNDR Cost?</h2><p>Render Network has a multi-tier pricing structure, based around speed, security and cost.</p><p>Both the RNDR token and credit are mapped to a unit of work called OctaneBench, a tool created by OTOY to define the computing power provided by any combination of graphics cards into a single score. When setting up a job, creators select a tier based on their preferences for speed, cost, security and node reputation.</p><p>Render Network currently has two pricing tiers:</p><ul><li><strong>Tier 1 (Priority):</strong> This provides rendering queue priority, more power and faster average speeds to handle larger and more complex scenes.</li><li><strong>Tier 2 (Economy):</strong> Provides the most economic rendering solution. Queue priority and requisite node power are not guaranteed. This tier is recommended for work that is not time-sensitive.</li></ul><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/RNDR_pricing_7def91950c.jpg"" alt=""RNDR pricing.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_RNDR_pricing_7def91950c.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_RNDR_pricing_7def91950c.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_RNDR_pricing_7def91950c.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Render Network Has a Multi-Tier Pricing Structure. Image via Render Network</figcaption></figure><p>The company is also currently working on another tier called ""Trusted."" Once that's rolled out, that'll become Tier 1.</p><p>Multi-tier pricing operates using a multiplier attached to the OctaneBench algorithm.</p><ul><li>Tier 1 (Trusted) work has an OctaneBench multiplier of 1x.</li><li>Tier 2 (Priority) has a multiplier that varies between 2x and 4x (thus, an artist will receive 2x to 4x more OB work at Tier 2 when compared to Tier 1).</li><li>Tier 3 (Economy) has a multiplier of 8x to 16x when compared to Tier 1.</li></ul><h2>RNDR Token</h2><p>RNDR is an ERC-20 utility token designed to power rendering work on the Render Network. RNDR tokens can be purchased and sold on exchanges and can be earned by node operators for work rendered on their nodes.</p><p>This is what the RNDR token allocation looks like:</p><ul><li>25% has been sold</li><li>10% is in the RNDR reserve</li><li>65% is in escrow for supply/demand flowback to the network</li></ul><p>As the network scales, Render says it will need to flow more tokens into the ecosystem. These tokens will either come through the reserve as user acquisitions, bonuses for node operators, airdrops, or other future token allocation methods. In the meantime, these tokens are sitting in a third-party custody and escrow account.</p><p>Render Network has undertaken two token sales:</p><ul><li>A public sale in October 2017 where 1 RNDR token was equivalent to $0.25.</li><li>A private sale from January to May 2018 where 1 RNDR token equalled $0.25.</li></ul><p>The token's price has come a long way since.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/RNDR_token_price_5eba34c716.jpg"" alt=""RNDR token price.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_RNDR_token_price_5eba34c716.jpg 197w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_RNDR_token_price_5eba34c716.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_RNDR_token_price_5eba34c716.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>RNDR is the 57th Largest Token by Market Capitalization. Image via <a href=""https://www.coingecko.com/en/coins/render"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">CoinGecko</a></figcaption></figure><p>Today, the token is the 57th largest by market capitalization, and its current price represents a decline of over 80% from its all-time high of $8.78 in November 2021. The RNDER Token has been one of the better performers in the 22/23 bear market and has even seen positive price action in recent months as excitement grows around the project.</p><h3>Where can you buy RNDR Tokens?</h3><p>If you're looking to purchase RNDR, you can check out crypto exchanges such as <a href=""/review/gate-io-exchange/"">Gate.io</a>, <a href=""/review/binance/"">Binance</a>, <a href=""/review/bitget-exchange-review/"">Bitget</a>, <a href=""/review/coinbase-pro/"">Coinbase</a> and <a href=""/review/kraken/"">Kraken</a>.</p><p>If you're in the market for a reliable exchange, head over to our article that examines the <a href=""/review/best-crypto-exchanges/"">best crypto exchanges</a>.</p><h2>What are the Benefits of Render Network?</h2><p>Render Network has a lot going for it:</p><ul><li><strong>Scalability:</strong> Embracing a decentralized global network for next-generation 3D rendering provides stability by efficiently managing computational scale, preventing overloads, enhancing resilience against failures, and offering seamless scalability.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Efficiency:</strong> Render Network's efficiency stems from its ability to transform idle GPUs into valuable assets, creating an ecosystem where supply meets demand in real-time. Through global coordination, decentralized scalability, transparent transactions, and cost-effectiveness, the network ensures that artists and developers can access the computational power they need efficiently and affordably.</li><li><strong>Digital Rights Management: </strong>Next-generation immersive media and artificial intelligence require new forms of authentication and provenance. The Render Network provides granular digital rights management through on-chain traceability of a node-based render graph.</li></ul><p>Render Network's approach paves the way for a more inclusive, diverse, and collaborative community of creators and innovators in several ways:</p><ul><li><strong>Accessibility and Affordability:</strong> Render Network reduces rendering costs and time up to 90% compared to traditional cloud services. This ensures that computational power is accessible to budget-savvy creators, unlocking the potential for the next generation of 3D content and Artificial Intelligence creation.</li><li><strong>Inclusivity through Global Coordination:</strong> Render Network's global coordination and decentralized scalability ensure that computational resources are distributed worldwide. This inclusivity breaks down geographical barriers, enabling creators from different countries and regions to collaborate seamlessly.</li><li><strong>Transparent and Fair Ecosystem:</strong> The transparent transactions facilitated by Render Network instil trust within the community. Creators can be assured of fair compensation for their work through the platform's on-chain traceability.</li><li><strong>Empowering Independent Creators:</strong> Render Network's cost-effectiveness and accessibility empower independent creators, enabling them to explore their creative potential without financial constraints.</li><li><strong>Supporting Collaboration and Innovation:</strong> Render Network's real-time supply and demand matching, along with seamless scalability, facilitates collaborative projects as creators and innovators can easily find the computational resources they need.</li><li><strong>Protection of Creative Assets:</strong> The granular digital rights management provided by Render Network ensures that creators maintain control over their intellectual property. This protection encourages creators to share their work without fear of plagiarism or unauthorized use.</li></ul><h2>Render Network Use Cases</h2><p>The Render Network is a versatile platform catering to an audience encompassing artists, engineers, designers and developers. It opens doors to an array of GPU workloads and applications.</p><h3>Visual Effects and Motion Graphics</h3><p>Independent artists and studios, leveraging the Render Network, can delve into the realm of large-scale 3D visual effects, a feat that would typically demand substantial upfront investments. The platform offers artists the flexibility of nearly limitless on-demand GPU resources, allowing them to render scenes at higher resolutions or multiple output formats.</p><h3>Virtual Assets and Non-Fungible Tokens (NFTs):</h3><p>The Render Network empowers 3D artists to craft <a href=""/education/non-fungible-tokens-nft/"">non-fungible tokens</a> and virtual assets, ensuring comprehensive provenance tracking. Moreover, artists can venture into the creation and tokenization of next-generation virtual assets, including interactive ORBX files. This functionality facilitates the monetization of portable 3D virtual assets, enhancing the creative and financial opportunities for artists in the digital space.</p><h3>Virtual Production</h3><p>For directors and cinematographers, the Render Network is a transformative tool. It enables the seamless integration of live action with vast, rendered 3D environments, revolutionizing the filmmaking process. This integration empowers creators to explore unlimited takes and push the boundaries of virtually crafted cinematic worlds.</p><p><a href=""https://hub.coinbureau.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg"" alt=""Join-The-CoinBureau-Club-Inline-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>What are the Challenges of Render Network?</h2><p>Render Network isn't all shiny and chrome. Just like every other business, it too faces its own set of unique challenges.</p><h3>Combining Blockchain and AI</h3><p>While the two technologies hold immense promise, they also present challenges:</p><ul><li><strong>Data Privacy:</strong> Blockchain networks are inherently transparent, which can conflict with the privacy requirements of certain AI applications. Ensuring that sensitive data used by AI algorithms remains private and secure while being processed within a transparent and immutable blockchain is a complex problem.</li><li><strong>Interoperability:</strong> Integrating diverse AI algorithms and blockchain platforms can be challenging due to the lack of standardized protocols. Ensuring seamless communication and data exchange between different AI models and various blockchain networks is a technical hurdle.</li><li><strong>Security Risks:</strong> Blockchain networks are touted for their security, but they are not immune to attacks. <a href=""/education/ethereum-smart-contracts/"">Smart contracts</a>, which are integral to Render Network, can contain vulnerabilities that AI-driven attacks might exploit. Ensuring the security of both the blockchain infrastructure and the AI algorithms is paramount.</li></ul><h3>Regulatory Risks</h3><p>Operating in a decentralized environment, especially within the world of emerging technologies like blockchain and cryptocurrencies, brings with it regulatory uncertainty and legal risks.</p><p>Many governments and regulatory bodies, especially the U.S., have yet to establish comprehensive guidelines and laws specific to decentralized platforms. This lack of clear regulations creates uncertainty, making it challenging for businesses and individuals to understand legal obligations and potential liabilities.</p><p>Render Network transcends traditional geographical boundaries. This makes determining which jurisdiction's laws apply in the case of disputes or legal matters becomes complex. Different countries have varying regulations regarding blockchain, cryptocurrencies, and decentralized applications, which may lead to conflicts in legal interpretation and enforcement.</p><p>AML and KYC regulations are stringent in the financial sector to prevent money laundering and illicit activities. Ensuring compliance with these regulations in decentralized environments, where transactions are pseudonymous, poses significant challenges.</p><h3>Competitors</h3><p><a href=""https://www.golem.network/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Golem Network</a> is another company that works more or less like Render Network.</p><p>Golem is a global, open-source, decentralized supercomputer that anyone can use. It is made up of the combined computing power of users' machines, from PCs to entire data centres. To facilitate that exchange, Golem implements a decentralized marketplace where IT resources are rented out. The participants in this decentralized network can assume one of the following two roles:</p><ul><li><strong>Requestor:</strong> This is someone with a need to use IT resources such as computation hardware.</li><li><strong>Provider:</strong> Someone who has free IT resources that can be shared with others in the network.</li></ul><p>The main difference between Golem and Render is that the former focuses on a wide range of use cases such as CGI rendering, scientific calculations, and machine learning, and while Render does all that too, its main focus is on AR, VR and MR.</p><h2>What is the Future of Render Network?</h2><p>Right now, bolstering the Render Network's capacity, finishing the Render Network SDK, providing Arnold support (via Hydra in the Render Network SDK), and validating some non-RNDR apps are the company's main priorities. Once these are done, the company has some interesting ideas:</p><ul><li><a href=""/review/siacoin-everything-need-know/""><strong>SiaCoin</strong></a><strong>:</strong> This is a project the Render Network team has kept on its radar for a number of years, and the possibility of integration has been discussed.</li><li><a href=""/review/basic-attention-token-bat/""><strong>Basic Attention Token</strong></a><strong>:</strong> BAT's technology for mapping ads and ad viewership has been discussed as a framework for potential Render Network development in ray-casting ad topology across virtual 3D spaces.</li><li><a href=""/review/decentraland-mana/""><strong>Decentraland</strong></a><strong>:</strong> The metaverse gaming app is on the company's radar as well.</li></ul><h2>Render Network: Closing Thoughts</h2><p>Render Network solves the challenges faced by creators in the virtual realm. By offering decentralized GPU computing power through blockchain technology, Render Network revolutionizes 3D rendering and computational tasks. The platform minimizes GPU wastage while providing on-demand rendering solutions in a cost-effective manner.</p><p>For Render Network, scalability, efficiency, and commitment to digital rights management is the name of the game. Its transparent, fair ecosystem empowers independent creators, fosters collaboration and innovation, and supports the protection of creative assets.</p><p>However, Render Network is not without its challenges. The integration of blockchain and AI presents complex issues related to data privacy, interoperability, and security. Moreover, operating in a decentralized environment brings regulatory risks and uncertainties, which can prove to be bumps in the road.</p><p>Render Network's journey signifies a significant step towards democratizing computational power, empowering creators, and shaping the future of immersive digital experiences.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Education/what-are-ethereum-testnets/,What are Testnets? Ethereum Testnets Explained!,Education,"<p>In the cryptocurrency space <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a> stands as a prominent and pioneering platform, facilitating the development of decentralized applications (DApps) and smart contracts. However, the path to innovation within the Ethereum ecosystem is not without its challenges. Before any ground-breaking innovation can go live on the Ethereum mainnet, it must undergo rigorous testing and development on test networks, known in short as ""<a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Testnet"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Testnets</a>.""</p><p>In the journey to create and deploy Ethereum blockchain improvements, developers face a daunting challenge - the need to ensure the reliability, security and functionality of their creations without risking real assets. This is where Ethereum Testnets step in as invaluable tools.</p><p>These Ethereum Testnets provide a vital intermediary step before core devs or individual dApp developers can launch their projects on the mainnet. Testnets allow developers and blockchain enthusiasts to use these specialized testing environments without any fear of damaging the live network and placing real crypto assets at risk.</p><p>The deployment of code and execution of transactions on the Ethereum mainnet require meticulous preparation and scrutiny, which requires the use of multiple different Testnets, which we will cover in this article.</p><p><a href=""/deals/trading/okx/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg"" alt=""OKX Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>Testnets provide a secure, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sandbox_(software_development)"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">sandboxed</a> space where code can be rigorously tested, thoroughly experimented with and diligently debugged. This critical phase in the development process is essential to avoid potentially catastrophic bugs, which could have devastating consequences.</p><p>The consequences of a catastrophic Layer 1 bug in mainnet Ethereum would be incredibly damaging to the cryptocurrency space as Ethereum's prominence within the blockchain world cannot be overstated.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/ETH_TVL_ab3ff523d8.png"" alt=""ETH TVL.png"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_ETH_TVL_ab3ff523d8.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_ETH_TVL_ab3ff523d8.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_ETH_TVL_ab3ff523d8.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_ETH_TVL_ab3ff523d8.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>ETH TVL, Image via <a href=""https://defillama.com/chain/Ethereum"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Defillama</a></figcaption></figure><p>Ethereum secures a staggering $20.96 billion in Total Value Locked (TVL) and supports a vast network of 31 different <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/layer-2/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Layer 2</a> solutions that all secure back to the Ethereum Layer 1. Consequently, if anything were to happen to Ethereum’s Layer 1, all of the Layer 2’s would also be compromised.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/l2beat_797c763038.jpg"" alt=""l2beat.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_l2beat_797c763038.jpg 185w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_l2beat_797c763038.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_l2beat_797c763038.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_l2beat_797c763038.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>A Look at Just a Few of the Protocols That Rely on Layer 2 Solutions. Image via <a href=""https://l2beat.com/scaling/summary"">L2Beat</a></figcaption></figure><p>In this article, we will delve into the world of Ethereum Testnets, shedding light on what they are, how they operate, their diverse applications, the inherent value they bring to the blockchain ecosystem and an exploration of the various Testnets available today.</p><p>This article will cover:</p><ul><li><strong>What Ethereum Testnets Are</strong>: We'll start by demystifying the concept of Testnets, explaining their role as separate blockchain networks designed for testing and experimentation.</li><li><strong>How They Work</strong>: Taking a look at the technical underpinnings of Ethereum Testnets, exploring the <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/evm/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum Virtual Machine</a> (EVM) and consensus mechanisms that power these networks.</li><li><strong>What They Are Used For</strong>: Discovering the wide array of use cases Ethereum Testnets serve, from smart contract development and quality assurance to educational purposes and protocol upgrades.</li><li><strong>Why They Are Useful:</strong> Delving into the intrinsic value of Testnets, including their role in risk mitigation, accelerated development and community collaboration.</li><li><strong>How Many Testnets There Are</strong>: Getting an overview of the main Ethereum Testnets, with each catering to different needs and use cases.</li><li><strong>What is the Future of Ethereum Testnets</strong>: How will new and existing Testnets be added and removed?</li></ul><p>Hopefully, by the end of this guide, you'll have a good understanding of Ethereum Testnets and their pivotal role in facilitating the development and growth of the Ethereum ecosystem. Whether you're a blockchain developer, enthusiast or simply curious about the inner workings of Ethereum, this guide will provide you with the knowledge needed to understand Testnets and what their purpose is.</p><h2>What are Ethereum Testnets?</h2><p>Ethereum Testnets are specialized blockchain networks designed to replicate the core functionality of the main Ethereum network, also known as the ""mainnet."" The primary difference lies in the currency used within these test networks.&nbsp;</p><p>Instead of real Ether (ETH), they use test Ether tokens, often referred to as ""Testnet Ether"" or ""test ETH."" These test Ether tokens are supposed to hold no actual monetary value as they can be obtained without any cost, allowing users to engage in various activities without the fear of losing real funds. Testnet ETH is also designed to be free or cheap to acquire as it allows developers to make lots of test transactions at virtually no cost.</p><p>Although Testnet ETH should be valueless as it can be created with relative ease, there are actually secondary markets that exist where Testnet ETH does have a surprisingly high market value as they have become scarce or hard to obtain.</p><p>An example of this would be <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/networks/#:~:text=Goerli%20is%20a%20testnet%20for,stakers%20can%20test%20network%20upgrades"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Goerli ETH</a> which is facing deprecation and at the time of writing is trading at $0.03312 with a 24-hour trading volume of $1668.</p><p>As stated by Coingecko:&nbsp;</p><blockquote><p>“Goerli Testnet is one of Ethereum Chain's many Testnets that serves as a test environment for Ethereum developers and is facing deprecation. It should also be noted that these Testnet tokens can be obtained for free as it is meant for testing of Ethereum smart contract in a sandbox environment.”</p></blockquote><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/goerli_eth_testnet_a6ec0f731a.jpg"" alt=""goerli eth testnet.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_goerli_eth_testnet_a6ec0f731a.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_goerli_eth_testnet_a6ec0f731a.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_goerli_eth_testnet_a6ec0f731a.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_goerli_eth_testnet_a6ec0f731a.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Image via <a href=""https://www.coingecko.com/en/coins/goerli-eth"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coingecko</a></figcaption></figure><p>Ethereum Testnets serve as invaluable tools for developers, businesses and anyone interested in Ethereum's capabilities. They enable experimentation, testing and exploration of smart contracts, <a href=""/analysis/best-ethereum-dapps/"">decentralized applications</a> (DApps) and other blockchain features without the financial risks associated with the mainnet.</p><h2>How do Testnets Work?</h2><p>Testnets come in a variety of flavours, with the most common being <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/networks/#:~:text=Goerli%20is%20a%20testnet%20for,stakers%20can%20test%20network%20upgrades"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Rinkeby</a>, <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/networks/#:~:text=Goerli%20is%20a%20testnet%20for,stakers%20can%20test%20network%20upgrades"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Goerli</a>, <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/networks/#:~:text=Goerli%20is%20a%20testnet%20for,stakers%20can%20test%20network%20upgrades"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Sepolia</a> and more recently, <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/networks/#:~:text=Goerli%20is%20a%20testnet%20for,stakers%20can%20test%20network%20upgrades"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Holesky</a>. Each Testnet offers a slightly different environment to cater to specific testing needs. For instance, Ropsten (now deprecated) used a <a href=""/analysis/proof-of-work-vs-proof-of-stake/"">proof-of-work</a> (PoW) consensus mechanism similar to the old mainnet, while Rinkeby employs a proof-of-authority (PoA) consensus mechanism and Goerli combines aspects of both. Developers can choose the Testnet that best suits their project's requirements.</p><p>Accessing a Testnet typically involves using specialized wallets or development tools. Once connected, users can create and deploy smart contracts, interact with DApps, simulate transactions, and test various blockchain-related functionalities. The open nature of Testnets fosters collaboration, community feedback and iterative development, ultimately contributing to the stability and security of applications before they are deployed on the main Ethereum network.&nbsp;</p><p>Ethereum Testnets are essential components of the Ethereum ecosystem that allow developers to test and deploy smart contracts and decentralized applications (DApps) without using real Ether (ETH) on the main Ethereum network and serve as a safe environment for experimentation. Here's how Ethereum Testnets work:</p><ul><li><strong>Testnet Networks</strong>: Ethereum has multiple Testnet networks, each serving a different purpose. The most commonly used Testnets include Holesky, Goerli and Sepolia. Each of these networks mimics the Ethereum mainnet to varying degrees but uses Testnet Ether, which has no real-world value.</li><li><strong>Testnet Ether (tETH)</strong>: Testnets have their own native cryptocurrency called ""Testnet Ether"" (tETH) or other Testnet-specific tokens. These tokens are freely available and can be obtained from faucets or other Testnet resources. Unlike real Ether, tETH is usually distributed for free and has no monetary value.</li><li><strong>Similar Blockchain Structure</strong>: Testnets replicate the structure of the Ethereum mainnet, including block generation, transaction processing and smart contract execution. They use the same underlying technology, such as the Ethereum Virtual Machine (EVM) and the same consensus algorithms (proof-of-work or proof-of-stake, depending on the Testnet).</li><li><a href=""https://goethereumbook.org/en/faucets/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Faucets</strong></a><strong>:</strong> Testnet Ether can be obtained from faucets, which are online tools that distribute tETH for free. Users often need to provide a Testnet address to receive the tokens. Faucets are available for each Testnet and developers can use them to acquire tETH for testing.</li><li><a href=""https://etherscan.io/gastracker"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Gas Fees</strong></a>: Just like the mainnet, Testnets require gas fees to process transactions and execute smart contracts. However, since tETH has no real-world value, the gas fees are minuscule and affordable. Developers need tETH to pay for gas when testing their applications.</li></ul><figure class=""image image_resized"" style=""width:50%;""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Rinkeby_e637276b63.jpg"" alt=""Rinkeby testnet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Rinkeby_e637276b63.jpg 88w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Rinkeby_e637276b63.jpg 281w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Rinkeby Testnet Transaction, Image via <a href=""https://ethereum.stackexchange.com/questions/117950/why-is-gas-fee-of-mainnet-higher-than-testnet"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">StackExchange</a></figcaption></figure><ul><li><strong>Development and Testing</strong>: Developers can deploy smart contracts and DApps on Testnets using the same tools and methodologies they would use on the mainnet. They can test their code, simulate interactions, and ensure that everything works as expected without risking real Ether.</li><li><strong>Community Support</strong>: Testnets have active developer communities that provide support, information, and resources to help developers navigate the testing environment. You can find <a href=""https://sepolia.etherscan.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Testnet block explorers</a>, forums, and other tools to monitor and interact with the Testnet.</li><li><strong>Network Upgrades</strong>: Testnets are periodically upgraded to test new Ethereum protocol upgrades and changes before they are implemented on the mainnet. Developers and network validators participate in these upgrades to ensure they are safe and effective. Examples include the already implemented <a href=""https://eips.ethereum.org/EIPS/eip-1559"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum Improvement Proposal 1559</a> so called EIP1559 which introduced a fee burning mechanism.</li><li><strong>Resetting and Pruning</strong>: Testnets may be reset or pruned periodically to maintain their performance and cleanliness. This means that Testnet data can be erased, and tETH balances can be reset to prevent accumulation and misuse.</li></ul><p>Ethereum Testnets provide a controlled and risk-free environment for developers to experiment with Ethereum smart contracts and DApps. They mimic the mainnet's functionality while using Testnet-specific tokens that have no real value, making it a safe space for development and testing.</p><h2>What Are Different Testnets Used For?</h2><p>Each Testnet will be designed for specific use cases or developer needs, as such, different Testnets will be used by different people for different tasks. Let’s break them down and take a look:</p><h3>Sepolia Testnet</h3><p>Sepolia is a Testnet primarily designed for developers and testers who want to interact with the Ethereum network without the constraints and complexities of the mainnet. &nbsp;Sepolia is the recommended default Testnet for application development and was designed to simulate harsh network conditions. Sepolia offers the following benefits and features:</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li><strong>Sepolia is suggested as the default Testnet:</strong> Developers who are building applications on a specific blockchain platform are recommended to use Sepolia. It’s designed for testing decentralized applications, smart contracts and other EVM functionality.</li><li><strong>Permissioned Validator Set</strong>: The Sepolia network employs a permissioned validator set. In a permissioned network, validators are chosen and controlled by specific entities, often client teams and testing teams. These validators are responsible for confirming and adding new transactions to the blockchain. Having a permissioned validator set provides more control and security, making it suitable for testing and development purposes.</li><li><strong>New Testnet with Small State and History</strong>: Sepolia is described as a relatively new Testnet. This means that it hasn't been in existence for very long, and as a result, the blockchain's state (current data and account balances) and history (past transactions and events) are quite small. This is in contrast to older Testnets or the mainnet, which may have accumulated a large amount of data over time.</li><li><strong>Quick to Sync</strong>: Because Sepolia's state and history are small, it's much quicker to synchronize (sync) with the network. Syncing refers to the process of downloading and updating a node's copy of the blockchain to match the current state of the network. In Sepolia's case, this process is fast and efficient.</li><li><strong>Minimal Disk Space Requirement</strong>: Running a node on the Sepolia Testnet doesn't require a lot of storage space. This is advantageous for developers who want to set up a node quickly and interact with the network directly without having to allocate a significant amount of disk space for storage.</li></ul><h3>Holesky Testnet (Replacing Goerli in 2023):</h3><p>Holesky is replacing Goerli as a Testnet for staking, infrastructure and protocol development and went live on 28 September 2023. Holesky is an impressive new Testnet and is the first long-standing, merged-from-genesis, public Ethereum Testnet whose main function is to replace Goerli as a staking, infrastructure and protocol-developer Testnet in 2023.&nbsp;</p><p>Holesky is specifically designed for thorough staking trials, infrastructure assessments and direct protocol developer testing, mirroring mainnet functionalities for precise evaluations.</p><p>Holesky aims to increase the number of validators on the Ethereum mainnet and test how changes affect its stability. The Ethereum Foundation’s DevOps team has several plans for Holesky.&nbsp;</p><ol><li>Test the network more thoroughly by having twice as many active validators as the main Ethereum network.</li><li>Improve the way inflation works using methods from the Sepolia testnet.</li><li>Start with a strong base of 1 million validators for better testing.</li><li>Encourage teams to run many of these validators, aiming for each team to handle around 100,000, ensuring the testnet works as intended.</li></ol><h3>Goerli Testnet</h3><p>Goerli is a widely used Ethereum Testnet with the following key purposes:</p><ul><li><strong>Open Validator Set</strong>: Goerli features an open validator set, allowing <a href=""/education/guide-to-staking-crypto/"">stakers</a> to participate and test network upgrades. This openness makes it suitable for developers and projects interested in testing their staking setups.</li><li><strong>Large State</strong>: Goerli has a larger state compared to some other Testnets, which is useful for testing complex smart contract interactions and scenarios that require a substantial amount of data.</li><li><strong>Longer Sync and Storage Requirements</strong>: Because of its larger state, Goerli may take longer to sync and requires more storage space to run a node. This means it's better suited for users who require a more comprehensive testing environment and are willing to invest in the necessary resources.</li></ul><p>In summary, Ethereum Testnets are specialized networks designed for specific use cases and developer needs. They cater to different tasks and audiences.&nbsp;</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li>The Sepolia Testnet, recommended for application development, offers benefits like a permissioned validator set, a small state and history, quick synchronization and minimal disk space requirements.&nbsp;</li><li>Holešky Testnet, replacing Goerli in 2023, focuses on staking, infrastructure, and protocol development, aiming to be the first long-standing public Ethereum Testnet.</li><li>Goerli Testnet is widely used and features an open validator set and a large state but requires longer sync times and more storage space.&nbsp;</li></ul><p>These Testnets serve distinct purposes, allowing developers and users to test various Ethereum network aspects based on their specific needs and resource availability. The choice of Testnet depends on your testing requirements and resource constraints.</p><h2>Why Are Testnets Useful?</h2><p>Ethereum Testnets are often overshadowed by the mainnet's spotlight but they play a pivotal role in the world of blockchain and Ethereum ecosystem development. They serve as invaluable sandboxes for developers and stakeholders alike, offering a controlled environment to experiment, test, and refine <a href=""https://defillama.com/chain/Ethereum"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum-based applications</a>.&nbsp;</p><p>First and foremost, Testnets are instrumental in mitigating risks associated with deploying <a href=""/education/ethereum-smart-contracts/"">smart contracts</a> and decentralized applications (DApps) on the Ethereum mainnet. The blockchain ecosystem is a high-stakes arena, with real-world assets and substantial economic value at risk. By allowing developers to deploy and assess their creations on Testnets, the Ethereum community can identify vulnerabilities, bugs and security loopholes before they potentially wreak havoc on the mainnet. This risk mitigation aspect is pivotal in preserving the integrity and trustworthiness of the Ethereum network.</p><p>In the fast-paced world of blockchain, developers are constantly innovating and iterating their projects. Testnets provide a rapid and cost-effective means to validate ideas and deploy prototypes. Without the burden of real-value transactions, developers can experiment freely, implement upgrades, and fine-tune their codebase with agility. This accelerated development cycle on Testnets not only reduces time-to-market but also fosters a culture of innovation, ensuring that Ethereum remains at the forefront of blockchain technology.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/testnet_ETH_pic_26dbc45695.jpg"" alt=""testnet ETH "" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_testnet_ETH_pic_26dbc45695.jpg 165w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_testnet_ETH_pic_26dbc45695.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Image via <a href=""https://www.argent.xyz/learn/how-to-get-testnet-eth-for-starknet/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Argent</a></figcaption></figure><p>Furthermore, Testnets are powerful tools for community collaboration. Ethereum is built on the principle of decentralization and a vibrant ecosystem of developers, enthusiasts and stakeholders. Testnets create a common ground where this diverse community can collaborate, test new features, and provide feedback. Developers can engage with the broader Ethereum community, seeking input and insights that can enhance their projects. This open and collaborative approach ensures that Ethereum evolves in a direction that benefits its users and maintains community-driven governance.</p><p>Ethereum Testnets are far more than just staging grounds for developers; they are indispensable pillars of the Ethereum ecosystem. They play a pivotal role in risk mitigation by identifying vulnerabilities early, facilitating accelerated development by providing a safe playground for innovation and fostering community collaboration by encouraging open dialogue and feedback. As <a href=""/analysis/decoding-ethereum/"">Ethereum continues to evolve</a>, Testnets will remain a cornerstone of its success, ensuring that it remains a secure, innovative and community-driven blockchain platform.</p><h2>What is the Future of Ethereum Testnets?</h2><p>The Ethereum community is facing a challenge with the rapid deprecation of Testnets, causing frustration among application developers and infrastructure providers. To address this issue, <a href=""https://ethereum-magicians.org/t/proposal-predictable-ethereum-testnet-lifecycle/11575"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">a proposal</a> has emerged from discussions within the Testnet workgroup. The proposal aims to create a more predictable Ethereum Testnet Lifecycle, providing stability and clarity for all stakeholders in the ecosystem.</p><p>The central idea of the proposal is to establish a predictable schedule for launching and maintaining Ethereum Testnets. Here are the key points:</p><ol><li><strong>New Testnets Every Two Years</strong>: Ethereum would launch a new Testnet every two years on a predefined date, such as October 1st, 2023, 2025, 2027, and so on.</li><li><strong>Testnet Lifetime Limit</strong>: Testnets will have a maximum lifetime of five years, comprising four years of active testing and one additional year of long-term support if necessary.</li><li><strong>Goerli Support Extension</strong>: Depending on the outcome of discussions regarding supply issues, Goerli's long-term support may be extended for another two years until 2024.</li></ol><p>The current approach of abruptly deprecating multiple Testnets with little notice ahead of the merge has caused frustration.
