Currently, only two major Testnets are available: Goerli (permissionless) and Sepolia (permissioned). Goerli has attracted more users due to its better infrastructure, creating a network effect.</p><p>The proposal suggests limiting the lifetime of public Ethereum Testnets to four years after genesis, with the possibility of extending it by one year for heavily used networks, reaching a maximum of five years.&nbsp;</p><p>Additionally, a new Testnet will be launched every two years. This ensures that at least two public Testnets will always be available to all stakeholders, reducing the frequency of application migrations to every four years.</p><p>The Predictable Ethereum Testnet Lifecycle proposal aims to bring stability and predictability to the Ethereum Testnet ecosystem. By establishing a clear schedule for launching and maintaining Testnets, it seeks to reduce frustration among application developers and infrastructure providers, ensuring a smoother transition for the Ethereum community during network upgrades and changes.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/timeline_5d7dc72faa.jpg"" alt=""timeline.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_timeline_5d7dc72faa.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_timeline_5d7dc72faa.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_timeline_5d7dc72faa.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_timeline_5d7dc72faa.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Timeline of Ethereum Testnet Lifecycles, Image via <a href=""https://github.com/eth-clients/holesky"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">GitHub</a></figcaption></figure><h2>Summary</h2><p>Ethereum Testnets serve as crucial elements in the world of blockchain development, providing a secure and controlled environment that benefits both developers and users. This article sheds light on their importance, encompassing their role as distinct blockchain networks designed for experimentation and highlights their technical intricacies, their wide-ranging applications in smart contract development and quality assurance and their undeniable value in risk mitigation and community collaboration.</p><p><a href=""https://t.me/cbinsider"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg"" alt=""Telegram Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>After gaining insight into the various Ethereum Testnets currently in existence, you should be better prepared to harness the full potential of these testing platforms and actively contribute to the Ethereum ecosystem. Testnets play a pivotal role in ensuring the ongoing growth and innovation within Ethereum, which in turn fuels progress in the broader cryptocurrency space.</p><p>The future of Ethereum Testnets looks promising, with a proposed Ethereum Testnet Lifecycle that promises predictability. Under this proposal, new Testnets will be launched every two years, each with a maximum lifespan of five years. The commitment also involves maintaining at least two public Testnets, reducing the need for frequent application migrations. All in all, these collective efforts aim to create a smoother and more predictable experience for the Ethereum developer community during Testnet network upgrades.</p><p>Hopefully this article will have provided some basic understanding of what Ethereum Testnets are and how they work. It is one of the fastest <a href=""/education/layer-1-blockchain-protocol/"">Layer 1</a> networks with TPS of up to 2,000. Like the majority of the other <a href=""/analysis/ethereum-dominance/#rival-blockchains-on-the-horizon"">Ethereum competitors</a> it is grouped with, Tron uses an account-based mechanism and has low transaction costs.&nbsp;</p><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">Its <a href=""/education/delegated-proof-stake-dpos/"">Delegated Proof of Stake</a> (DPos) consensus technique differs slightly from that of the other Layer-1 platforms that use Proof-of-Stake (PoS). &nbsp;It is also one of the most popular blockchains for trading USDT.&nbsp;</p><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">Tron's goal is to become the decentralized platform of choice for all entertainment-related services. The platform encourages direct communication between content producers and users without worrying about censorship issues.</p><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">Tron's total value locked stands at $6.79 billion, second only to Ethereum.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Tron_vs_ETH_TVL_d2b90063d6.jpg"" alt=""Tron vs ETH TVL.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Tron_vs_ETH_TVL_d2b90063d6.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Tron_vs_ETH_TVL_d2b90063d6.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Tron_vs_ETH_TVL_d2b90063d6.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Tron_vs_ETH_TVL_d2b90063d6.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Tron's TVL is Second Only to Ethereum. Image via <a href=""https://defillama.com/compare?chains=Ethereum&amp;chains=Tron"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">DefiLlama</a></figcaption></figure><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">Interested to know more? Our full review of the <a href=""/review/tron-trx-review/"">Tron network</a> covers everything you need to know.</p><h2>What is the Tron (TRX) Coin?</h2><p>TRX is Tron's native cryptocurrency, used for the payment of transaction fees and also as a governance token.</p><p>Unlike other <a href=""/analysis/proof-of-work-vs-proof-of-stake/"">Proof-of-Stake</a> blockchain projects where the validators are the ones to validate transactions and earn rewards, Tron has Super Representatives, selected by other TRX holders to approve transactions and maintain the network. TRX holders stake their tokens in order to be eligible to vote for Super Representatives.&nbsp;</p><p>The staked tokens generate three things for holders: energy, bandwidth and yield. The first two are concepts within the Tron network that are used to operate the blockchain and keep things fast and cheap. <strong>Bandwidth</strong> is used to offset the transaction fees on Tron and <strong>Energy</strong> is needed to interact with the smart contracts on the Tron network.</p><p>According to <a href=""https://www.stakingrewards.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Stakingrewards.com</a>, the current yield for staked TRX is 3.45%. That's not too bad considering that ETH gives you 3.76% these days.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/ETH_TRX_Staking_Yield_3561b220f9.png"" alt=""Where to buy Tron"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_ETH_TRX_Staking_Yield_3561b220f9.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_ETH_TRX_Staking_Yield_3561b220f9.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_ETH_TRX_Staking_Yield_3561b220f9.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_ETH_TRX_Staking_Yield_3561b220f9.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>ETH's Yield Edges Out the Yield for Staked TRX. Image via Staking Rewards</figcaption></figure><h2>What are the Best Exchanges to Buy Tron?</h2><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">TRX coins can easily be obtained through most cryptocurrency exchanges such as <a href=""/review/coinbase-pro/"">Coinbase</a>, <a href=""/review/kraken/"">Kraken</a>, <a href=""/review/okx/"">OKX</a>, and <a href=""/review/bitget-exchange-review/"">Bitget</a> to name a few. Some of them allow for purchases of TRX using fiat currency which needs to be deposited on the exchange first. Decentralised exchanges like <a href=""/review/uniswap-uni/"">Uniswap</a> let you swap <a href=""/guides/guide-to-stablecoins/"">stablecoins</a> (<a href=""/education/what-is-tether-usdt/"">USDT</a>, <a href=""/education/what-is-the-usdc-stablecoin/"">USDC</a> etc.) for TRX on their platform.&nbsp;</p><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">A quick note here: Decentralized exchanges require no KYC but you will need to have some level of understanding about crypto to interact with them. If you are completely new to the crypto scene, a centralized exchange could be a good choice but you will need to give up just a bit of your privacy in order to use them.&nbsp;</p><p style=""margin-left:!important;"">Also for newbies, we have a <a href=""/education/cryptocurrency-beginners-guide/"">cryptocurrency beginner's guide</a> that explains the digital asset class in plain English.</p><h2>How to buy TRX in 5 Steps</h2><p>Getting your cash converted into crypto is not as hard as you may think. Nowadays, there are quite a few ways to do this safely and relatively easily.</p><p>Centralized exchanges are one of the most popular places to buy crypto, including TRX. Note that these exchanges usually require their customers to undergo a KYC process. For those who are more privacy-minded, you might want to skip this section and move on to the next one.&nbsp;</p><h3>Step 1: Choosing a platform</h3><p>We've given you some ideas on the best exchanges to buy TRX. As long as it is an exchange that's been around for at least five years, has proof of reserves, has gone through audit checks, and may even be regulated in certain jurisdictions, these are usually the more reputable exchanges you can consider. Some of them may not operate in the region you are in, so please check this carefully before signing up for an account with them.&nbsp;</p><h3>Step 2: Do KYC</h3><p>The next step is usually to undergo the KYC process, often required by regulators. They'll likely ask for some form of ID and proof of address as a basic requirement. This step can take a few minutes or several days, depending on the exchange.&nbsp;</p><h3>Step 3: Deposit Funds</h3><p>After having successfully opened an account, it's time to move some money into it. Be sure to follow the instructions carefully when filling out the bank details for making a deposit. Check that all the required fields are entered correctly, including any reference numbers needed to accompany the bank transfer. Incorrect details may lead to delays in crediting the funds to your account, or worse still, having the funds returned to your bank. Some exchanges might also have deposit minimums, so check before making the transfer.</p><h3>Step 4: Place an Order&nbsp;</h3><p>Hooray, your funds are credited and you're ready to convert your cash into TRX. Exchanges consider this a “trade” since you are trading cash for crypto. There are two common ways to place an order:</p><ul><li><strong>Market orders:</strong> A market order means you are ready to trade at whatever price the crypto happens to be at the time. These orders are usually processed instantly.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Limit orders:</strong> These let you set the price you want to buy TRX at. For example, the current price of TRX is around $0.088. If you think this price is too high and are more comfortable buying it at $0.06, that's the price you enter in the order. Anytime the market price matches the price you want, that's when the order is fulfilled.&nbsp;</li></ul><h3>Step 5: You have TRX!&nbsp;</h3><p>Once the TRX is credited to your account, the next thing to consider is where to store it. Exchanges allow you to store your balance because it's easy for you to make trades. However, these funds are in the custody of the exchange, which means if it goes bust a la FTX or if there's a major hack, you may end up losing your money. For more on protecting your digital tokens, check out our <a href=""/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/"">crypto safety guide</a>.</p><p>If you don't intend to trade TRX, it's much better to store it in a non-custodial wallet. More on this later in the article.</p><h2>How to Buy TRX with a Debit or Credit Card</h2><p>Aside from exchanges, you can also buy TRX with plastic. The platform is connected with the local payment provider Windcave, which gives you access to either pay by bank transfer or via credit card. You do need to set up an account with them to get started. The business models for these companies are fee-based, hence you might be paying an arm and a leg to use them. The other thing is that you can't pick and choose the price you want to buy unless you wait for the market rate to be aligned with your price of choice.</p><p>On the other hand, while trading cash for crypto on an exchange is a lot cheaper fee-wise, a certain amount of patience is required as you wait for the funds to be transferred from your bank account to theirs. If all goes well, this is a fairly quick transfer that requires less than a day. In some instances, however, it could take up to a week or more, something I know far too well from personal experience. With limit orders, you have the option of buying at a price that you find favourable, especially if you're in no hurry to obtain it, or the price you want is not too far from the current market rate.</p><p>However you choose to make your purchase, we hope that this article gives you an idea of where to buy TRX in a manner that best suits your preferences.&nbsp;</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Analysis/ellipal-vs-ngrave-review/,ELLIPAL Titan vs. NGRAVE ZERO: Hardware Wallets Compared!,Analysis,https://www.coinbureau.com/Review/alethea-ai-review/,Alethea Review 2023: A Deep Dive into Artificial Liquid Intelligence (ALI),Review,"<p>Just as the internet revolutionized content distribution, AI is bringing a new era in content creation to the fore.&nbsp;</p><p>The emergence of powerful large language models like ChatGPT, Google's Bard, and Microsoft's Bing, among others, points to a massive shift in creative possibilities. Protocol</li><li>DApps</li></ul><h2>What Is Alethea AI?</h2><p>Alethea AI is building a progressively decentralized and permissionless protocol that enables the creation of AI assets, characters, and DApps, governed by its community.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Alethea_AI_review_2d8b97349a.jpg"" alt=""Alethea AI review"" Image via <a href=""https://alethea.ai/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Alethea AI</a></figcaption></figure><p>A significant challenge arises in integrating AI models within the current decentralized infrastructure due to hardware limitations. This hurdle often results in AI-crypto projects having centralized elements.</p><p>Alethea AI bridges this gap. Instead of burdening decentralized networks with AI computations, the company takes a unique approach. It keeps AI processing off-chain while harnessing the power of <a href=""/education/ethereum-smart-contracts/"">smart contracts</a> on the <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum blockchain</a> to support its protocol layer, a foundation crucial for the creation of iNFTs (more on that later. A LOT more).</p><p>Alethea AI's vision is to preserve and evolve human culture, stories, and collective intelligence. How does it plan to go about it? By combining AI-generated personalities with NFTs to craft intelligent NFT avatars. These entities serve a dual purpose: they not only act as guardians of the cultures that inspired their creation but also offer people an opportunity to delve deep into collective intelligence as they interact with these imaginative and self-sufficient iNFTs.</p><p>The company is backed by some big names in the crypto industry, including <a href=""/review/binance/"">Binance</a>, <a href=""/education/polygon-2023-beginners-guide-to-matic/"">Polygon</a> and <a href=""/review/crypto-com-exchange/"">Crypto.com</a>. In January 2023, Alethea <a href=""https://medium.com/@arikhan/generative-ai-launches-on-polygon-b73a8d387f0d"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">debuted</a> its generative AI prowess on the Polygon blockchain.</p><p>Two other examples of AI-blockchain projects include <a href=""/review/singularitynet-agix/"">SingularityNET</a> and <a href=""/review/fetch-fet/"">Fetch.AI</a>.</p><h3>Who founded Alethea AI?</h3><p>Arif Khan is the founder of Alethea AI and currently serves as its CEO.</p><p>His resume includes working as chief marketing officer at SingularityNET, a decentralized marketplace for artificial intelligence. Khan has also worked as an account director of emerging markets at LinkedIn, where he led cross-functional projects in enterprise sales and product marketing.&nbsp;</p><h2>Alethea AI Review: Top Features</h2><p>AI is Alethea's bread and butter. Let's explore how the company has applied AI to its ecosystem.</p><h3>Intelligent NFTs</h3><p>What do you get when you combine non-fungible tokens with the power of artificial intelligence? iNFTs.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/What_are_i_NF_Ts_402b33b87f.jpg"" alt=""What are iNFTs.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_What_are_i_NF_Ts_402b33b87f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_What_are_i_NF_Ts_402b33b87f.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Intelligent NFTs Mark an Evolution of Otherwise Mundane NFTs. Image via Alethea AI</figcaption></figure><p>Alethea AI is the pioneer of intelligent non-fungible tokens, or iNFTs. For the uninitiated, <a href=""/education/non-fungible-tokens-nft/"">NFTs</a> are unique digital assets that are verified using blockchain technology. They are often used to represent digital art and collectables. Wouldn't it be cool if NFTs were not merely static assets but intelligent entities capable of learning, evolving, and interacting with their environment?</p><p>Introduce the brilliance of AI with its ability to analyze vast datasets, simulate human cognition, and generate innovative content, and you get iNFTs. Intelligent NFTs, which mark an evolution of NFTs, possess the ability to adapt, respond, and even create new content based on user interactions, preferences and contextual data.</p><p>The fusion of NFTs with AI allows creators to craft dynamic, ever-evolving digital assets. For collectors of these digital assets, they can now possess not just boring, run-of-the-mill NFTs, but living entities they can engage with.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Alethea_Alice_086c0cd2c2.jpg"" alt=""Alethea Alice.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Alethea_Alice_086c0cd2c2.jpg 169w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Alice, The World's First Intelligent NFT. Image via Alethea</figcaption></figure><p>In June 2021, Alethea AI <a href=""https://www.sothebys.com/en/buy/auction/2021/natively-digital-a-curated-nft-sale-2/to-the-young-artists-of-cyberspace"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">auctioned</a> Alice, the world's first iNFT, at Sothbey's for $478,800.</p><h3>iNFT Protocol</h3><p>All that NFT magic happens here.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/How_to_create_i_NFT_74e5b39344.jpg"" alt=""How to create iNFT.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_How_to_create_i_NFT_74e5b39344.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_How_to_create_i_NFT_74e5b39344.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Unlike Traditional NFTs, Which Are Static, iNFTs Can Learn, Respond, or Generate New Content. Image via Alethea AI</figcaption></figure><p>The iNFT Protocol refers to a set of smart contracts based on the Ethereum blockchain that allows anyone to create iNFTs in a permissionless manner. Any NFT can be turned into an iNFT via the iNFT Protocol. This is achieved by fusing the NFT with another ERC-721 asset called the Personality Pod. Once the NFT is fused with a Personality Pod, it acquires its own unique intelligence and personality. This is because the Personality Pod comprises various on-chain personality traits that shape the overall personality of the iNFT and in doing so, dictate the iNFT's intelligence.</p><p>The iNFT Protocol is designed with a non-custodial framework. Such an architecture enables users to turn their NFTs into iNFTs without the protocol requiring custody (locking, staking, wrapping, swapping) or applying other changes to the underlying NFT. As a result, users can utilize their NFTs outside the iNFT Protocol and reduce the risks of losing their valuable NFTs by an error, or an attack on the smart contracts of the iNFT Protocol.</p><h3>CharacterGPT</h3><p>Imagine talking to a computer and it creates characters that not only look real but also sound and act like real people or creatures. Alethea AI's CharacterGPT is all about bringing characters to life, just by using words. This technology has just received a significant upgrade.</p><p>With this new version, called CharacterGPT V2, you can create characters that are incredibly lifelike. They have detailed appearances, unique voices, and distinct personalities. But that's not all — CharacterGPT V2 is now smarter and understands what you want better than ever before.</p><p>CharacterGPT V2 can be accessed via a website called MyCharacter.ai, where you can create, customize, and bring to life a wide range of characters — all that's required is a simple text input.</p><p>CharacterGPT V2 and MyCharacter.ai offer an exciting playground to unleash your imagination, and I did exactly that albeit with mixed results.</p><p><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/My_Character_942270a7ed.jpg"" alt=""MyCharacter.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_My_Character_942270a7ed.jpg 208w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_My_Character_942270a7ed.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_My_Character_942270a7ed.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></p><p>I fashioned my character after John Wick, protagonist of the American media franchise <i>John Wick,</i> played by Keanu Reeves in the movies.</p><p>John Wick is a legendary globetrotting bad-guy-buster. When I asked him about where his next mission would lead to, he said his mission was to provide me with the “ultimate relaxation experience.” 🤷‍♂️""Let me work my magic on your muscles and melt away your stress.""</p><p>Not to give up so easily, I reframed my question: If you were John Wick, what would be your next mission? Here's the answer: If I were John Wick, my next mission would be to open my own wellness centre and bring the healing power of massage therapy to a larger community.</p><p>I couldn't help but chuckle at the absurdity of it all. The Tendermint consensus connects to the blockchain execution environment (where all the DApps live and the computation takes place) using the Application Blockchain Interface (ABCI). ABCI allows the execution environment to support multiple programming languages without compatibility issues with the underlying consensus engine.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Gas and fees</strong> - All transactions on OKBC will settle with the OKB token. Therefore, if OKBC successfully attracts developer attention and hosts a thriving DApp environment, the demand for OKB to pay transactions will increase significantly.</li></ul><p><a href=""https://hub.coinbureau.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg"" alt=""Join-The-CoinBureau-Club-Inline-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Conclusion</h2><p>In summary, OKB serves as a multi-faceted utility token within the OKC ecosystem, offering a range of benefits and use cases that extend from trading fee discounts to participation in token sales. Its tokenomics are designed to encourage long-term holding, and the introduction of the OKC Chain adds another layer of utility and potential for growth.&nbsp;</p><p>While the future of any cryptocurrency is inherently uncertain, OKB seems well-positioned for sustained relevance due to its integration with the OKX platform and its expanding utility. For those interested in buying, trading, or earning OKB, various avenues are available, making it accessible for both novice and experienced investors. As with any investment, conducting your own research and understanding the risks involved is crucial.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Review/coinbase-base-review/,Coinbase Base Review: What to Know About Base Layer 2,Review,"<p>Coinbase has emerged as a household name in the crypto sphere, akin to the likes of Amazon or Google in the tech realm. The US-based platform is not just a cryptocurrency exchange, it's a gateway to the entire crypto universe.</p><p>Imagine Coinbase as the front door to a digital financial wonderland where you can trade, invest and store your digital assets. Founded in 2012 by Brian Armstrong and Fred Ehrsam, Coinbase has quickly become one of the most user-friendly on-ramps for both newcomers and crypto degens.</p><p>At its core, Coinbase is a cryptocurrency exchange where you can buy, sell and trade various cryptocurrencies. It offers an easy-to-navigate interface that simplifies the process of buying cryptocurrencies.</p><p>Beyond its primary exchange, Coinbase has been instrumental in expanding the crypto ecosystem. In 2021, it made history by becoming the first major cryptocurrency exchange to go public on the Nasdaq stock exchange. This move brought further legitimacy and mainstream recognition to the world of cryptocurrencies.</p><p>In the fast-paced crypto market, Coinbase wields significant influence. While it has played a pivotal role in popularizing cryptocurrencies, it faces challenges like any other player in the industry, including regulatory scrutiny, technological advancements and competition from other exchanges.</p><p>In keeping with its dedication to the growth of the crypto ecosystem, Coinbase launched its own network on <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a> as a <a href=""https://help.coinbase.com/en/coinbase/getting-started/crypto-education/glossary/layer-2"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Layer 2</a> known as “BASE.”</p><p><a href=""/deals/wallet/unstoppable-domains/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Unstoppable_Domains_Inline_f1d93210d7.jpg"" alt=""Unstoppable Domains Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Unstoppable_Domains_Inline_f1d93210d7.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Unstoppable_Domains_Inline_f1d93210d7.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Unstoppable_Domains_Inline_f1d93210d7.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>In this Coinbase Base review, we'll touch base on (see what I did there?) everything you need to know about the network.</p><h2>What is Layer 2?</h2><p>Ethereum has long grappled with <a href=""/analysis/ethereum-dominance/#advantages-of-ethereum-over-other-blockchains"">scalability issues</a>, resulting in slow transaction processing times and exorbitant fees during peak usage. In response to this, various Layer 2 scaling solutions have emerged, offering a glimmer of hope for Ethereum's scalability woes.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Coinbase_Base_Review_fd1ab3e280.jpg"" alt=""Coinbase Base Review.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Coinbase_Base_Review_fd1ab3e280.jpg 229w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Coinbase_Base_Review_fd1ab3e280.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Coinbase_Base_Review_fd1ab3e280.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Base Aims to Bring the Next Billion Users Onchain. Image via <a href=""https://base.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Base</a></figcaption></figure><p>This is where BASE comes in. Coinbase, one of the most prominent cryptocurrency exchanges, has introduced BASE, a Layer 2 scaling solution that employs Optimism's <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/scaling/optimistic-rollups/#:~:text=An%20optimistic%20rollup%20is%20an,data%20to%20Mainnet%20as%20calldata%20."" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Optimistic Rollups</a> to address these challenges. BASE is a Layer 2 blockchain network built to help scale Ethereum using <a href=""https://stack.optimism.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">OP Stack</a> in collaboration with Optimism.</p><p>That sounds great, but what is Layer 2 (L2)?</p><p>Layer 2 solutions, in the context of Ethereum, are secondary blockchain networks or protocols built on top of the Ethereum mainnet (<a href=""/education/layer-1-blockchain-protocol/"">Layer 1</a>) with the primary purpose of improving its scalability, reducing transaction fees and increasing overall efficiency. They are designed to alleviate the limitations of the Ethereum network, which include slow transaction processing times and high gas fees. Layer 2 solutions achieve these goals by moving some of the computational and transaction load off the Ethereum mainnet, while still maintaining a connection to it for security and trust.</p><p>Layer 2 solutions offload a significant portion of transaction processing from the Ethereum mainnet. This reduces congestion on Layer 1 and allows for faster and cheaper transactions. They use various techniques to bundle multiple transactions together and submit them to the mainnet as a single transaction or checkpoint.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/optimistic_rollups_explanation_c9da9bba24.jpg"" alt=""optimistic rollups explanation.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_optimistic_rollups_explanation_c9da9bba24.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_optimistic_rollups_explanation_c9da9bba24.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_optimistic_rollups_explanation_c9da9bba24.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_optimistic_rollups_explanation_c9da9bba24.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Optimistic Rollup Which BASE Uses, Explained by Arbitrum. Image via </i><a href=""https://twitter.com/arbitrumcore/status/1605600913216913408/photo/1"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>X</i></a><i> (Formerly Twitter)</i></figcaption></figure><p>If you want a deeper look into the world of Ethereum Layer 2 scaling solutions, we have a great analytical piece that compares <a href=""/analysis/what-is-the-best-layer-2/"">Arbitrum vs. Optimism, ZkSync and Base</a> side by side.&nbsp;</p><h2>What is BASE by Coinbase?</h2><p>BASE is an open-source Ethereum L2 chain developed in collaboration with <a href=""/review/optimism-review/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Optimism</a> and incubated within Coinbase. It provides a secure, cost-effective and developer-friendly platform for building decentralized applications (DApps) which secure back to Ethereum's Layer 1 (L1) blockchain. BASE was built on the open-source <a href=""https://stack.optimism.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">OP Stack</a> with the following features:</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li><strong>Secured by Ethereum:</strong> BASE is built on the security and scalability of Ethereum, leveraging Coinbase's expertise to facilitate onboarding from Coinbase, Ethereum L1 (the mainnet), and other interoperable chains. It benefits from Ethereum's security while offering additional features.</li><li><strong>Empowered by Coinbase:</strong> BASE offers easy integration with Coinbase's products, access to its user base and various developer tools. This enables developers to tap into the 110 million verified users and $80 billion+ assets in the Coinbase ecosystem.</li><li><strong>Low Fee Transactions:</strong> BASE is designed to offer full <a href=""https://help.coinbase.com/en/coinbase/getting-started/crypto-education/glossary/ethereum-virtual-machine"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum Virtual Machine</a> (EVM) compatibility at a lower cost. BASE supports cheaper transactions for DApps and provides developer APIs for account abstraction.&nbsp;</li><li><strong>Open Source:</strong> BASE aims to be decentralized, permissionless and open to anyone interested in creating a standard, modular, rollup-agnostic <a href=""https://optimism.mirror.xyz/2jk3D1Y8-hid8YOCUUa6yXmsyzNCYYyFJP0Nhaey9x0"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Superchain</a> powered by Optimism. It joins Optimism as a Core Dev on the open-source OP Stack and seeks to foster a thriving developer community.</li></ul><h2>How Does Base Work?</h2><p>As BASE is built using OP stack, it inherits all the benefits and technology of Optimistic roll-ups. Roll-ups are at the heart of the Layer 2 movement happening on Ethereum which radically reduces gas fees and transaction costs.&nbsp;</p><p>BASE employs Layer 2 technology to optimize cost-efficiency while retaining the full functionality of Ethereum. It does this by running a parallel blockchain network that operates on top of the primary Ethereum chain — hence the term “layer.” This Layer 2 network handles transaction processing for all participants within the BASE network. Subsequently, once these transactions are validated, they are transmitted to Ethereum Layer 1. The primary Ethereum blockchain then incorporates this data into its ledger, adding it to the main chain.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/OP_L2_infographic_d1d6febe2a.png"" alt=""OP L2 infographic.png"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_OP_L2_infographic_d1d6febe2a.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_OP_L2_infographic_d1d6febe2a.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_OP_L2_infographic_d1d6febe2a.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>How an L2 Solution Works. Image via </i><a href=""https://www.coingecko.com/learn/what-is-optimism-op"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>CoinGecko</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>BASE uses that ""<a href=""https://academy.binance.com/en/articles/optimistic-vs-zero-knowledge-rollups-what-s-the-difference"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">rollup</a>"" mechanism, which essentially aggregates data from numerous distinct transactions into a single transaction bundle. By consolidating similar transactions, BASE further reduces the expenses associated with appending transactions to the Ethereum blockchain. In essence, BASE serves as a cost-efficient solution for Ethereum developers, where users and developers can make transactions much cheaper.</p><h2>Features of Coinbase BASE Protocol</h2><p>Coinbase BASE packs a punch. Let's explore!</p><h3>Security</h3><p>BASE inherits Ethereum's security by leveraging the power of Ethereum's Layer 1. When transactions are executed on BASE's Layer 2 scaling solution, they undergo a two-step process. First, they are swiftly processed off-chain, optimizing transaction speed and cost efficiency. However, the crucial security aspect comes into play during the second step when transaction data is periodically submitted to Ethereum's Layer 1 for verification.&nbsp;</p><p>This means that BASE relies on Ethereum's robust consensus mechanisms and battle-tested security protocols to ensure the integrity of transactions. Attempting to compromise or reverse a transaction on BASE would necessitate undermining the entire Ethereum network, an exceptionally challenging feat that effectively bolsters BASE's security and reinforces its trustworthiness for users and developers alike.</p><h3>Transaction Speeds and Capacities</h3><p>As BASE is built using OP stack, it inherits all the traits of Optimism’s optimistic rollups. In its current form, the max TPs achievable is 2,000 TPS according to <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/developers/docs/scaling/optimistic-rollups/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum.org</a>. However, the introduction of data sharding on Ethereum is expected to improve scalability in optimistic rollups. Because roll-up transactions must share blockspace with other non-rollup transactions, their processing capacity is limited by data throughput on the main Ethereum chain. <a href=""https://ethereum.org/en/roadmap/danksharding/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Danksharding</a> will increase the space available to L2 chains to publish data per block, using cheaper, impermanent ""blob"" storage instead of expensive, permanent CALLDATA.&nbsp;</p><p>Proto-danksharding, or <a href=""https://eips.ethereum.org/EIPS/eip-4844"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">EIP-4484</a>, is an intermediate step in the Danksharding journey which will further reduce gas costs and thus transaction fees on BASE and&nbsp;is expected to go live in Q4 2023.</p><h3>Integration with other platforms</h3><p>Because BASE is EVM-compatible, it’s very easy for developers to launch their platforms on BASE. Some of the biggest OG DeFi DApps such as <a href=""/review/aave-lend/"">AAVE</a>, <a href=""/review/sushiswap-sushi/"">SushiSwap</a>, <a href=""/review/curve-finance-crv/"">Curve Finance</a>, <a href=""/review/uniswap-uni/"">Uniswap</a> and <a href=""/review/compound-finance-comp/"">Compound</a> have already launched on BASE and boast high Total Value Locked (TVL). This demonstrates users' high confidence in a newly launched borderline experimental Layer 2.</p><h2>User Experience</h2><p>In Coinbase’s own words:</p><blockquote><p>&nbsp;“BASE is an easy way for decentralized apps to leverage Coinbase’s products and distribution. Seamless Coinbase integrations, easy fiat onramps, and access to the $130B assets on platform in the Coinbase ecosystem.” (Source: <a href=""https://help.coinbase.com/en/coinbase/other-topics/other/base"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coinbase)</a></p></blockquote><p>In real terms of how this will benefit actual users in the future, I do imagine a scenario where users will be able to buy their assets from the Coinbase centralized exchange (CEX) and immediately withdraw to the BASE L2. From there, users will be able to use most of their favourite <a href=""/analysis/best-ethereum-dapps/"">Ethereum DApps</a> as well as some new and unique DApps at substantially lower cost than if they were using Ethereum Layer 1.</p><p>Essentially, new users will be using L2s, paying for fees in ETH at low rates and depositing their crypto to Coinbase to sell for fiat currencies without even realizing they are using Ethereum infrastructure and benefitting from Ethereum’s security. In much the same way that not many of us really understand how the internet works but we use it daily, I imagine a similar scenario with L2s and I believe Coinbase will facilitate this transition with ease as it’s already a huge and popular CEX.&nbsp;</p><h2>Advantages</h2><p>Coinbase's L2 solution, BASE, offers several to benefits the cryptocurrency ecosystem:</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li><strong>Cost-Efficient Transactions: </strong>BASE significantly reduces transaction costs compared to Ethereum's Layer 1. In fact, BASE claims it is 10 times cheaper than the Ethereum mainnet. This eliminates a technical barrier for newcomers, making it easier for them to start using DeFi and DApps.</li><li><strong>User-Friendly Experience:</strong> Users won't necessarily need to understand the intricacies of Layer 2 technology. They can simply use Coinbase's platform and experience faster, cheaper transactions without the need for complex technical knowledge.</li><li><strong>Scalability for DeFi:</strong> The reduced fees and faster confirmation times on BASE can incentivize more users to participate in DeFi projects. This could lead to increased liquidity, improved yield opportunities, and a more robust DeFi ecosystem overall.</li><li><strong>Mainstream Adoption:</strong> By providing a more efficient and cost-effective user experience, BASE can help bridge the gap between cryptocurrency enthusiasts and mainstream users. This may encourage more people to explore and adopt blockchain technology.</li></ul><p>BASE aims to make cryptocurrency and blockchain technology more accessible, user-friendly, and cost-effective, ultimately benefiting both newcomers and seasoned crypto enthusiasts while contributing to the growth of the cryptocurrency ecosystem.</p><h2>BASE vs. Other Ethereum L2s</h2><p>Let’s compare BASE with some other popular blockchains as well as some ETH L2s using TVL and daily volume.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/defillama_BASE_2bf7a46715.png"" alt=""defillama BASE.png"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_defillama_BASE_2bf7a46715.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_defillama_BASE_2bf7a46715.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_defillama_BASE_2bf7a46715.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_defillama_BASE_2bf7a46715.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>BASE Stacks up Well Against Other Long-Established Blockchains Such as Solana or Cardano. The hackers responsible for the attack demanded a ransom of A$1.5 million not in <a href=""/education/what-is-bitcoin/"">Bitcoin</a> or <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a>, but in a lesser-known coin known as Monero.&nbsp;</p><p>Transparency is a major benefit of <a href=""/education/what-is-blockchain-technology/"">blockchain technology</a>, a public ledger recording all transactions. This helps prevent fraud and corruption because anyone with a little bit of knowledge about the underlying technology can identify suspicious transactions. Monero is the leading privacy protocol that works differently. By using privacy-enhancing technologies, it can obfuscate users' transactions and wallet addresses from the public view.</p><p><a href=""/deals/trading/bitget-crypto-exchange/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg"" alt=""Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Bitget_Deals_CTA_3581081c63_e7d4f61a3a.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>In this Monero guide, we will give you the lowdown on everything you need to know about how to use Monero.</p><h2>What is Monero?</h2><p>Monero XMR is a cryptocurrency with a twist. Just like other blockchains, you can use the Monero network to conduct transactions. However, the network is designed in a manner that hides transaction activity. To achieve this, Monero has a few tricks up its sleeves:</p><ul><li><strong>Ring signatures:</strong> This mixes real transactions with old decoy transactions to make it difficult to work out which transaction is legitimate.</li><li><strong>Stealth addresses:</strong> A one-time address that auto-generates numerous addresses for each transaction.</li><li><strong>RingCT: </strong>Also known as Ring Confidential Transactions, this feature mixes the amount sent so that the amount involved for each transaction cannot be easily tracked without the appropriate access.</li><li>On top of all this, a private ""<strong>view key</strong>"" is required to check the details of a transaction.</li></ul><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Ultimate_Monero_guide_f92ffb4081.jpg"" alt=""Monero guide.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Ultimate_Monero_guide_f92ffb4081.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Ultimate_Monero_guide_f92ffb4081.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Ultimate_Monero_guide_f92ffb4081.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Ultimate_Monero_guide_f92ffb4081.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Monero is a Privacy Coin that Hides Transactions Across its Network. Image via <a href=""https://www.getmonero.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Monero</a></figcaption></figure><p>Make no mistake, the Monero network is a public and decentralized ledger, just like Bitcoin and Ethereum. However, Monero has come up with ways to hide a user's footprints. In fact, Monero is so good that the IRS <a href=""https://cointelegraph.com/news/the-irs-offers-a-625-000-bounty-to-anyone-who-can-break-monero-and-lightning"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">offered</a> up to $625,000 to anyone who could break Monero's privacy features. Monero's privacy-centric ethos has given the company a loyal following among privacy advocates, crypto-anarchists and cypherpunks.</p><p>Monero XMR is far from the only privacy coin — <a href=""/review/dash-coin/"">Dash</a> and <a href=""/education/what-is-zcash/"">Zcash</a> are two other major privacy coins. Dash traces its roots to a privacy-focused coin called Darkcoin, but a strategy pivot later saw the company focus on digital payments. Zcash is still a privacy coin, but you can turn its privacy features off.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Monero_price_31515b3717.jpg"" alt=""Monero price.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Monero_price_31515b3717.jpg 196w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Monero_price_31515b3717.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Monero_price_31515b3717.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Monero XMR is the Largest Privacy Coin by Market Cap. Image via <a href=""https://www.coingecko.com/en/coins/monero"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">CoinGecko</a></figcaption></figure><p>With a <a href=""https://www.coingecko.com/en/coins/monero"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">market cap</a> of $2.67 billion, Monero XMR is the largest privacy-focused token. Its circulating supply is over 18.1 million coins and its current price is close to $147. XMR reached an all-time high of $542.33 in January 2018. By comparison, the market capitalization for both Dash and Zcash is far lower than Monero — $302.9 million and $206.6 million, respectively.</p><p>The initial supply of Monero’s private cryptocurrency that could be mined was 18.4 million XMR. After this amount was reached, mining incentives came in the form of ""tail emissions,"" which are small rewards of XMR that are fed into the system every 60 seconds, keeping miners incentivized to continue validating the network. When tail emissions are taken into account, the maximum supply of XMR is infinite. By comparison, both Dash and Zcash have a finite supply.</p><h2>A Brief History of Monero</h2><p>Man, this is still straight out of a movie!</p><p>Monero is based on the CryptoNote protocol. Bytecoin's July 2012 launch marked the first real-life implementation of CryptoNote. However, it was soon discovered that 80% of the coins had already been mined. The Bytecoin team came out with an explanation: The coin wasn't entirely new and had existed on the deep web for two years.</p><p>Needless to say, these claims weren't well received by the community, and some enthusiasts started to explore the CryptoNote protocol and concluded that the protocol itself was solid and innovative. The Bytecoin fork race was on!</p><p>In April 2014, the first Bytecoin fork, Bitmonero, was announced and a small community was formed which constituted the Monero core team at the time. However, something started to feel off. The founder, known only by an online alias, often disappeared for days at a time and tried to merge the new fork with Bytecoin against the community's wishes.</p><p>The founder eventually disappeared altogether, and Bitmonero went on to become the Monero project. Monero community members single-handedly saved it even though the Monero project may have had scammy beginnings.</p><p>We've covered all that and much, much more in our <a href=""/education/what-is-monero/"">in-depth Monero review</a>.</p><h2>How to Buy Monero XMR</h2><p>If you'd like to get your hands on some XMR coins, you can do so through reputable cryptocurrency exchanges such as <a href=""/review/binance/"">Binance</a>, <a href=""/review/kraken/"">Kraken</a> and <a href=""/review/coinbase-pro/"">Coinbase</a>, where you can also exchange Monero.</p><p>It's as simple as one, two, three!</p><ul><li><strong>Create your free account: </strong>You'll be asked to provide your name, email address and country of residence, and secure your account with a strong password.</li><li><strong>Connect your funding method:</strong> Once your account is verified, it's time for some financial information. You can link your credit/debit card to purchase XMR. You can also transfer fiat currencies from your bank account and then use that money to buy Monero.</li><li><strong>Buy Monero:</strong> And that's it! You can now purchase Monero. Just be sure to check payment details and fees before you purchase XMR.</li></ul><p>Head over to our <a href=""/review/best-crypto-exchanges/"">best crypto exchanges</a> list if you're having a tough time deciding which exchange to choose.</p><h2>How to Store Monero Safely: Top Monero Wallets</h2><p>To use Monero, you are going to need a wallet. These wallets are designed for users to securely and conveniently store XMR coins on the Monero blockchain.</p><p>The list below will provide top-level information, but if you'd like to get into the weeds, check out our full list of the <a href=""/analysis/best-monero-wallets/"">Top Monero Wallets</a>.</p><h3>Types of Monero wallets</h3><p>We're going to list our top Monero wallets across the three main categories: <a href=""/review/best-crypto-desktop-wallets/"">Desktop</a>, <a href=""/review/top-mobile-wallets/"">mobile</a> and <a href=""/analysis/best-hardware-wallets/"">hardware</a>. Here's a quick primer on each before we dive any further:</p><ul><li><strong>Desktop:</strong> These are installable software packs available for operating systems such as Windows, MacOS and Linux. If you're using this type of wallet, it's good to have anti-virus software on your system because Internet connectivity poses security vulnerabilities.</li><li><strong>Mobile:</strong> Desktop wallets made for smartphones, these wallets often use QR codes for transactions. They may be suitable for daily operations, but they're also more susceptible to malware infection when compared to hardware wallets.</li><li><strong>Hardware:</strong> The most secure method of storing your cryptocurrencies at the cost of convenience. These are hardware devices that individually handle public addresses and keys. Unlike desktop and mobile wallets, which are mostly free, you'll have to pony up cash for hardware wallets.</li></ul><p>With that out of the way, let's get back to the best Monero wallets.</p><p><strong>Desktop</strong></p><ul><li><strong>Guarda Wallet:</strong> This wallet supports over 50 major blockchains and over 400,000 tokens. It is available and both a desktop and mobile wallet.</li><li><strong>Official Monero Desktop GUI:</strong> The official Monero desktop client is available for Windows, Mac, Linux and other operating systems. But this is a full-node wallet, which means you’ll have to wait for the wallet to download and synch with the full blockchain.</li></ul><p><strong>Mobile</strong></p><ul><li><strong>MyMonero:</strong> This wallet is managed by the same Monero core developer who created the Monero Ledger integration, and provides users with secure, hosted Monero accounts.</li><li><a href=""/review/monerujo-wallet/""><strong>Monerujo</strong></a><strong>:</strong> Monerujo runs as a light wallet, giving you the option of running your own node or of using remote nodes to synchronize your wallet with the Monero blockchain. Monerujo is completely open source. Bad news for iOS users, however, as this wallet is only available on Android.</li></ul><p><strong>Hardware</strong></p><ul><li><strong>Ledger Nano:</strong> Ledger Nano was one of the first hardware wallets offering support for XMR. Ledger Nano comes in two versions: the <a href=""/review/ledger-nano-s-plus-review/"">Nano S Plus</a> for EUR79 and the <a href=""/review/ledger-nano-x/"">Nano X</a> for EUR149. The wallets allow you to manage over 5,500 coins and tokens.</li><li><strong>Trezor Model T:</strong> Costing $219, the <a href=""/review/trezor-model-t-review/"">Trezor Model T</a> is the only wallet in the Trezor lineup that supports XMR. Monero is supported on the Trezor Model T and can be used with third-party wallets including Monero GUI and Monero CLI.</li></ul><h3>Steps to Create a Monero Wallet</h3><p>Depending on which wallet you choose, the wallet creation process will look different. However, in a broader sense, each wallet has essentially the same pattern.</p><p>Here's what the process looks like for a software wallet:</p><ul><li><strong>Download the wallet:</strong> Most desktop wallets also offer apps for mobile devices. Once you have locked in on a wallet you like, download it to your desktop or phone.</li><li><strong>Backup the wallet:</strong> Be sure to create a backup of your wallet, we cover this step in our <a href=""/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/"">crypto safety article</a>. You may also need to set up your assets of choice. Some wallets also have an identity verification process where you'll be asked to submit a selfie or a government ID.</li><li><strong>Transfer your assets:</strong> There are several ways you can go about this process, including depositing funds from a bank account, exchanging cryptocurrencies or receiving them from another wallet.</li></ul><p>For a hardware wallet, you can expect to jump through a few extra hoops.</p><ul><li><strong>Select your device:</strong> Security features and the manufacturer's reputation should be considered when you're in the market for a hardware wallet. Ledger, Trezor, <a href=""/review/ngrave-zero-hardware-wallet/"">NGRAVE</a> and <a href=""/review/bc-vault-review/"">BC Vault</a> are some of the most trusted hardware wallets.</li><li><strong>Install required software:</strong> Most wallets have a setup wizard that will guide you through the installation process. Once you've downloaded the software to either your phone or desktop, you can connect your hardware wallet using a USB cable or Bluetooth connection.</li><li><strong>Transfer your cryptocurrency:</strong> You will need to link your hardware wallet to a brokerage account or an exchange to transfer your assets. Once the crypto is transferred, it will be stored offline.</li></ul><h2>Sending and Receiving Transactions</h2><p>There are a few important things to know about sending and receiving confidential transactions on the Monero blockchain.</p><ul><li><strong>Irreversible transactions:</strong> Monero transactions are irreversible once they have been confirmed by a miner. Transferred money by mistake? If you know who owns the receiving address, the only way to get it back is to ask the receiver to send it back to you (we know how that will go).</li><li><strong>Monero transactions are private:</strong> Monero employs privacy-enhancing technologies to hide details of a transaction, such as the sender's address, amount and the recipient's address. Even the payment recipient wouldn't know the sender's wallet address.</li><li><strong>Sender pays the fees:</strong> In Monero, the payment sender will be on the hook for any transaction fee.</li><li><strong>Transaction fees are not dependent on the amount:</strong> Instead, the fee depends on the network congestion at the time and the data size of your transaction, which increases together with the number of recipients and coins being spent.</li></ul><p>Right, let's now explore how to send and receive transactions on the Monero network.</p><h3>Creating a transaction</h3><p>In order to send a transaction, your node and wallet must be synchronized and the currently selected account must have an available unlocked balance. Next, enter the recipient's address (a Monero address starts with a 4 or an 8). Then, it's just a matter of entering the amount in XMR (conversion in USD or EUR should be visible). You can also conduct multiple transactions.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Monero_transaction_555de9ac6a.jpg"" alt=""Monero transaction.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Monero_transaction_555de9ac6a.jpg 196w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Monero_transaction_555de9ac6a.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>An Image by Monero on How to Make a Payment. Image via Monero</figcaption></figure><p>It's important to note that a transaction with multiple recipients will only pay a single transaction fee. However, more recipients means you'll be charged a higher fee.</p><p>The transaction fee does not depend on the amount sent, it depends on the network congestion at the time and the data size of your transaction.&nbsp;</p><p>Because of the level of privacy that Monero allows, people cannot just see a public record of payments you've sent. To validate transactions, you need to have a record of something called a ""TXKEY,"" which is only stored against a local copy of your Monero wallet. If you have created multiple wallets for the same address, then you cannot use any other wallet to obtain the TXKEY that you will require to prove payment.</p><h3>Receiving funds</h3><p>When someone sends Monero to you, the Monero network will include that transaction in a Monero block, a record of a batch of confidential transactions that have been announced to the Monero network of nodes. Each block takes on average two minutes to mine by the network. The successful mining of each block results in a confirmation.</p><p>To receive XMR, you only need to provide the payer with an address to which they can send funds. Most of the time, it's easier to just share a QR code and let the payer scan it, instead of copy-pasting the alphanumeric string. With the GUI, every generated address comes with its QR code.</p><p>The sender can scan the QR code with the Monero wallet on their phone and the recipient will receive their XMR in minutes. Remember you can generate as many addresses (subaddresses) as you want. This is useful if you want to keep funds separated for any reason.</p><h2>Monero Privacy Features</h2><p>By now, you're aware that Monero takes a privacy-centric approach to blockchain transactions, cloaking the movement of funds across its network.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Monero_privacy_features_56bdc50390.jpg"" alt=""Monero privacy features.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Monero_privacy_features_56bdc50390.jpg 208w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Monero_privacy_features_56bdc50390.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Monero_privacy_features_56bdc50390.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Monero_privacy_features_56bdc50390.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Monero Utilizes 3 Privacy-Enhancing Technologies to Hide Transactions. Infographic Created via Canva</figcaption></figure><p>Let's explore all three in detail.</p><h3>Ring Signatures</h3><p>Ring Signatures make it difficult to identify the sender and recipient in a transaction.</p><p>In cryptography, a ring signature is a type of digital signature that can be performed by any member of a group of users that each have keys. At Monero, a ring signature uses your account keys and a number of public keys pulled from the blockchain.</p><p>In a ""ring"" of possible signers, all ring members are equal and valid. This means an outside observer can't tell which of the possible signers in a signature group belongs to your account. As a result, ring signatures ensure that transaction outputs are untraceable.</p><h3>Stealth Addresses</h3><p>Stealth addresses create random one-time addresses for every transaction on behalf of the recipient. The recipient can publish just one address, yet have all of their incoming payments go to unique addresses on the blockchain, where they cannot be linked back to either the recipient's published address or any other transactions' addresses.</p><p>Stealth addresses allow only the sender and the receiver to know where a payment was sent.</p><h3>Ring Confidential Transactions (RingCT)</h3><p>This deals with how transaction amounts are hidden in Monero. Ring CT was implemented in January 2017 and became mandatory for all transactions on the network after September 2017.</p><p>RingCT introduced an improved version of ring signatures called ""A Multi-layered Linkable Spontaneous Anonymous Group signature"", which allows for hidden amounts, origins and destinations of transactions.</p><h2>Monero vs. Other Cryptocurrencies</h2><p>Bitcoin is the first and the most famous of all cryptocurrencies today. It is highly liquid and transaction history on the network is available to the general public. Monero, on the other hand, offers something the Bitcoin blockchain lacks: privacy and anonymity.</p><p>Here's a handy table that outlines the main differences between Monero and Bitcoin.</p><figure class=""table""><table><thead><tr><th>Feature</th><th>Bitcoin</th><th>Monero</th></tr></thead><tbody><tr><td>Privacy</td><td>Pseudonymous, not anonymous</td><td>Hides the sender, receiver, and amount of every transaction</td></tr><tr><td>Supply</td><td>Limited supply</td><td>Infinite supply due to “<a href=""https://cointelegraph.com/news/with-90-percent-of-monero-mined-attention-turns-to-tail-emission-from-2022"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Tail Emissions</a>”</td></tr><tr><td>Mining</td><td>Requires special hardware</td><td>Can be mined with home computers</td></tr><tr><td>Block size</td><td>Limited</td><td>Adaptive</td></tr><tr><td>Transaction speed</td><td>About 10 minutes</td><td>About 20 minutes</td></tr><tr><td>Frequency of forks</td><td>Low</td><td>High</td></tr></tbody></table></figure><h2>Monero Mining: How to Mine XMR</h2><p>Bitcoin brought the term ""crypto mining"" into the lexicon, but requires specialized hardware and dedicated mining farms have sprung up, leading to mining centralization. Monero's Cryptonote RandomX mining algorithm is resistant to this type of hardware and as such, keeps the mining decentralized.</p><p>Every transaction requires a miner to validate a transaction, and when miners complete this task they earn block rewards in the form of Monero XMR tokens.</p><p>There are two ways you can go about mining XMR coins:</p><ul><li>DIY</li><li>Monero mining pools</li></ul><p>Check out our dedicated guide to <a href=""/mining/monero-home/"">Monero Mining</a> if you would like to learn the ins and outs of Monero mining.&nbsp;</p><h3>DIY</h3><p>A proof of work consensus mechanism requires miners to validate transactions. Miners set up computer GPUs and CPUs, along with Monero mining software, which works to solve complex cryptographic puzzles. However, taking the DIY approach is basically like playing the lottery — your odds of being a successful solo miner are considerably low.&nbsp;</p><p>Miners receive <a href=""https://www.getmonero.org/resources/moneropedia/tail-emission.html "" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">0.6 XMR</a> for every block that gets added to the Monero blockchain. According to one estimate, Monero mining can fetch <a href=""https://www.coinwarz.com/mining/monero/calculator"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">$1 per day</a>.&nbsp;</p><h3>Mining pool</h3><p>Solo mining lacks the hash power needed to adequately compete with the larger mining pools. As a result, many people choose to join a mining pool. Sure, this will result in fewer rewards per miner, but there's a high chance of successfully mining blocks, which translates into regular rewards.</p><p>We also have a guide to finding the <a href=""/mining/best-monero-pools/"">best Monero mining pools</a> if you choose this route.</p><p><a href=""https://hub.coinbureau.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg"" alt=""Join-The-CoinBureau-Club-Inline-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Join_The_Coin_Bureau_Club_Inline_Banner_494b0ce69b.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Tips for Secure Monero Transactions</h2><p>With great power comes great responsibility! This is especially true for Monero, where transactions aren't public information and the only way to reverse one is to ask the other party to send it back, presuming you even know who you sent them to.</p><p>Here are a few tips to keep you safe on the Monero adventure trails.</p><ul><li><strong>Keep your software updated:</strong> ""Ugh, not again,"" I groan as I'm notified of a pending system update. Software updates may look like a minor inconvenience, but these security updates serve to patch any vulnerabilities before they are discovered by hackers.</li><li><strong>Invest in a hardware wallet:</strong> Hardware wallets provide the most bang for your buck when it comes to storing your Monero. A hardware wallet is a physical device that stores your private keys. Come transaction time, you can sign with a single click.</li><li><strong>Verify the recipient's address:</strong> Crypto wallet addresses are a complicated set of mumbo jumbo. To ensure accuracy, it's best to always copy/paste the address AND manually check the entire address because keyboard-hacking software is a thing now.</li><li><strong>Test small:</strong> Before you conduct a transaction, it's advisable to do a small test run to ensure everything is working A-OK. Instead of the whole amount, you can send a small amount of Monero as a test transaction.</li></ul><h2>Master Guide to Monero: Conclusion</h2><p>And, there you have it folks! This ultimate Monero guide has provided insights into creating a Monero wallet, buying XMR, sending and receiving transactions, and mining XMR. It also highlighted the importance of privacy and security in Monero transactions, emphasizing the use of hardware wallets, verifying recipient addresses, and conducting small test transactions to ensure smooth operations.</p><p>Monero distinguishes itself from other cryptocurrencies, such as Bitcoin, by offering true privacy. While Bitcoin transactions are pseudonymous and transparent, Monero ensures that all transaction details remain confidential. Moreover, Monero's dynamic block size, ASIC-resistant mining algorithm, and continuous tail emissions contribute to a decentralized and accessible mining network.</p><p>In a world where data breaches and surveillance are prevalent concerns, Monero remains a go-to option for individuals seeking financial privacy and transactional anonymity.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Education/how-to-use-ethereum/,How to Use Ethereum: Surfing Ethereum Transactions,Education,https://www.coinbureau.com/Analysis/cardano-use-cases/,Cardano Use Cases: How ADA is Shaping the Future,Analysis,https://www.coinbureau.com/Education/dappos/,dappOS: The Intent-Centric Operating Protocol,Education,https://www.coinbureau.com/Press Release/token2049-sets-record/,"TOKEN2049- Sets Record With Over 10,000 Attendees",Press Release,"<p style=""text-align:center;""><strong>With Over 10,000 Attendees Confirmed, TOKEN2049 Singapore Sets Record-Breaking</strong></p><p style=""text-align:center;""><strong>Attendee and Sponsor Numbers Amid All-Star Speaker Line-Up</strong></p><p style=""text-align:center;"">● <i>World’s largest Web3 event hits full capacity with over 10,000+ attendees globally, 300+ exhibitors and 400+</i></p><p style=""text-align:center;""><i>side events;
