The S&amp;P 500, a revered index tracing the growth of the largest U.S. companies, stands as a testament to the enduring strength of established markets, with its historical returns and pivotal role in assessing economic health.</p><p>Contrastingly, the realm of cryptocurrencies has stormed onto the financial stage, offering breathtaking returns and embodying a paradigm shift in investment ideologies. In this digital arena, crypto tokens have achieved meteoric rises (and losses), outpacing the traditional market indices by margins that appear surreal. The volatile nature of the crypto landscape, while presenting risks, has also demonstrated its resilience to macroeconomic turmoil for the most part.&nbsp;</p><p>As the global financial landscape evolves and adapts to new challenges, both the S&amp;P 500 and cryptocurrencies continue to shape investor strategies. The former, grounded in historical significance and offering steady growth, remains a foundation for many portfolios. The latter, with its explosive returns and transformative potential, is intriguing for risk-tolerant investors seeking to capitalize on innovation and disruption.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Review/phantom-wallet-review/,Phantom Wallet Review: Top Solana Wallet Pros and Cons,Review,"<blockquote><p>""The crypto wallet that’ll take you places.""</p></blockquote><p>That's what Phantom Wallet proclaims on its website. And a quick glance makes it clear the company wants it to be your go-to choice for interacting with networks on three blockchains.</p><p>While decentralized finance (<a href=""/adoption/how-safe-is-decentralized-finance/"">DeFi</a>) allows crypto users to transact without an intermediary, you still need a crypto wallet to transact with and store your digital assets, and there's no shortage of <a href=""/analysis/best-hardware-wallets/"">hardware wallets</a>,<a href=""/review/best-crypto-desktop-wallets/""> desktop wallets</a> or <a href=""/review/top-mobile-wallets/"">mobile wallets</a> thanks to wide crypto adoption.</p><p>In this Phantom Wallet review, we will look at its security, usability, supported blockchains and other features it rolled out recently. Let's take a deep dive!</p><p><strong>Phantom Wallet Review: Summary</strong></p><blockquote><p>Initially renowned as a Solana-based digital asset wallet, Phantom Wallet has since branched out to include <a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a> and <a href=""/education/polygon-2023-beginners-guide-to-matic/"">Polygon</a> networks as well. At its core, Phantom Wallet aims to be a hassle-free way to make make managing your private keys for DeFi projects easy.</p><p>It is a decentralized Web3 self-custodial browser extension and wallet that works with some of the most famous browsers such as Firefox, Chrome, Brave and Edge. It can be accessed through your iOS or Android mobile device as well. You can use the wallet to collect NFTs, send and receive cryptocurrencies and tokens, and swap tokens.</p></blockquote><p>If you are interested in Guy's take on the Phantom Wallet, feel free to check out his beginner's guide below:</p><figure class=""media""><div data-oembed-url=""https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=zI-Xd9vVnwY""><div style=""position: relative; padding-bottom: 100%; height: 0; padding-bottom: 56.2493%;""><iframe src=""https://www.youtube.com/embed/zI-Xd9vVnwY"" style=""position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; top: 0; left: 0;"" frameborder=""0"" allow=""autoplay; encrypted-media"" allowfullscreen=""""></iframe></div></div></figure><p><strong>The Key Features of Phantom Wallet are:</strong></p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li><strong>Solana staking:</strong> Users who hold SOL tokens can participate in the Solana network and earn rewards by delegating their tokens to stake with one of the hundreds of validators who run, maintain and secure the blockchain. A smaller validator with a higher APY and lower commission is best for the Solana ecosystem and your returns, according to the company. Phantom Wallet recommends <a href=""https://www.validators.app/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">validators.app</a> or <a href=""https://stakeview.app/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">StakeView.app</a> to find a ranked list of the best options.</li><li><strong>Token swap:</strong> Phantom Wallet allows you to conduct in-app swaps for Ethereum, Polygon and Solana networks. It charges a flat 0.85% fee for searching and offering the best pricing available for most swaps. This fee is on top of <a href=""/education/complete-guide-to-crypto-network-fees/"">network fees.</a></li><li><strong>NFTs and collectables storage:</strong> Non-fungible tokens may not be hot right now, but Phantom Wallet makes storing them easy. A feature lets you group similar NFTs together, saving you precious time of having to sift through hundreds of them to find what you're looking for. You can hide and remove unwanted spam, discover new collections, and manage listings all from within your wallet. Users also have access to metadata like floor price, last sale price, total return and total unique holders.</li><li><strong>Multichain support:</strong> Phantom Wallet may have started with support for just the Solana ecosystem, but it has since added Ethereum and Polygon to the list of supported networks. You can import your existing <a href=""/education/metamask-beginners-guide/"">MetaMask</a>, <a href=""/review/solana-sol/"">Solana</a> or EVM wallets to Phantom. You can view all your tokens and NFTs in one place and connect to apps automatically.</li><li><strong>Ledger integration</strong>: If you have a <a href=""/review/ledger-nano-x/"">Ledger hardware wallet</a>, you can use it for Solana, Ethereum and Polygon through Phantom Wallet. However, if you're looking to integrate Ledger with Phantom, it can only be achieved via Chrome, Brave or Microsoft Edge; Firefox isn't currently supported. Phantom mobile apps currently don't support Ledger hardware wallets either, but the company plans to add this feature soon.</li><li><strong>Non-custodial:</strong> Phantom Wallet puts you in the driver's seat, which means users can control their assets completely without any intrusion from a third party. In a non-custodial wallet, users have full control of their wallet. On the flip side, if you lose your seed phrase, the account cannot be recovered.</li></ul><p><a href=""/deals/trading/swissborg/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Swissborg_inline_57564f04fd.jpg"" alt=""Swissborg inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Swissborg_inline_57564f04fd.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Swissborg_inline_57564f04fd.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Swissborg_inline_57564f04fd.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Phantom Wallet Overview</h2><figure class=""table""><table><tbody><tr><td>Type of wallet</td><td>Software (browser extension support for Chrome, Brave, Firefox and Edge)</td></tr><tr><td>Released</td><td>2021</td></tr><tr><td>Supported networks</td><td>Solana, Ethereum and Polygon</td></tr><tr><td>Cost</td><td>Free to download</td></tr><tr><td>Staking</td><td>Yes, Solana tokens only</td></tr><tr><td>Mobile app</td><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><td>Security</td><td>High</td></tr><tr><td>NFT support</td><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><td>Transaction or balance limits</td><td>No</td></tr></tbody></table></figure><h2>What is Phantom Wallet?</h2><p>Phantom is a non-custodial multichain <a href=""/adoption/what-is-web-3-0/"">Web3</a> wallet with support for Solana, Ethereum and Polygon networks. With self-custody, users can use DApps without any third-party interference. This also means users will be responsible for their transactions and security. Phantom works as a browser extension, similar to <a href=""/education/metamask-beginners-guide/"">MetaMask</a>. For those looking to use it on the go, the company also has apps for Android and iOS devices.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Homepage_94a88822c2.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet review"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Homepage_94a88822c2.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Homepage_94a88822c2.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Homepage_94a88822c2.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Homepage_94a88822c2.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>A look at the Phantom homepage. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom</a></figcaption></figure><p>Phantom Wallet started in 2021 with 40,000 active beta testers supporting the Solana ecosystem. In the same year, it <a href=""https://www.theblock.co/post/111249/defi-wallet-solana-phantom-9-million-series-a-a16z"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">raised $9 million</a> to fuel its growth plans and introduced an in-app token swapper. A year later, it raised $109 million in a <a href=""https://techcrunch.com/2022/01/31/paradigm-invests-in-solana-wallet-app-phantom-at-1-2-billion-valuation/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Series B funding</a> round at a $1.2 billion valuation, achieving the coveted unicorn tag. Today, the company boasts over three million users, and it has launched a host of features since its nascent days.</p><p>Support for Ethereum and Polygon network arguably marked its biggest leap and broadened the scope of assets and decentralized applications users can access and interact with through the app. With Phantom, you can:</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li>Manage your crypto and NFTs</li><li>Stake Solana</li><li>Swap tokens</li><li>Access DeFi applications</li></ul><p>Phantom Wallet aims to provide users with a secure and user-friendly way to manage their digital assets, interact with decentralized applications (DApps), and participate in DeFi ecosystem. Phantom allows users to store their private keys, giving them full control over their digital assets. With integrated MoonPay and Coinbase Pay, users can purchase or transfer <a href=""/education/ethereum-2-guide/"">ETH</a>, <a href=""/review/matic-network/"">MATIC</a> and SOL directly from their wallet.</p><p>You can also connect your Ledger Nano hardware wallet with Phantom. However, this feature is only available on Chrome, Brave and Microsoft Edge web browsers. Phantom's iOS and Android mobile apps do not currently support this integration, but the company plans to bring this feature to its mobile apps soon.</p><p>It is important to note that last year, some 8,000 Solana hot wallets were <a href=""https://twitter.com/PeckShieldAlert/status/1554674781383180289?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1554674781383180289%7Ctwgr%5E9efe7ae5ccf152cfaa357ef15c5b2320e520623c%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&amp;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fcointelegraph.com%2Fnews%2Fongoing-solana-based-wallet-hack-has-already-seen-millions-drained"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">hacked</a> for an estimated loss of about $8 million. Phantom, then a fast-growing Solana wallet, said at the time that it wasn't a “<a href=""https://twitter.com/phantom/status/1554626111535026177"">Phantom-specific issue</a>” but the hack did affect Phantom wallet users.</p><h2>Phantom Wallet Review: Top Features</h2><h3>Token Swaps in the Phantom Wallet</h3><p>Phantom launched its in-app token swapper in June 2021 and recorded over $1 billion in swap volume by October of that year. As it currently stands, in-app swaps are available for EVM chains. Phantom has a built-in swapper system, which aggregates liquidity from multiple decentralized exchanges or DEXes.&nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Phantom_Wallet_Token_Swaps_11c087c7c6.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Token Swaps.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Phantom_Wallet_Token_Swaps_11c087c7c6.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Phantom_Wallet_Token_Swaps_11c087c7c6.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Phantom_Wallet_Token_Swaps_11c087c7c6.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Phantom_Wallet_Token_Swaps_11c087c7c6.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>A Look at Swapping Tokens in the Phantom Wallet. Image via <a href=""https://twitter.com/phantom/status/1389298960989257729"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Twitter.com/phantom</a></figcaption></figure><p>Phantom charges a flat 0.85% fee on token swaps in addition to network fees. It also uses the default setting of slippage limited to 0.5%. As is the case with swaps, it's important that you have enough of the network's native token for transaction costs (ETH tokens on Ethereum, Matic on Polygon and SOL on Solana). An insufficient native token balance will cause a swap fail to occur. You can learn more about network fees and transaction costs in our <a href=""/education/complete-guide-to-crypto-network-fees/"">Guide to Network Fees.</a></p><h3>Crypto Staking in Phantom Wallet</h3><p>Cryptocurrency staking allows holders of certain cryptocurrencies to participate in the network's operations and earn rewards in return for locking up their coins as collateral. Phantom currently only supports Solana tokens for this purpose. The company recommends checking validators.app or StakeView.app to find a ranked list of the best options based on current network conditions.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Staking_363b3e9958.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Staking"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Staking_363b3e9958.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Staking_363b3e9958.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Phantom Wallet currently only lets users stake SOL. Image via <a href=""https://help.phantom.app/hc/en-us/articles/4406374138771-How-to-stake-Solana-SOL-"">Phantom Wallet&nbsp;</a></figcaption></figure><p>APY for Solana staking can currently fetch APY of as high as 9%, according to StakeView. Phantom recommends choosing a smaller validator with a higher APY and lower commission. You can check your Solana staking rewards in the Phantom app. These rewards cannot be withdrawn unless you unstake your SOL. Instead, rewards are compounded and you earn more SOL.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Staking2_d48ae631b5.jpg"" alt=""Solana Staking Rewards"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Staking2_d48ae631b5.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Staking2_d48ae631b5.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>APY for Solana staking can currently fetch APY of as high as 9%. Image via <a href=""https://help.phantom.app/hc/en-us/articles/4406374138771-How-to-stake-Solana-SOL-"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>If at any point you'd like to unstake, you must first ensure you have enough SOL for gas fees (0.05 SOL is enough for most transactions). Otherwise, your transaction will fail to go through.</p><h3>Phantom Wallet NFT Support</h3><p>Phantom lets you connect to several NFT marketplaces. You can sell your NFTs and immediately get funds using the ""Instant Sell"" feature.</p><p>Here's how that works: Phantom aggregates offers from the top marketplaces to get you the best possible price. It's then served to you directly within your NFT. If you have an offer, you'll see an ""Instant Sell"" banner with a ""sell now” price listed, which is your NFT's highest available bid.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/NF_Ts_82995e1f4d.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet NFTs"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_NF_Ts_82995e1f4d.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_NF_Ts_82995e1f4d.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_NF_Ts_82995e1f4d.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_NF_Ts_82995e1f4d.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Phantom lets you connect to several NFT marketplaces. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/explore"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>You'll have access to information such as the marketplace's name, estimated fees, what your profit/loss looks like, and other helpful information to help you make an informed decision. The company currently gathers bids from Solana and EVM marketplaces like OpenSea, Blur, LooksRare, X2Y2, Magic Eden and Tensor.</p><h3>Phantom Hardware Wallet Integration</h3><p>If you're looking to use Phantom to manage Solana and SPL tokens on your <a href=""/review/ledger-nano-s-plus-review/"">Ledger hardware wallet</a>, you'll first have to enable ""blind signing."" However, if you have already installed the Solana, Ethereum and Polygon apps onto your Ledger, then you can skip this step.</p><p>Once you've connected your Ledger wallet with Phantom, you can send/deposit funds using the Ledger accounts you've connected in the networks you selected to interact with Solana, Ethereum and Polygon dApps using your Ledger device.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Ledger_ff917de69e.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Ledger integration"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Ledger_ff917de69e.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Ledger_ff917de69e.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>You can connect your Ledger hardware wallet with Phantom. Image via <a href=""https://help.phantom.app/hc/en-us/articles/4406388670483-How-to-use-your-Ledger-Nano-hardware-wallet"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>At this time, the Ledger hardware wallet integration isn't available for the Firefox web browser or the Phantom mobile apps.</p><h3>Phantom Sign In With Solana</h3><p>If you connect your wallet to any major app, you'll likely be met with a popup message that, to an average human, is just a bunch of random numbers and letters. But that mumbo jumbo is meant to authenticate your identity. When you connect your wallet to an app, most wallets share your address without verifying that the private keys are in your control.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Untitledfff_b3bbcd3428.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Transaction Signing"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Untitledfff_b3bbcd3428.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Untitledfff_b3bbcd3428.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>What a typical authentication message looks like. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/learn/developers/sign-in-with-solana"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>Sign In With Solana lets apps authenticate their users with just a Solana address. Solana developers can make use of the new sign-in method on all extension platforms, with mobile support coming soon. This new method prompts users to connect and sign a standardized authentication message in a single click.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Phantom_Wallet_Review_16d395feb4.jpg"" alt=""Sign with Solana"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Phantom_Wallet_Review_16d395feb4.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Phantom_Wallet_Review_16d395feb4.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Phantom_Wallet_Review_16d395feb4.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Image via Phantom</figcaption></figure><p>As part of the launch, Phantom worked with Solana Labs to create an open standard for the Solana ecosystem. The newly launched sign-in method comes with full support for the Solana Wallet Standard's SIWS feature.</p><h3>Phantom Solana-Only Mode</h3><p>Don't care about Phantom's multichain support? You can turn your Phantom Wallet into a Solana-focused experience.</p><p>Once you switch to the Solana-only mode, you can manage your Solana accounts, balances, tokens and NFTs without seeing other chains, network icons or EVM addresses. If you'd like to return to Phantom Multichain, you can do so by turning off the Solana-only toggle in the menu. Switching between the two modes doesn't disrupt account balances or assets.</p><h2>Is Phantom Wallet Safe?</h2><h3>Phantom Wallet Security</h3><p>The bedrock of any crypto wallet is its emphasis on security. Cryptocurrencies operate on the principles of trustless transactions and immutable ledgers, which mandate rigorous security protocols.</p><p>Phantom Wallet's code has been independently <a href=""https://kudelskisecurity.com/audits/?_sft_audit-projects=phantom"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">audited</a> by <a href=""https://kudelskisecurity.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Kudelski Security</a>. In addition, its scam detection flags malicious transactions instantly. There's also a bounty program that pays white hat hackers up to $50,000 if you find a vulnerability that may cause users to lose their money.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Security_50f358aae6.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Security"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Security_50f358aae6.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Security_50f358aae6.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Security_50f358aae6.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Security_50f358aae6.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Phantom Wallet employs top-notch security measures. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/security"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>Here are a few other things to consider from a security perspective:</p><ul><li><strong>Non-custodial wallet:</strong> A self-custody wallet like Phantom provides users with full control and ownership over their private keys and digital assets. This means you'll have sole responsibility over transactions, including sending and receiving your digital assets. And because users control their private keys, they can maintain a higher level of privacy compared to custodial wallets, where third-party services might have access to transaction history and other user data.</li><li><strong>Transaction previews:</strong> Transaction previews act as a firewall that identifies malicious transactions and warns you before they're approved by you. They protect users against attacks such as phishing, dApp-level DNS hijacking and software supply chain attacks, among many others. It also provides users with real-time warnings and human-readable transaction context.</li><li><strong>Open-source block list: </strong>The company has an open-source and community-maintained block list of malicious domains that it blocks users from mistakenly connecting to. Once Phantom finds out about a malicious token or NFT, it adds the contract address and domain to the block list. This hides the NFT from the wallet and creates a warning if the user tries to connect to the site. This block list is updated every day and currently houses over 2,000 domains.</li><li><strong>Burn NFT:</strong> This feature is available across all devices, and it allows for the manual removal of any unwanted spam NFTs. Once an NFT is burned, it results in the permanent removal of the digital collectible from your Phantom Wallet. In return, you're rewarded with Solana tokens. This is because when you burn an NFT, you are reclaiming some of the SOL that a scammer spent on sending you an NFT in the first place.</li></ul><h2>How To Install the Phantom Browser Extension</h2><p>To ensure you download the official Phantom extension and not a malicious app, it's best to download Phantom Wallet directly from the <a href=""https://phantom.app/download"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">company's website</a>.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Download_af91a82396.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Download"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Download_af91a82396.jpg 231w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Download_af91a82396.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Download_af91a82396.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Download_af91a82396.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>To ensure you're not the victim of a scam, you should download the browser extension from the company's website. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/download"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>Once you have downloaded the extension, all that's left is following the steps in your respective extension store to add the Phantom wallet extension to your browser. After installing, you should see Phantom open in a new tab.</p><p>In order for Phantom to work, you'll have to grant it permission to ""read and change all your data on all websites."" The company explains that this permission is needed so dApps can engage with the blockchain network and access public wallet data such as your NFTs, transaction history or token balances.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Permissions_bce9d5c5fd.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Guide"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Permissions_bce9d5c5fd.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Permissions_bce9d5c5fd.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>In order for Phantom to work on your browser, you'll have to grant it this permission. Image via <a href=""https://help.phantom.app/hc/en-us/articles/16514003246611-Why-does-Phantom-require-browser-permissions-"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>If you have privacy concerns, Phantom recommends that you create a separate browser profile dedicated to your Phantom Wallet. This will allow you to explore Web3 while keeping your data access strictly controlled.</p><h2>Phantom Wallet on Mobile</h2><p>As noted, Phantom Wallet is also available for Android and iOS mobile devices to give you access to crypto, NFTs and apps while on the go. Again, it's best to get the links for your mobile phone through the company's website so you don't fall victim to a malicious app.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Mobile_9a2366e878.jpg"" alt=""Phantom Wallet Mobile"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Mobile_9a2366e878.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Mobile_9a2366e878.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Mobile_9a2366e878.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Mobile_9a2366e878.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Setting your account via a mobile app is similar to doing it through a web browser. Image via <a href=""https://phantom.app/download"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Phantom Wallet</a></figcaption></figure><p>Setting up via a cell phone works just like it does on a web browser. One difference is that you'll have to enable biometric security using a fingerprint or facial recognition to ensure you're the only one with access to the wallet. Once that's done, you'll be presented with your secret recovery phrase, also known as a seed phrase.</p><p>If you have an existing wallet, you can simply enter your recovery phrase and restore your wallet on Phantom.</p><h2>How to Use Phantom Wallet</h2><p>As far as crypto wallets go, Phantom Wallet is pretty standard. As you're aware by now, you can use Phantom on certain web browsers and your mobile phone.</p><p>Once you've downloaded the extension for your browser, you can either choose to create a new wallet or restore an existing wallet to Phantom. If you're importing a wallet to Phantom, simply enter your seed phrase to restore your wallets.</p><p>If you create a new wallet, you'll be asked to create a password. Once you've chosen a strong password, select ""continue."" You'll then be presented with your confidential recovery phrase. It's <strong>extremely important</strong> that you write this down and store it in a safe location We cover this step in great detail in our <a href=""/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/"">Crypto Safety Guide</a>.&nbsp;</p><p>Phantom has an integration with 1Password for the safe storage of recovery phrases. Next, you'll find the keyboard shortcuts to access the Phantom app. Select ""continue"" and you're all set.</p><p>Setting up Phantom Wallet on your mobile phone works in the same manner.</p><h2>Phantom vs. MetaMask Comparison</h2><figure class=""table""><table><tbody><tr><td><strong>Feature</strong></td><td><strong>Phantom</strong></td><td><strong>MetaMask</strong></td></tr><tr><td>Number of users</td><td>Over 3 million</td><td>Over 30 million</td></tr><tr><td>Year released</td><td>2021</td><td>2016</td></tr><tr><td>Blockchain supported</td><td>Solana, Ethereum and Polygon</td><td>Ethereum, Arbitrum, Optimism, Binance Smart Chain, Polygon, and Avalanche</td></tr><tr><td>Type of wallet</td><td>Software, non-custodial</td><td>Software, non-custodial</td></tr><tr><td>Browser extension</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><td>Mobile app</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><td>Token swap</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td></tr><tr><td>Swap fee</td><td>0.85%</td><td>0.875%</td></tr><tr><td>Hardware wallet integration</td><td>Yes</td><td>Yes</td></tr></tbody></table></figure><p>As you can see, Phantom Wallet and MetaMask have more similarities than differences. A recent <a href=""https://cer.live/wallets"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">CER audit</a> listed MetaMask as the #1 most secure software wallet, which is further emphasized by the fact that MetaMask is the most widely used wallet in the world.&nbsp;</p><p>If your main focus is on the Ethereum ecosystem, or any of the chains supported by MetaMask, then that will be the likely choice for most users. However, if your main interest is in the Solana Ecosystem, then Phantom is a good choice.</p><p><a href=""https://www.tiktok.com/@coinbureau?lang=en"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg"" alt=""CoinBureau-Blog-TikTok-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Phantom Wallet Review: Closing Thoughts</h2><p>Phantom Wallet offers a comprehensive and user-friendly solution for managing digital assets, interacting with decentralized applications and participating in the DeFi ecosystem. Image via OKX</figcaption></figure><h2>Best Place to Store Bitcoin</h2><p>Bitcoin bought from the OKX exchange automatically gets credited to your spot account balance. Note that any funds on the exchange are under their custody, so not necessarily the safest place to store your crypto. It's preferable to store them in a <a href=""/education/types-of-crypto-wallets/"">crypto wallet</a>.&nbsp;</p><p>A crypto wallet is a device, which can be virtual or an actual thing, that holds the private keys needed to access your crypto on the blockchain, <i>not the actual funds</i>. Whoever holds the private keys is allowed to move the funds out of the blockchain where they are stored. With an exchange, the funds are stored in an account with a wallet address and these funds are ultimately controlled by the exchange. The only thing you can do is trust that they won't move your funds without first obtaining your permission or go bankrupt and lose all your assets.&nbsp;</p><p>If you're new to crypto and still learning the ropes, <a href=""/review/okx-wallet"">OKX has its own wallet</a> that you can store funds in. It removes the third-party risk associated with keeping funds on the exchange. Aside from having ownership of your own funds, you can also explore the world of DeFi and Web3 through the wallet. &nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/OKX_Wallet_f6483fb07d.png"" alt=""OKX Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_OKX_Wallet_f6483fb07d.png 172w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_OKX_Wallet_f6483fb07d.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_OKX_Wallet_f6483fb07d.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_OKX_Wallet_f6483fb07d.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>OKX wallet for your Web3 needs. Image via OKX</figcaption></figure><p>What OKX offers is something called a hot wallet aka a software wallet. It is connected to the Internet and allows you to interact with DApps in the DeFi space and NFTs. However, it is vulnerable to risks such as hacking into the wallet itself or your funds can be drained by giving permission for other DApps to access it automatically.&nbsp;</p><p>The next level-up option is a cold wallet, also known as a <a href=""/analysis/best-hardware-wallets/"">hardware wallet</a>. This type of wallet is not connected to the Internet and it requires an actual hardware device, usually the size of a USB key or something similar. What keeps this wallet safe is that it's not constantly connected to the Internet, so less chances of someone being able to hack into your wallet to gain access to your private keys.&nbsp;</p><p>The downside though is that these wallets aren't free and you will need to take very good care of your devices and make sure no one else who is not authorised has access to it.&nbsp;</p><p>You can learn more about wallets by reading about <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/types-of-crypto-wallets"">the types of crypto wallets available</a> or <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/how-do-hardware-wallets-work"">how hardware wallets work</a> before deciding on whether you need one.</p><p>We also go into far greater detail on the security strengths and weaknesses of crypto storage devices in our <a href=""/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/"">Crypto Safety Guide</a>.</p><h2>How to Convert Bitcoin to Fiat Currency with OKX</h2><p>OKX has no option for cash withdrawals, only crypto withdrawals are permitted. Users on OKX are able to withdraw Bitcoin or any other supported cryptocurrencies, or sell Bitcoin for stablecoins and withdraw fiat-pegged stablecoins to a wallet or another exchange as an alternative. &nbsp;</p><p><a href=""https://www.tiktok.com/@coinbureau?lang=en"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg"" alt=""CoinBureau-Blog-TikTok-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Conclusion</h2><p>The OKX platform is a solid one for all manners of trading. This section goes behind the scenes to explain how they differ—the positives and downsides and what type of copy replication might suit you best.</p><h3>Mirror Trading: A Hands-Off Approach</h3><p>Mirror trading is when you copy the trading strategies of other traders. Companies offering a mirror trading service combine the best-performing strategies of their top traders to give reliable signals.&nbsp;</p><p>Nowadays, mirror trading is smarter, using big data and artificial intelligence to make signals accurate and predictable. It's great for investors wanting an easy, hands-off crypto trading experience.</p><p>The only downside is that mirror trading requires you to copy everything – you can't choose specific signals to follow. The entire process is automated, so you don't have much control.&nbsp;</p><p>Mirror trading requires special software or a MetaTrader plugin that does it all for you to do mirror trading.</p><h3>Copy Trading: Emulate Top Traders</h3><p>Copy trading is a more advanced version of mirror trading. Unlike mirror trading, where you must follow all signals without control, copy trading allows you to select specific traders whose trades you want to copy. Your trading account automatically copies a trade whenever the chosen trader opens a trade.</p><p>Copy trading is still automated, but you can switch between traders and follow their strategies at different times. In addition, you can even choose to follow multiple traders for various currency pairs, depending on the platform's capabilities.</p><p>One of the key benefits of following the best traders is that it provides an opportunity to learn from their strategies. You can monitor their open trades in real-time and try to understand the reasoning behind each trading decision they make.&nbsp;</p><p>Copy trading lets you gain valuable insights into successful trading techniques you may use later if you intend to start trading crypto yourself.</p><h3>Social Trading: Being Part of a Trading Team</h3><p>A popular copy trade service is social trading. It's a blend of mirror and copy trading with a social aspect. Unlike relying solely on automated signals and plugins, social trading lets you join a community of traders to engage in real-time discussions about market updates.</p><p>Social trading offers a learning opportunity for crypto trading novices. You won't have to guess the reasoning behind the trades, such as the technical and fundamental analysis. Instead, you'll have a group of traders to discuss the crypto market and make trading decisions together.&nbsp;</p><p>From experience, I know trading is a lonely game, so being part of a community can improve your trading skills as you learn from others.</p><p>The best part is that social trading is relatively safe because you retain complete control over your decisions. The signals and insights from the trading group or forum are only guidance and trading aids. This way, you'll master advanced trading strategies much faster and with the support of a knowledgeable community.</p><p>The downside of social trading is that executing successful trades relies on timing, and you need to understand the basics of completing an order and setting a stop loss and exit point. It sounds easy, but the tendency to interfere with trades is a daily reality for <a href=""/education/cryptocurrency-beginners-guide/"">novice traders</a>.&nbsp;</p><p>In addition, the proviso is that you join a reputable social trading community with a solid background in supporting its members.</p><p><a href=""https://www.tiktok.com/@coinbureau?lang=en"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg"" alt=""CoinBureau-Blog-TikTok-Banner.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Coin_Bureau_Blog_Tik_Tok_Banner_6c43c3059f.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Bitget Copy Trading Closing Thoughts</h2><p>Bitget's copy trading service is one of the most popular in the crypto space. You can opt for the Bitget wallet or choose from various wallet types.</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li>Cold Storage: A cold wallet is an offline physical storage product that looks like a memory stick. When you are ready to transfer your Bitcoin (BTC), you connect it to your computer and the Bitget exchange.&nbsp;<br><br>When setting up your <a href=""/analysis/best-hardware-wallets/"">hardware wallet</a>, you create a recovery phrase. It's crucial to store this phrase securely because if you lose it, you cannot recover your wallet and lose whatever assets are held.&nbsp;<br><br>Watch Guy's take on the <a href=""https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=BrRP-KxUnoU"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coin Bureau YouTube</a> video to learn more about hardware wallets,<br>&nbsp;</li><li>Hot Wallet: It can be an online <a href=""/review/top-mobile-wallets/"">mobile app</a> or <a href=""/review/best-crypto-desktop-wallets/"">desktop wallet</a>. It also requires a recovery phrase. A hot wallet is convenient but riskier than a cold wallet because it is permanently online, leaving it vulnerable to remote attacks such as <a href=""/analysis/ransomware-cybercrime-brief-overview-current-security-concerns-crypto-space/"">hacks and phishing scams</a>.<br>&nbsp;</li><li>Paper Wallet: Similar to the cold wallet, a <a href=""/education/types-of-crypto-wallets/#5.-paper-wallets"">paper wallet</a> is an offline, printed version of private and public keys. The potential downside of a paper wallet is it's easy to lose a bit of paper.&nbsp;</li></ul><p>Once you have decided on the best crypto wallet, the next step is to buy Bitcoin (BTC) on Bitget.</p><h2>Buying Bitcoin On Bitget</h2><p>At the top of the payment page, you have a choice of the following:&nbsp;</p><ul style=""list-style-type:disc;""><li>Credit / Debit Card</li><li>P2P Trading (0 Fees)</li><li>Third-party</li></ul><p><strong>Credit / Debit Card</strong></p><p>Before paying with a debit or credit card, Bitget requires that you verify your identity. Now that’s something I sure didn’t have in my crypto 2023 predictions.</p><figure class=""image image_resized"" style=""width:84.58%;""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_70afc79f65.png"" alt=""Udi Wertheimer Eric Wall"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_70afc79f65.png 143w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_70afc79f65.png 458w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_70afc79f65.png 687w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_70afc79f65.png 916w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>The Bitcoin Miami wizard appearance Source:</i><a href=""https://twitter.com/udiWertheimer/status/1660829752427687937?s=20"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i> Twitter/udiWertheimer</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>There is context to this. The duo co-founded <a href=""https://taprootwizards.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Taproot Wizards</a>, one of the first-ever NFT projects in the Bitcoin blockchain. Udi and Eric started the project as a response to the reluctant-to-change reaction from some Bitcoin community members after ordinals first entered the scene. Many defended that Bitcoin should be used for financial transactions exclusively, as Satoshi intended, and anything else may add complexities that damage its ethos and may harm decentralization.</p><p>On the other side of the coin, the duo believes in growth by embracing change and creating products that people want. They wanted to make Bitcoin “fun” again. Their vision is shared with a large part of the crypto community (and so is their troll-ish posturing toward the more dogmatic <a href=""/education/bitcoin-maximalism/"">Bitcoin Maximalists</a>).&nbsp;</p><p>So why do I bring this up? Well, firstly, the ludicrousness is quite entertaining. Secondly, it illustrates the two sides of sentiment within the Bitcoin community. Since people started using ordinals in mid-January 2023, discussions have shown different views within the community on how the Bitcoin blockchain should be used regarding its technical applications and larger narrative.&nbsp;</p><p>But I also bring it up because the act symbolizes a much more critical phenomenon – Bitcoin is changing. You can get Guy's take on Bitcoin's evolution below if you are interested:</p><figure class=""media""><div data-oembed-url=""https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=IyuwI5q7HwA&amp;t=379s""><div style=""position: relative; padding-bottom: 100%; height: 0; padding-bottom: 56.2493%;""><iframe src=""https://www.youtube.com/embed/IyuwI5q7HwA?start=379"" style=""position: absolute; width: 100%; height: 100%; top: 0; left: 0;"" frameborder=""0"" allow=""autoplay; encrypted-media"" allowfullscreen=""""></iframe></div></div></figure><p><i><strong>Bitcoin Ordinals have changed the Bitcoin network’s status quo - Bitcoin can now be used for more than simple peer-to-peer transfers, and there’s a large community behind this movement.</strong></i></p><p>The novelty of ordinals-enabled use cases in the Bitcoin blockchain has led to unprecedented network activity. Earlier this year, interest in ordinals propelled <a href=""/education/complete-guide-to-crypto-network-fees/"">Transaction fees</a> in the network to a two-year high. Over 15 million ordinals have been minted to date, with their growth being the unquestionable highlight in the Bitcoin Network this year. So far, the primary uses of ordinals are <a href=""/education/non-fungible-tokens-nft/"">non-fungible tokens</a> (NFTs) and memecoins that use the new <a href=""https://www.brc-20.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">BRC-20 token</a> standard for semi-fungible tokens in Bitcoin.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_d844ba8054.png"" alt=""Ordinals Wizards Meme"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_d844ba8054.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_d844ba8054.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_d844ba8054.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_d844ba8054.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Source: </i><a href=""https://twitter.com/udiWertheimer/status/1660829752427687937?s=20"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>Twitter/udiWertheimer</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>While the surge in activity may have been a momentary craze and current use cases may be shallow, we shouldn’t judge ordinals by its current cover of questionable “artworks” and memecoins – the underlying idea is quite powerful.</p><p>Ordinals are fully on-chain and inherit the security characteristics of Bitcoin itself. They have enabled the most immutable network in the world to secure more than just digital money. Existing ordinals could be the canary in the coal mine for what may be coming, a world where we leverage Bitcoin for ownership of digital items with next-level data immutability characteristics. Think of things like deeds, legal contracts, land title ownerships, basically, anything “real-world” that could potentially be digitized and secured/verifiable on the Bitcoin blockchain.</p><p>This article will explain what Bitcoin ordinals are, how they have emerged from seemingly nothing, how they work and differ from Ethereum NFTs, the new use cases they may unlock, how they might benefit Bitcoin’s security, and what the future of ordinals might hold.</p><p><a href=""/deals/wallet/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg"" alt=""Crypto-Wallets-Design Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Crypto_Wallets_Design_V2_4028807bbc.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>What are Bitcoin Ordinals?</h2><p>There appears to be confusion around the terminology used surrounding ordinals. This is because the community is using the terms ordinals, inscriptions, and Bitcoin NFTs interchangeably, while there are distinctions between the three.</p><h3>What is an Ordinal?</h3><p>The traditional definition of an Ordinal originates from “<a href=""https://trustmachines.co/glossary/ordinal-theory/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ordinal Theory,</a>” a methodology where individual satoshis can be labelled and tracked. So, the most traditional definition of an ordinal is a singular individual satoshi that can be identified thanks to a numbering scheme.</p><h3>What is a Satoshi?</h3><p>Named after Bitcoin’s pseudonymous creator <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Satoshi_Nakamoto"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Satoshi Nakamoto</a>, a satoshi (sat for short) is the very smallest unit of denomination of a Bitcoin, with every Bitcoin consisting of 100 million satoshis (sats). Sats make up a Bitcoin in a similar way that cents make up a dollar.</p><h3>What is an Inscription?</h3><p>An inscription is general arbitrary data and metadata posted to a Bitcoin transaction. The metadata are instructions on how to read said data, whether it is an image, text, audio, or other.</p><p>Inscriptions themselves are nothing new. Since the Segregated Witness (SegWit) upgrade (BIP 141) to the Bitcoin Network in 2017, they have existed independently.&nbsp;</p><h3>What are Bitcoin NFTs?</h3><p>The marriage of the ideas behind ordinals and Inscriptions enables Bitcoin NFTs. An inscription is “bound” to an Ordinal, creating a sat with unique data attached, effectively creating an NFT.</p><p>Now that the distinction between the terms has been made, we note that seeing both Bitcoin NFTs, inscriptions, or simply ordinals to refer to Bitcoin NFTs may be expected. I believe the term ordinals will be the one to stick, given that it is the catchiest of the three and seems to have already been adopted by the community. Therefore, this article will refer to the idea of Bitcoin NFTs as ordinals.</p><h2>The difference between Bitcoin Ordinals and Ethereum NFTs</h2><p>In practice, ordinals and <a href=""/education/fundamental-analysis-of-nfts/"">Ethereum NFTs</a> work similarly. They represent unique digital assets with associated data. However, the two have vital technological differences, as highlighted in the table below.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_694719f27c.png"" alt=""Bitcoin and Ethereum NFTs compared"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_694719f27c.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_694719f27c.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_694719f27c.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_694719f27c.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>The tech differences between ordinals and Ethereum NFTs. Source: </i><a href=""https://www.galaxy.com/research/whitepapers/bitcoin-ordinals-inscriptions-5-billion-nft-market/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>Galaxy Research</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>The most critical difference highlighted above is whether the content is on-chain. Unlike traditional NFTs that utilize smart contracts and store the data in external systems, Ordinal NFT data is stored on the Bitcoin blockchain. Fully on-chain content makes ordinals immutable. In contrast, Ethereum NFT data can sometimes be altered.</p><p>An additional essential difference not included above is that minting an ordinal is significantly more expensive than minting an NFT on Ethereum. At the average 2022 fee rate of 3 sats/vByte, inscribing a single Bored Ape NFT would cost 298,620 sats, which at the current Bitcoin price of around $30,000 per BTC equates to $89.59. This means the cost to mint the 10,000-unit BAYC collection would be close to $1 million. The high costs associated with ordinals are one of the reasons why most NFTs are simple pixelated artworks, as the minting fees vary proportionately with the size of the files being inscribed.</p><p>The features of higher costs and immutability make ordinals suited for differentiated use cases compared to Ethereum NFTs.</p><h2>Digital Artifacts</h2><p>Bitcoin Ordinal's properties make them perfect digital artifacts. What is a digital artifact? They are akin to physical artifacts, holding unique value in the digital sphere. They possess vital attributes: clear ownership, completeness, permissionless functionality, uncensorability, and immutability. Due to their intrinsic properties, Bitcoin ordinals perfectly embody these principles, thus standing as ideal digital artifacts.</p><p>Every Bitcoin Ordinal has a distinct owner, just like a rare physical artifact, differentiating it from unowned data. This explicit ownership lends significant value to these ordinals, heightening their appeal in the digital realm.</p><p>The attribute of completeness is crucial. Unlike some non-fungible tokens (NFTs) dependent on off-chain content, Bitcoin ordinals are complete entities within the blockchain itself. They carry all necessary information within the inscription, ensuring they are self-contained and not reliant on external data sources like Arweave or IPFS.</p><p>Permissionless operation is another cornerstone of digital artifacts. Bitcoin ordinals can be transferred freely without constraints such as royalty payments.</p><p>Finally, Bitcoin ordinals inherit the Bitcoin blockchain's immutability and censorship-resistant properties. They are resistant to change and censorship, offering a robust and unalterable record of existence. In this sense, they encapsulate the core principles of digital artifacts, preserving their integrity in the digital realm.</p><h2>The History of Ordinal NFTs</h2><p>Ordinals were made economically viable thanks to Bitcoin’s most recent major upgrade, <a href=""https://github.com/bitcoin/bips/blob/master/bip-0341.mediawiki"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Taproot (BIP 431),</a> activated in November 2021. Combined with the 2017 SegWit upgrade, it made it possible to wrap data cheaply into a taproot script stored in a transaction's witness data section.</p><p>But blockchain updates generally only lay the groundwork for new-use cases. For them to be made accessible, additional work from the community is required. Bitcoin ordinals reaching the mainstream only happened in December 2022, when Casey Rodarmor, a Bitcoin developer, released the <a href=""https://github.com/casey/ord"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">ordinals protocol software</a>. The software runs on a Bitcoin full node on top of the Bitcoin core software, enabling minting and trading ordinals.</p><h2>Ordinals Have Been a Hit, With Bitcoin Transaction Fees Surging</h2><p>Once the Bitcoin ordinals protocol emerged, the idea of NFTs on the Bitcoin blockchain quickly caught the crypto community's attention. Since they came into the spotlight in January 2023, the growth of ordinals has been staggering. Over 15 million Bitcoin Ordinals have been created, and no signs of significant slowdowns exist.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_91b1c995f3.png"" alt=""Ordinal Inscriptions Dune"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_91b1c995f3.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_91b1c995f3.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_91b1c995f3.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_91b1c995f3.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>A look at daily and total ordinals created. Source: </i><a href=""https://dune.com/dgtl_assets/bitcoin-ordinals-analysis"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>@dgtl_assets Dune Analytics Dashboard</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>As a result, Bitcoin block space demand has also surged. Today, daily network fees are a steady 2-3 times higher than throughout 2022. At one point this last May, transaction fees even spiked to levels not seen since the top of the 2017 bull run after a Bitcoin NFT and meme-coin craze. During those days of fever, ordinals' interest and daily inscriptions soared, causing the Bitcoin network to become crowded with transactions.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_4ca1a63642.png"" alt=""Bitcoin Transaction Fees"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_4ca1a63642.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_4ca1a63642.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_4ca1a63642.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_4ca1a63642.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Total daily transaction fees in Bitcoin. Source: </i><a href=""https://studio.glassnode.com/metrics?a=BTC&amp;category=Fees&amp;m=fees.VolumeSum"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>Glassnode</i></a></figcaption></figure><h2>Bitcoin Miners are Set to Benefit from the Ordinals Protocol.</h2><p>Ordinal inscription transactions offer substantial benefits for Bitcoin miners. The higher transaction fees illustrated in the previous section are the most apparent benefit. As a result, since the ordinals protocol emerged, the amount of BTC in blocks originating from transactions is substantially higher.</p><p>For instance, in June 2023, 46.5 BTC per day coming for transactions were mined on average, almost 3x the amount in June 2022. The figures in May are even more pronounced. Fees now constitute a much higher % of the total BTC available per block, as shown in the chart below.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_2c0040c4a4.png"" alt=""Transaction Fees Mined"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_2c0040c4a4.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_2c0040c4a4.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_2c0040c4a4.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Daily Transaction Fee Revenue and the Share of the Total Block Rewards made by Transaction Fees Source: Coinbureau with data from </i><a href=""https://bitcoinvisuals.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>Bitcoin Visuals</i></a></figcaption></figure><p>The second way ordinals benefit miners is by offering more consistent, more valuable blocks. This is because users minting ordinals can be buyers of blockspace when blocks are not whole. This can happen as inscribers can wait until average fee rates drop to finalize their transactions, as creating ordinals may not be as time-sensitive as financial transactions. If we see this pattern of behavior, blocks are likely to be full more consistently, thereby increasing the BTC per block floor.</p><h2>How Do Ordinals Impact the Security of the Bitcoin Network?</h2><p>The Bitcoin halving happening every 210,000 blocks, roughly every four years, is perceived positively. Traditionally, bitcoin’s price has rallied following a halving, and by more than a factor of 2. This is important because, for every halving, Bitcoin’s security budget also drops by around 50%, meaning a price increase of 2x or more is needed to ensure that the security budget of the network doesn’t fall.</p><p>However, the price of BTC increasing by a factor of 2 or more is not guaranteed, and with each halving, whether sooner or later, block rewards will be inevitably small given the math behind BTC supply. To ensure a healthy security budget, it is therefore critical that miners accrue a substantial amount of transaction fees.</p><p>Here is where ordinals could play a significant part. Ordinal fees can increase the profitability for miners and thus contribute positively to Bitcoin's security budget. Overall, Ordinal’s impact on miners and Bitcoin's long-term security model appears to be largely positive.</p><p><i><strong>We have seen the first signs of block reward independence, shedding some light on a future where the Bitcoin security budget is less likely to be compromised.</strong></i></p><h2>How to Buy, Sell, and Trade Ordinals</h2><p>The ordinals protocol uses the Bitcoin Taproot update; therefore, a taproot-compatible wallet with a taproot address is required. A wallet with “coin control” capabilities that prevent spending inscribed ordinal satoshis is also needed.</p><p>Note that many popular wallets may not be compatible due to these requirements. This is because many wallets may only support taproot or see all sats as the same, with ordinal inscription distinctions.</p><p>Popular taproot-compatible wallets are the <a href=""https://ordinalswallet.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ordinals Wallet</a>, <a href=""https://www.xverse.app/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Xverse</a>, and <a href=""https://unisat.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Unisat</a>. The typical user journey involved in buying Bitcoin ordinals is similar to purchasing non-Bitcoin NFTs, which is as follows:</p><ol style=""list-style-type:decimal;""><li>Create an ordinals wallet. This can be done through the webpage of one of the wallets mentioned.</li><li>Take a backup of the recovery phrase for the wallet.</li><li>Set up a password to access the wallet.</li><li>Send some sats to the wallet using the address or buy some bitcoin via built-in onramp services.</li><li>Go to an ordinals marketplace such as <a href=""http://gamma.io"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">gamma.io</a></li><li>Find your favorite ordinal.</li><li>Buy the ordinal using the sats in the wallet.</li></ol><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/image_d4477a3ec6.png"" alt=""image.png"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_image_d4477a3ec6.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_image_d4477a3ec6.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_image_d4477a3ec6.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_image_d4477a3ec6.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Bitcoin ordinals marketplace Gamma. Source: </i><a href=""http://Gamma.io"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><i>Gamma.io</i></a><i>&nbsp;</i></figcaption></figure><p>As a nascent technology, the tools around Bitcoin ordinals are still at a very early stage. With more users drawn to ordinals, the ecosystem, and the tooling will mature to provide a more intuitive user experience.</p><h2>How to Create Bitcoin Ordinals</h2><p>Until recently, the only way to create ordinals was with a fully synced Bitcoin node, which can be costly and requires a technically competent user. Now inscription services like Gamma and Ordinals Bot provide more user-friendly ways to inscribe Bitcoin ordinals suited for non-technical users.</p><p>1. Create an ordinals wallet. This can be done through the webpage of one of the wallets mentioned. Follow steps 1-4 above.</p><p>2. Connect to an inscription service like <a href=""http://Gamma.io"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Gamma.io</a> or <a href=""https://ordinalsbot.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ordinalsbot</a></p><p>3. Select the type of file to inscribe. You can choose between an image, text, BRC-20 tokens, and even .sats, a name service similar to ENS. Remember that the file size will affect the transaction cost, anyone can view the file, and it cannot be changed or deleted.</p><p>4. Enter the taproot-compatible wallet address where you wish to receive the NFT.</p><p>5. Choose your transaction fee. The higher the payment, the more likely it will be that the ordinal will be created sooner. However, keep in mind that the time it will take to make an ordinal will depend on Bitcoin's network congestion, and it is not guaranteed that a high fee will mine the NFT sooner than a lower fee at a time of lower congestion.</p><p>6. Inscribe the Ordinal NFT by sending the BTC requested. You’ll need to own some BTC to pay the transaction.</p><p>Once the transaction is confirmed, you'll get a link to see your inscription on the <a href=""https://ordinals.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">ordinals explorer</a> and transaction data details.&nbsp;</p><h2>What is Next for Ordinals?</h2><p>Bitcoin Ordinals are in their nascent stage, with continuous enhancements to the technology and associated tools. The earliest developments were driven by a need to rectify some issues, but more recently, enhancements focused on performance and user-friendliness.</p><h3>The Cursed Ordinals Issue.</h3><p>The term ""cursed inscriptions"" pertains to ordinals rendered invalid due to incorrect usage or intentional misuse of opcodes. These ""cursed"" entities could not be recognized or traded, limiting their usability within the ordinal's ecosystem. However, a new upgrade to the ordinals protocol, version 0.6.0, has started to address this issue by indexing these previously unrecognized Bitcoin ordinals.</p><p>The solution proposed by ordinals creator Casey Rodarmor involved transforming these cursed inscriptions into ""blessed"" ones. This transformation consists in introducing support for a subset of the different types of cursed ordinals, achieved by setting a block activation height at which specific types of previously invalid inscriptions would start being indexed as regular, valid ordinals. This transformation would solve some pain points around the 70,000 affected ordinals.</p><h3>Ordinals Recursive Inscriptions</h3><p>More recently, on the 4th of July, Bitcoin ordinals entered a new era with the introduction of the <a href=""https://www.theblock.co/post/237658/bitcoin-ordinals-brc-69"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">BRC-69 standard</a>. This game-changing development reduces the cost of Bitcoin ordinals by 90% and removes the existing data limit, previously constrained by Bitcoin’s block size of 4 Mb.&nbsp;</p><p>This innovation is based on ""recursive inscriptions,"" a process that allows inscriptions to request data from existing ones. This can be used in many ways. For instance, rather than inscribing 10,000 JPEG files for, let's say, the BAYC collection, which would be expensive, as we saw earlier, you could use recursive inscriptions to make everything more lightweight. It could be possible to inscribe the 200 traits from the collection and then make 10,000 low-memory inscriptions to request traits and programmatically render the image, resulting in significant cost savings.&nbsp;</p><p>The use cases are not limited to images, there have already been text and audio files also inscribed. Bitcoin is getting a more advanced file system, meaning that building more complex and elaborate systems will make pushing the innovation frontier even more attainable.</p><p><a href=""https://t.me/cbinsider"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg"" alt=""Telegram Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Telegram_inline_fe7d5fe2dc.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2>Ordinals Have Changed The Ethos of the Bitcoin Blockchain</h2><p>What was traditionally a blockchain for peer-to-peer financial transactions is now evolving into a network that can do more, and Ordinals are the technology behind this movement. Many felt like Bitcoin was falling behind in blockchain innovation and relying too much on its previously-held narratives such as being a store of value, <a href=""/analysis/bitcoin-vs-gold-inflation-hedge/"">inflation hedge</a>, and peer-to-peer payment system, but now the tides are changing. Recently, <a href=""https://twitter.com/udiWertheimer/status/1678049715194150913?s=20"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Vitalik Buterin spoke positively</a> about the impact of ordinals on Bitcoin's future, stating:</p><blockquote><p>“I definitely see signs of hope now that we have ordinals bringing back a culture of doing things. It feels like there’s an organic return to builder culture"" (<a href=""https://twitter.com/udiWertheimer/status/1678049715194150913?s=20"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Source</a>)</p></blockquote><p>With a halving in sight, a potential US spot ETF approval, and ordinals to drive innovation, Bitcoin is set to have some action-packed months ahead.</p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Education/how-to-read-a-crypto-chart/,How to Read a Crypto Chart: Master Guide to Crypto Analysis,Education,https://www.coinbureau.com/Guides/how-to-sign-up-on-okx/,How to Signup on OKX: Step-by-Step Guide,Guides,"<p>If you want to know how to sign up for OKX, this article is your step-by-step guide to registering with the innovative cryptocurrency exchange.&nbsp;</p><p>Whether you are an experienced crypto trader or a <a href=""/trading/basics-of-crypto-trading/"">crypto beginner</a>, we understand you want all your assets to have good protection, and have access to reliable cryptocurrency management services.</p><p>The crypto industry has hundreds of crypto exchanges, but they don't all provide secure or reputable services. interviewer's question about Binance's HQ location was:&nbsp;</p><blockquote><p>""<i>Well, I think what this is is the beauty of the blockchain, right, so you don't have to … like where's the Bitcoin office, because Bitcoin doesn't have an office. Wherever I sit is going to be the Binance office. Wherever I need somebody is going to be the Binance office</i>."" (Source: <a href=""https://www.coindesk.com/markets/2020/05/08/binance-doesnt-have-a-headquarters-because-bitcoin-doesnt-says-ceo/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coindesk</a>)</p></blockquote><p>Though the lack of transparency could be a concern, overall, we're considering how Binance secures digital assets for its customers. For that information, the headquarters location is not a significant factor.&nbsp;</p><p>While trying to find Binance's headquarters is like playing a game of Whack-A-Mole, you may find it helpful to note that Binance has offices in cities like Bahrain, Dubai, and Paris, and will soon announce the location of a single global holding. Binance has also registered its legal entity in Italy and has plans to expand its local team in the area. According to <a href=""https://craft.co/binance/locations"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Craft.co</a>, Binance's corporate headquarters is located in the Cayman Islands, with additional strategic locations in Vilnius, Lithuania, and Malta.</p><p>In the next section, we explore the key features and learn more about the Binance platform.</p><p>This article focuses on whether Binance is safe and secure. If you want to learn more about the products, features, and functions Binance offers crypto traders and enthusiasts, you can read our in-depth <a href=""/review/binance"">review of Binance</a> to find out more about the platform.&nbsp; &nbsp;</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/shutterstock_1139475203_a9c557a9ca.jpg"" alt=""shutterstock_1139475203.jpg"" Shutterstock</figcaption></figure><p>We also have in-depth articles and guides covering various aspects of the Binance Exchange that you may find interesting:</p><ul><li><a
