The title of the Bitcoin white paper called it a “Peer-to-peer Electronic Cash system."" Ironically, it is ill equipped to fulfil the narrative of becoming a global payment network, at least, not until the Bitcoin Lightning Network becomes more widely adopted.</p><p>Despite the top-notch security and limited token supply that drives the value of Bitcoin, the network’s transaction processing speed leaves much to be desired, moving at a paltry 7 transactions per second.</p><p><a href=""/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a>, its second closest competitor in terms of market cap fared slightly better with 13 transactions per second. However, blockchains known as Layer-2s or sidechains like <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/polygon-2023-beginners-guide-to-matic/""><strong>Polygon</strong></a>, have taken on the burden of processing transactions on behalf of Ethereum. These alternative solutions greatly speeded up the processing speed, with theoretical outputs in the tens of thousands per second, rivalling Visa and Mastercard.</p><p>No such layer existed for Bitcoin until the Lightning network came about in 2015. Due to the fast processing speed and low transaction fees, the popularity of the project increased. One thing that brought the project to the forefront is the development of Lightning Network wallets. In this article, we are going to look at the 8 Best Bitcoin Lightning Wallets.</p><p>Don't forget to check our top picks for <a href=""/analysis/best-hardware-wallets/"">hardware</a>, <a href=""/review/best-crypto-desktop-wallets/"">desktop</a> and <a href=""/review/top-mobile-wallets/"">mobile wallets</a>.</p><p>If you are looking for an exchange that supports the Lightning Network for fast, cheap payments, OKX is our top pick. OKX is renowned for being one of the most secure exchanges with the lowest fees and a massive selection of altcoins and crypto products. You can find out more in our <a href=""/review/okx/"">OKX Review</a>.</p><p>New signups can also enjoy up to <a href=""/deals/trading/okx/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener nofollow"">40% off trading fees</a> for life!</p><p><a href=""/deals/trading/okx/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener nofollow""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg"" alt=""OKX Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_OKX_Inline_4c6ce0ceba.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2><strong>Best Bitcoin Lightning Wallets: Summary</strong></h2><h3><strong>Key Features of These Wallets Are:</strong></h3><p><strong>Nodes</strong> – A Lightning node is required to perform transactions on the Lightning network. It has two responsibilities: monitor the Bitcoin network to ensure the funds’ safety, and perform transactions by communicating with other nodes. It keeps tabs on which channel has how much so that there will be enough to make a payment when the need arises.</p><p><strong>Channels </strong>– Channels are how two parties pay each other. Each party opens a channel on a node by depositing some BTC in it. Think of a channel like the sender and receiver. They need to know who is on the other end making and receiving the payment. How the payment is made is the node’s business. It can be a direct payment between two nodes, or it could involve multiple nodes along the way.</p><p>Both the opening and closing of channels are recorded on the Bitcoin network. What happens in the time period between these two actions though is none of Bitcoin’s business.</p><p><strong>Invoices</strong> – It is a request for payment on the Lightning network. The invoice is identified with a long string of alphanumeric characters which contains all the necessary information required. These include:</p><ul><li>Payment amount</li><li>Expiration time</li><li>Invoice ID with timestamp</li><li>Invoice description</li><li>Backup bitcoin address</li><li>Payment routes</li></ul><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/What_a_Lightning_Invoice_looks_like_Image_via_medium_com_suredbits_d4c586dd7b.png"" alt=""best bitcoin lightning wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_What_a_Lightning_Invoice_looks_like_Image_via_medium_com_suredbits_d4c586dd7b.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_What_a_Lightning_Invoice_looks_like_Image_via_medium_com_suredbits_d4c586dd7b.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_What_a_Lightning_Invoice_looks_like_Image_via_medium_com_suredbits_d4c586dd7b.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>What a Lightning Invoice looks like. Image via medium.com/suredbits</i></figcaption></figure><h2><strong>What Are Lightning Network Wallets?</strong></h2><p>A Lightning Network wallet allows users to make and receive payments via the <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/technology/lightning-network/""><strong>Lightning Network</strong></a>, commonly referred to as Bitcoin’s Layer-2. It enables fast and cheap transactions on Bitcoin through the use of channels and Lightning nodes.</p><p>There are two types of wallets catering to different types of users.</p><h3><strong>Custodial Wallets</strong></h3><p>When you use a custodial wallet, your funds are parked with the custodian. As a result, you will need to trust that they won’t run away with your money or mismanage the business. On the other hand, you do not have the responsibility of safeguarding your own funds. When you want to send a payment, the wallet routes the funds on your behalf and shows you the balance you have with them. However, there’s no way for you to verify if the balance you see is true unless you move your funds to a non-custodial wallet through the Bitcoin network.</p><p>In return for your trust, custodial wallets take care of the node-running and channel management part for the user. All they need to do is follow the simple UI to send and receive funds. All the complicated stuff is handled by the wallet. In some cases, if two customers use the same app to send funds to each other, a channel is not needed as the wallet can shuffle the funds from one party to another using their system. You can also receive BTC via Lightning without having to first provide liquidity to activate the channel.</p><h3><strong>Non-Custodial Wallets</strong></h3><p>Security is solely on the user’s shoulders if they choose to go with a non-custodial wallet. Those who like to have complete control over their funds consider this a blessing as they do not have to trust a third party with their precious BTC.</p><p>Each non-custodial wallet has its own node. Some offer the option for users to connect to their node of choice instead of using the wallet’s node. Aside from that, other related operations such as channel management, including the opening and closing of channels, channel capacity etc can be handled by the non-custodial wallet for those who do not want to muck around. Certain wallets offer advanced users the ability to fiddle with channel-related settings.</p><p>One thing they will have to consider is how much BTC to allocate when opening a channel. This is because there needs to be a minimum amount of sats to keep the channel open, especially if it will be open for an extended period of time, like a running tab at a restaurant or your neighbourhood Quik-E Mart where you only settle the bill once a month.</p><p>If you are going to be using any non-custodial wallets for cryptocurrencies, I recommend checking out our article on <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/""><strong>crypto safety</strong></a> to ensure you are following the best practices to keep your crypto safe!</p><h2><strong>How Do Lightning Wallets Work?</strong></h2><p>It is a well-known fact that Bitcoin has a <a href=""https://ieeexplore.ieee.org/document/8946216"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>scaling problem</strong></a>. This makes it a less-than-ideal choice for a global payment system despite the super-tight security and value-retaining features. It wasn’t until the emergence of the <a href=""https://dci.mit.edu/lightning-network"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Lightning Network</strong></a>, introduced by Thaddeus Dryjo and Joseph Poon in a white paper, that gave Bitcoin a shot at overcoming the issue of scalability.</p><p>The Lightning Network allows Bitcoin micropayments to happen off-chain through nodes and channels, similar to a sidechain for Ethereum. These micropayments are made instantly and save a lot on transaction costs, compared to the main Bitcoin network. Transactions that happen on the Lightning Network are not recorded on the main Bitcoin network except for the opening and closing of channels as these transactions carry the BTC balances needed to keep track of the overall balance. It’s like having a fixed amount for a monthly food budget but you may not track every single penny spent for food.</p><p>A Bitcoin Lightning wallet usually is its own Lightning node where it allows payments to be routed through it to other nodes/destinations. At the same time, it also enables channels to be opened and to be the party initiating the transaction to someone else.</p><p>The job of each Lightning node is to route payments. The compensation they get is the fees set by the node operators. In order to be a successful node operator, a certain amount of capital is required as liquidity. Insufficient liquidity from the nodes means that the payments will fail, and node operators won’t get any compensation.</p><p>To maintain the balance of funds in a node, you want to have almost equal amounts of inbound and outbound payments so that the funds in the node do not get depleted from making too many payments but not enough paid to you. Here is where fees come in.</p><p>There are two types of fees: the ones charged by the network and by the wallet. The amount of fees charged, denominated in sats, may not appear to be a lot in cash terms, but as the price of Bitcoin rises, there would be a significant difference between 120 sats and 12,000 sats. The fees charged include channel management and making a transaction or payment.</p><p>Aside from payments, the wallet also gives the users access to apps or locations where they can use their sats. This encourages more people to consider using Bitcoin for their daily needs.</p><h2><strong>Best Bitcoin Lightning Wallets</strong></h2><p>In the following section, we will introduce a number of wallets, both custodial and non-custodial ones, for your consideration. Bearing in mind that the context is around ease of making payments in everyday situations, the focus is on mobile apps as most of us have accepted using some kind of e-wallet on our phones to pay for things.</p><h3><strong>Wallet of Satoshi</strong></h3><p>The official website of <a href=""https://walletofsatoshi.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Wallet of Satoshi</strong></a> claims that it’s “the world’s simplest Bitcoin Lightning wallet” and it does appear so. This Lightning wallet is the custodial type that is only available on mobile for both Android and iOS users.</p><p>After downloading the app to your phone, you are greeted with a screen with the Send and Receive button, allowing you to instantly send or receive Bitcoin. For the full menu list, select the three lines in the top-right corner. Enter an email address to use the account on multiple devices.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/The_various_layouts_of_the_app_Image_via_Wallet_Of_Satoshi_33d04b03a1.png"" alt=""The various layouts of the app Satoshi Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_The_various_layouts_of_the_app_Image_via_Wallet_Of_Satoshi_33d04b03a1.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_The_various_layouts_of_the_app_Image_via_Wallet_Of_Satoshi_33d04b03a1.png 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>The various layouts of the app. Image via WalletOfSatoshi</i></figcaption></figure><p>The wallet offers three ways to add funds to it: receiving Bitcoin from another wallet via the main Bitcoin network, Lightning Network, and buying Bitcoin directly from them. Moonpay is the partner for buying and selling Bitcoin through the app. Prior to entering your card details, you get an email notification with the verification code through the email address you entered for creating an account. Note that this is subject to the regions supported by Moonpay.</p><p>If you’re at a loss as to where you can spend your Bitcoin, the app links you up with <a href=""https://btcmap.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>btcmap.org&nbsp;</strong></a> which lets you know which vendors or ATMs in your area accept Bitcoin as payment. In terms of security, the app has a biometric setting and the ability to hide your balance.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Menu_and_Setting_options_Image_via_Wallet_of_Satoshi_f290f35c68.png"" alt=""Menu and Setting options Satoshi Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Menu_and_Setting_options_Image_via_Wallet_of_Satoshi_f290f35c68.png 190w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Menu_and_Setting_options_Image_via_Wallet_of_Satoshi_f290f35c68.png 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Menu and Setting options. Image via Wallet of Satoshi</i></figcaption></figure><p>Overall, the clean and simple interface presents an inviting allure to use the app, giving users the confidence to try it out.</p><h3><strong>Electrum</strong></h3><p><a href=""https://electrum.org/#home"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Electrum</strong></a> is a non-custodial Bitcoin wallet designed specifically to store Bitcoin only. It’s been around since 2011 and is used by many of the Bitcoin OGs. Security is one of the great features of the wallet because it has a watching-only wallet function for tracking transactions, multisig abilities, and supports hardware wallets that were introduced by Guy in his <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/videos/top-5-best-hardware-wallets-which-are-the-safest/""><strong>Top 5 Hardware Wallets</strong></a> video. The wallet features both a desktop and mobile version (but only for Android), making it handy for mobile users to make payments to merchants.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Configure_Electrum_for_Lightning_Payments_Image_via_Electrum_Google_Playstore_82578a5d10.png"" alt=""Configure Electrum for Lightning Payments"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Configure_Electrum_for_Lightning_Payments_Image_via_Electrum_Google_Playstore_82578a5d10.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Configure_Electrum_for_Lightning_Payments_Image_via_Electrum_Google_Playstore_82578a5d10.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Configure_Electrum_for_Lightning_Payments_Image_via_Electrum_Google_Playstore_82578a5d10.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Configure Electrum for Lightning Payments. Image via Electrum Google Playstore</i></figcaption></figure><p>Electrum is also the oldest wallet to adopt Lightning network payments since they announced their support in 2020. The wallet itself is open-source and free to download. However, it is not a wallet for newbies as there are many options to configure the wallet to do a lot of things. However, it is great for those who want as complete control as possible over their wallet setup.</p><h3><strong>Breez Mobile</strong></h3><p>Breez Mobile is a non-custodial open-source wallet available in iOS and Android for Lightning payments. By using Breez, you are essentially running your own Lightning node on your mobile. You will also need to open a channel with Breez and have a minimum of around 600 sats in your balance to keep this wallet active.</p><p>To add funds to the wallet, you can make a BTC deposit from another address, buy Bitcoin, or use a FastBitcoins voucher. Note that both the actions of adding and removing funds involve interacting with the main Bitcoin network.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Breez_Mobile_Wallet_1024x545_e201a5712f.png"" alt=""Breez Mobile Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Breez_Mobile_Wallet_1024x545_e201a5712f.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Breez_Mobile_Wallet_1024x545_e201a5712f.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Breez_Mobile_Wallet_1024x545_e201a5712f.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Breez_Mobile_Wallet_1024x545_e201a5712f.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Use Breez for P2P payments, accept BTC for services, or support your favorite podcaster. Image via Breez Google Playstore</i></figcaption></figure><p>The wallet can be backed up to a cloud storage such as Google Drive so it’s not great for anonymity or if you want to divest yourself from the clutches of a big tech company. For extra protection, add a 12-word phrase during the backup process. That being said, it also lets you restore your wallet using your Google account. Note that the wallet is still in Beta mode so please use at your own risk.</p><p>What makes Breez interesting is that it’s not just a mobile wallet. It can also double as a Point-of-Sale app for merchants who want to accept Bitcoin for their products and services. In addition, you can also listen to podcasts on the app and support your favorite podcasters by paying them in sats. This is possible by giving them a “boost” with a one-time payment or entering an amount for Sats/minute, basically, pay as you listen.</p><h3><strong>Zap Wallet</strong></h3><p><a href=""https://zaphq.io/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Zap wallet</strong></a> is the brainchild of <a href=""https://twitter.com/jackmallers"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Jack Mallers</strong></a>, known for the Strike app, a payment network for merchants used by Shopify. He was one of the first to publicly preach the gospel of the Lightning Network to the masses. The non-custodial wallet, in both desktop (MacOS, Windows, Linux!) and mobile versions, is more suited for medium to advanced users. Some setup is required to get the wallet up and running. Jack has made <a href=""https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=Z2XDt7iKE7A&amp;list=PLMj6UA3-f3cQq_TjCXAAeP1mmRnjgnDrI"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>some YouTube tutorials</strong></a> on this topic and a few more. Note that the mobile versions do not contain a Lightning node and require a separate node to use it.</p><p>You can connect the wallet to an existing node prior to opening a channel there. Future features include the ability to run a full Lightning node in one click and use the Tor network to connect, thus maximizing anonymity and security, plus the ability to buy Bitcoin directly from the app.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Zap_Wallet_requires_some_setup_Image_via_Zap_Wallet_Google_Playstore_d6d87d9108.png"" alt=""Zap Wallet requires some setup"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Zap_Wallet_requires_some_setup_Image_via_Zap_Wallet_Google_Playstore_d6d87d9108.png 242w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Zap_Wallet_requires_some_setup_Image_via_Zap_Wallet_Google_Playstore_d6d87d9108.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Zap_Wallet_requires_some_setup_Image_via_Zap_Wallet_Google_Playstore_d6d87d9108.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Zap_Wallet_requires_some_setup_Image_via_Zap_Wallet_Google_Playstore_d6d87d9108.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Zap Wallet requires some setup. Image via Zap Wallet Google Playstore</i></figcaption></figure><h3><strong>Muun Wallet</strong></h3><p>Launched in 2019, Muun Wallet is also a well-known option for a non-custodial Lightning Wallet, especially ever since Jack Dorsey <a href=""https://twitter.com/jack/status/1480673213210193920"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>tweeted about it</strong></a> in 2022. Security is a key concern with any wallet and Muun has taken great measures to keep your funds safe.</p><ul><li>2 for 2 multisig, which means you hold one key for spending, and the other key is held by Muun.</li><li>Emergency Kit that exports your private keys and output descriptors. Both pieces of information combined tells you how to find your funds on the Bitcoin network.</li><li>Choose between a randomly-generated code or multi-factor authentication as your backup option.</li></ul><figure class=""image""><a href=""https://blog.muun.com/introducingmuun/""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Image_via_Muun_Wallet_blog_32e4109ce8.png"" alt=""Muun Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Image_via_Muun_Wallet_blog_32e4109ce8.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Image_via_Muun_Wallet_blog_32e4109ce8.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Image_via_Muun_Wallet_blog_32e4109ce8.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a><figcaption><i>Image via Muun Wallet blog</i></figcaption></figure><p>Muun Wallet also has some interesting features not found in other wallets. These include:&nbsp;</p><ul><li>Lightning Invoices expiration from 1 hour to 24 hours</li><li>Mempool estimator is a tool to check that you are neither overpaying nor underestimating fees required for the transaction.</li><li><a href=""https://blog.muun.com/a-closer-look-at-submarine-swaps-in-the-lightning-network/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Submarine Swap</strong></a> is a feature that involves making payments via a third party known as a swap provider. In situations where you need to pay someone but you don’t have a direct channel with that person, the funds will then go through a swap provider who helps you pass along the funds to the intended party. The swap provider sends the funds to the recipient first, then claims the same amount from the sender by the revelation of a secret created by the recipient within a certain timeframe.</li></ul><h3><strong>Phoenix wallet</strong></h3><p>ACINQ, one of the teams that contribute to the development of the Lightning network and created the Eclair wallet, has released another product called <a href=""https://phoenix.acinq.co/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Phoenix Wallet</strong></a> while sunsetting the former one.</p><p>Phoenix is a non-custodial mobile native LN wallet for both iOS and Android users. It will handle the opening and closing of channels for you and the wallet itself is a full-fledged Lightning node. A minimum of 10,000 sats is needed to open the channel and “activate” the account.</p><p>The wallet allows for on-the-fly channel creation but there’s a fee involved. This function is recommended to be disabled on the app as it may result in the unnecessary creation of multiple channels when receiving payment amounts that exceed the channel’s balance limit. When this function is disabled, unsuccessful payments will simply fail, thus never leaving the sender’s wallet.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Image_via_Phoenix_Wallet_aa275863e5.png"" alt=""Phoenix Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Image_via_Phoenix_Wallet_aa275863e5.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Image_via_Phoenix_Wallet_aa275863e5.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Image_via_Phoenix_Wallet_aa275863e5.png 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Image via Phoenix Wallet</i></figcaption></figure><h3><strong>Zeus Wallet</strong></h3><p>Rather than a straight-up wallet, the <a href=""https://zeusln.app/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Zeus Wallet</strong></a> app is more of a mobile version of a Lightning node management app that allows for Lightning payments to be made on it. This app does not have its own node and requires the user to connect to an existing node. This alone makes it out of reach for beginners. However, for those who are interested to run their own node, this would be a good app to consider.</p><p>The app is open-sourced and non-custodial, and supports both Lightning and the Bitcoin network itself, with a strong privacy focus through Tor connection and the ability to hide the sending data in Privacy mode.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Zeus_Wallet_1024x498_a869335c87.png"" alt=""Zeus Wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Zeus_Wallet_1024x498_a869335c87.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Zeus_Wallet_1024x498_a869335c87.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Zeus_Wallet_1024x498_a869335c87.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Zeus_Wallet_1024x498_a869335c87.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Secure transactions with Zeus wallet. Image via Zeus</i></figcaption></figure><h3><strong>Bitcoin Beach Wallet (Blink)</strong></h3><p>The <a href=""https://blink.sv/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Bitcoin Beach Wallet</strong></a> was created at El Zonte in El Salvador, the only country in the world that currently accepts Bitcoin as legal tender. The wallet is helping enable El Salvadorians with the ability to make quick and cheap transfers of Bitcoin, dating back to 2020. Unlike Chivo, the official wallet used only by El Salvadoreans, the Bitcoin Beach wallet is available for anyone around the world.</p><p>The app is designed not only for beginners using the Lightning Network but also for onboarding newbies to Bitcoin. It features an Earn and Learn section where users can stack sats by learning about Bitcoin. Other features include:</p><ul><li>Multi-language support</li><li>Multi-currency support</li><li>Stablesats – an open-source project that creates a form of “synthetic USD” through a derivatives trading strategy in the background. The result is that users can receive, send, and hold their funds in a USD equivalent account.</li><li>Localised map showing where one can spend their sats.</li><li>Log in using your phone number.</li><li>Integration with Nostr for tipping</li></ul><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Bitcoin_Beach_Wallet_Blink_1024x562_115cd6fad3.png"" alt=""Bitcoin Beach Wallet (Blink)"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Bitcoin_Beach_Wallet_Blink_1024x562_115cd6fad3.png 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Bitcoin_Beach_Wallet_Blink_1024x562_115cd6fad3.png 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Bitcoin_Beach_Wallet_Blink_1024x562_115cd6fad3.png 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Bitcoin_Beach_Wallet_Blink_1024x562_115cd6fad3.png 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Image via Bitcoin Beach Wallet Google Playstore</i></figcaption></figure><p>The app also has a merchant interface that acts as a Point-of-Sale (POS) system for accepting Bitcoin payments.</p><h2><strong>Lightning Network Development and Adoption Rate</strong></h2><p>Although the idea of having a payment channel has been around for as long as Bitcoin, it wasn’t until the Lightning Network white paper,&nbsp; released in February 2015 by Joseph Poon and Thaddeus Dryja, that the idea really caught on. Central to the white paper is the Hashed Timelock Contract (HTLC), used for payment routing over multiple channels, that gave Lightning Network a meaty feature.</p><p>In August 2015, ACINQ debuted its new implementation of the Lightning Network known as Eclair. Not long after, they unveiled the Android version of their Lightning wallet by the same name. This was quickly followed by <a href=""https://lightning.engineering/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Lightning Labs</strong></a> and <a href=""https://blockstream.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Blockstream</strong></a>. The three companies were the main actors pushing the development of the Lightning protocol.</p><p>From the first purchase of a physical item in January 2018 to today, where there are companies like Bitrefill and Fold App to name a few that offer BTC purchases for daily necessities, adoption is slow but surely growing by the day. As more and more people cotton on to the possibility of using Bitcoin to make payments, the promise of a future where Bitcoin can be accepted alongside cash is coming ever closer.</p><p><a href=""https://www.tiktok.com/@coinbureau?lang=en""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp"" alt=""TikTok inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><h2><strong>8 Best Lightning Wallets: Conclusion</strong></h2><p>A key impetus for me to do this article is because I was recently introduced to <a href=""https://www.bitrefill.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Bitrefill</strong></a> and the possibilities of paying for daily necessities using Bitcoin. I then decided to go on the hunt for a good Lightning wallet to use and share my findings with you. It’s clear to me that mobile apps are the way to go for maximum convenience.</p><p>Depending on how adventurous I am (or you are), I may consider running my own Lightning node in the future. For now though, I’m happy to use a custodial wallet as the quickest and easiest way to dip my toes in. While there is a risk of funds’ safety with a custodial wallet, it’s worth pausing a moment to consider: if I only keep 10,000 sats in that wallet, and it’s all gone, that’s a small price to pay, whereas I may benefit greatly from the upside.</p><p>Once you start seeing Bitcoin as a denomination of sorts, it could be a gradual shift to viewing the value of items in sats instead of dollars. Somewhere in there is the germination of a way of seeing the world in a completely different manner.</p><p><strong>Disclaimer: These are the writer’s opinions and should not be considered investment advice. Readers should do their own research.</strong></p>"https://www.coinbureau.com/Analysis/is-it-safe-to-keep-crypto-on-coinbase/,Is it Safe to Keep Crypto on Coinbase?,Analysis,"<p>If you’re a crypto beginner, you probably have dozens of questions about how to store your cryptocurrency. For example, is it safe to keep crypto on Coinbase compared to any other crypto platform? Should you use a crypto wallet instead of leaving crypto on an exchange?</p><p>Coinbase is a centralised <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/videos/top-5-best-crypto-exchanges-in-2023-are-they-safe/""><strong>cryptocurrency exchange</strong></a>, meaning it operates on a centralised infrastructure run by a single entity, unlike decentralised exchanges, which use a peer-to-peer network without intermediaries.</p><p>As a centralised exchange, Coinbase provides a user-friendly interface for buying, selling, and trading over 240 listed cryptocurrencies. The platform offers security features such as two-factor (2FA), biometric authentication, and insurance protection to help protect users’ accounts and funds.</p><p>This post explores Coinbase as a centralised exchange. You will discover whether you can trust the platform to securely hold your funds, protect critical personal information, and learn the steps to increase security on the Coinbase platform.</p><p><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Trezor_Inline_jpg_a6f083e538.webp"" alt=""Trezor Inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Trezor_Inline_jpg_a6f083e538.webp 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Trezor_Inline_jpg_a6f083e538.webp 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Trezor_Inline_jpg_a6f083e538.webp 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></p><h2><strong>What is Coinbase?</strong></h2><p>Founded by Brian Armstrong and Fred Ehrsam in 2012, Coinbase is a reputable, established crypto exchange that enables users to trade, invest and exchange more than 240 different cryptocurrencies like Bitcoin (BTC), <a href=""https://ethereum.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Ethereum (ETH),</strong></a> and <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/videos/dogecoin-is-the-hype-real-this-you-need-to-know/""><strong>Dogecoin (DOGE)</strong></a>.</p><p>Coinbase has over 108 million users. From 2021 to 2022, Coinbase attracted 56 million new users because of its popularity as a trusted exchange with a beginner-friendly interface. The platform caters to <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/cryptocurrency-beginners-guide/""><strong>novice</strong></a> and experienced crypto traders and investors.</p><p>It’s important to note that cryptocurrencies are a relatively new asset class that can be volatile and risky and may not be suitable for all investors.</p><p>Coinbase has excellent security measures to ensure its users’ funds are safe. However, we recommend moving your crypto assets off any exchange into a <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/how-do-hardware-wallets-work/""><strong>self-custodial hardware wallet</strong></a>.</p><p>For new users looking to make simple buy and sell orders, the original Coinbase platform is likely the best option. In November 2022, Coinbase began migrating more advanced accounts on their Coinbase Pro platform to a new, more sophisticated platform called “Advanced Trade.”</p><p>To find out more about Coinbase, read our <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/review/coinbase-pro/""><strong>in-depth, unbiased Coinbase review</strong></a>.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/coinbase23_4_23_20fb219553.jpg"" alt=""coinbase wallet"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_coinbase23_4_23_20fb219553.jpg 156w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_coinbase23_4_23_20fb219553.jpg 500w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Coinbase is a Trusted Cryptocurrency Exchange (Image source: Coinbase)</i></figcaption></figure><h3><strong>Is Coinbase a Good Exchange?</strong></h3><p>Coinbase has an excellent reputation, and its loyal users consider it one of the best. Naturally, every cryptocurrency exchange has pros and cons, as the following information shows regarding Coinbase: –</p><p><strong>Pros:</strong></p><ul><li><strong>User-friendly for beginners:</strong> Coinbase’s website and mobile app are easy to navigate and allow for quick buying, selling, and exchanging of cryptocurrencies.</li><li><strong>Large selection of cryptocurrencies:</strong> Coinbase offers over 240 cryptocurrencies, with new cryptos added regularly.</li><li><strong>Earning opportunities:</strong> Users can earn interest on eligible balances and participate in Coinbase Learning Rewards by completing crypto education courses.</li></ul><p><strong>Cons:</strong></p><ul><li><strong>High transaction fees:</strong> Coinbase’s main platform transaction fees are often expensive.</li><li><strong>Customer service issues:</strong> Coinbase has received negative feedback regarding their customer service, especially regarding security issues.</li><li><strong>Coinbase controls private keys:</strong> On the primary platform, Coinbase holds and controls users’ private keys, which represent ownership of their cryptocurrency. Only with the Coinbase Wallet can users have responsibility for their private keys.</li></ul><p>The cons of Coinbase, to be fair, are comparable with most cryptocurrency exchanges. If you’re <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/cryptocurrency-beginners-guide/""><strong>new to the cryptocurrency</strong></a> market, you may wonder if using Coinbase for your cryptocurrencies is safe.</p><h2><strong>Is Coinbase Safe to Use for Cryptocurrencies?</strong></h2><p>Coinbase takes user account protection seriously, but you must take essential steps to protect your account. <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/review/forta-fort/""><strong>Cybercrime</strong></a> is increasing, and hackers are becoming more adept at applying sophisticated protocols to identify vulnerabilities on exchange platforms.</p><p>You’ve worked hard to build your cryptocurrency assets, so take responsibility for their security.</p><h3><strong>Should You Keep Your Cryptocurrency on Coinbase?</strong></h3><p>It’s important to note that while Coinbase and other cryptocurrency platforms implement security measures, by the nature of a cryptocurrency exchange, they are all centralised entities. Therefore, the risk of a hack or cybercrime exists.</p><p>Let’s explore how to get started if you intend to store your cryptocurrency on Coinbase.</p><h2><strong>How to Store Your Cryptocurrency Safely on Coinbase</strong></h2><p>To protect your crypto assets, we advise best practices on Coinbase and other crypto exchanges, such as enabling two-factor authentication and a super strong password.</p><p>Only have your crypto assets live on Coinbase when you are actively trading. Once your session completes, transfer your cryptocurrencies to your self-custody wallet.</p><h3><strong>Security Features of Coinbase</strong></h3><p>Coinbase has implemented several robust security features to protect its users’ accounts and funds.</p><p><strong>Some of the key security features on Coinbase include:</strong></p><ul><li><strong>Two-factor authentication:</strong> Coinbase users enable two-factor authentication (2FA), which requires a second verification step, such as a text message or an authentication app, before they can access their account.</li><li><strong>Biometric Authentication:</strong> Coinbase enables user biometric authentication on its mobile app, such as fingerprint or face recognition.</li><li><strong>SSL Encryption: </strong>Coinbase uses SSL (Secure Sockets Layer) encryption to secure all website traffic between the browser and web server. It protects users’ sensitive information by scrambling data, so it isn’t easy for hackers to intercept.</li><li><strong>Offline Storage:</strong> Most users’ funds on Coinbase are held in offline storage, also known as cold storage, to protect against potential hacking attacks.</li><li><strong>Insurance Protection</strong>: Coinbase has insurance protection for all eligible cryptocurrency holdings, including digital currency in the Coinbase Vault (<i>see below</i>), to protect against theft and hacking.</li><li><strong>Account Activity Monitoring:</strong> Coinbase monitors account activity for suspicious behaviour and alerts users if any unusual activity is detected.</li><li><strong>Whitelisting:</strong> Users can set up a whitelist of approved addresses to ensure that withdrawals get sent to trusted addresses.</li></ul><p>As you can see, Coinbase has an excellent range of security features, and we would advise using as many of them as possible. Coinbase Vault is a popular cold storage feature to protect your digital assets, which we will cover below.</p><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/coinbasewallet_768x416_d41697d16f.jpg"" alt=""coinbasewallet-768x416.jpg"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_coinbasewallet_768x416_d41697d16f.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_coinbasewallet_768x416_d41697d16f.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_coinbasewallet_768x416_d41697d16f.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>The Coinbase Wallet has Many Security Features (Image source: Coinbase)</i></figcaption></figure><h3><strong>Coinbase Vault</strong></h3><p>Coinbase Vault is a helpful feature offered by Coinbase for users to store their cryptocurrency, such as <a href=""https://bitcoin.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Bitcoin (BTC</strong></a>) in a secure offline location called cold storage (offline storage). It’s an additional security layer that helps protect your assets from potential hacking attacks.</p><p>With Coinbase Vault, users can create multiple sub-accounts with different permission levels, allowing them to give other trusted people access to their funds for specific purposes.</p><blockquote><p><i>“Coinbase Wallet supports hundreds of thousands of coins and a whole world of decentralized apps. It’s your crypto – use it how and where you’d like.”</i> (source: Coinbase)</p></blockquote><h2><strong>Storing Crypto Safely</strong></h2><p>Keeping your crypto on an exchange isn’t recommended, regardless of the level of security. No matter the platform’s trustworthiness, we recommend storing your crypto assets in a self-custody wallet.</p><p>If you don’t wish to use Coinbase Vault, the following is a brief list of recommended self-custody wallets: –</p><ul><li><strong>Ledger Nano S:</strong> The Ledger is a popular hardware wallet supporting multiple cryptocurrencies, such as <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/review/optimism-review/""><strong>Ethereum</strong></a> (ETH), Bitcoin (BTC), and <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/videos/litecoin-is-ltc-seriously-underrated-my-take/""><strong>Litecoin</strong></a> (LTC). It offers high-security features like PIN protection, seed backup, and passphrase support.</li><li><strong>Trezor Model T:</strong> A hardware wallet that supports over 1,000 cryptocurrencies, including Bitcoin (BTC), <a href=""https://ethereum.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><strong>Ethereum (ETH),</strong></a> and Ripple (XRP). It has a touch screen, passphrase support, and a strong emphasis on security.</li><li><strong>Exodus:</strong> A desktop and mobile wallet that supports multiple cryptocurrencies, including Bitcoin (BTC), Ethereum (ETH), and Litecoin (LTC). It offers a user-friendly interface and built-in exchange but lacks advanced security features like passphrase support.</li><li><strong>MyEtherWallet:</strong> A web-based wallet that supports Ethereum (ETH) and other ERC-20 tokens. It allows users to generate and manage their private keys and integrates with popular hardware wallets for added security.</li><li><strong>Trust Wallet:</strong> Another popular mobile wallet that supports multiple cryptocurrencies, including Ethereum (ETH), Bitcoin (BTC), and Binance Coin (WBNB). It has a user-friendly interface allowing users to control their private keys but lacks advanced security features like passphrase support.</li></ul><p>By definition, a self-custody wallet means you have responsibility for managing the private keys instead of a centralised entity having control of your digital assets.</p><p>Enable 2FA, use super strong password protection and keep backup copies of your seed phrase in a safe place to protect your funds.</p><p>Read <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/education/crypto-safety-protect-crypto/""><strong>Crypto Safety 101: How to Protect Your Crypto</strong></a> to learn more about protecting your crypto assets.</p><blockquote><p><i>“Store all of your NFTs: Safely store and easily view all of your Ethereum and Polygon NFTs right in your Wallet.”</i> (source: Coinbase)</p></blockquote><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/coinbase23_4_768x560_2004d63437.jpg"" alt=""coinbase for beginners and expert traders"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_coinbase23_4_768x560_2004d63437.jpg 214w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_coinbase23_4_768x560_2004d63437.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_coinbase23_4_768x560_2004d63437.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption><i>Coinbase is Suitable for Beginners &amp; Experienced Crypro Investors and Traders (Image source: Coinbase)</i></figcaption></figure><h2><strong>Is it Safe to Keep Crypto on Coinbase: Conclusion</strong></h2><p>Coinbase is GDPR compliant and a safe exchange trusted by millions of crypto users. Compared to many other cryptocurrency exchanges, Coinbase is one of the safest as the platform prioritises security to protect user assets.&nbsp;</p><p><a href=""https://www.tiktok.com/@coinbureau?lang=en""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp"" alt=""TikTok inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Tik_Tok_inline_jpg_f2075ed425.webp 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>Coinbase is registered with FinCEN (Financial Crimes Enforcement Network) as a money services business. It has a KYC policy (know your customer: mandatory verification) to prevent fraudulent activity and complies with anti-money laundering (AML) regulations. Even though Coinbase is considered one of the safest exchanges in the industry, most crypto veterans, including us here at the Coin Bureau do not recommend keeping crypto on any exchange for long-term storage and highly encourage self-custody.</p><p>Read our in-depth <a href=""https://www.coinbureau.com/tag/coinbase-review/""><strong>Coinbase review.</strong></a></p><p><i><strong><u>Disclaimer:</u></strong></i> These are the writer’s opinions and should not be considered investment advice. It didn’t take long for AI crypto projects to start garnering their share of the limelight as well.&nbsp;</p><p>Within weeks, YouTube was bursting at the seams with YouTubers telling us how to use prompts, create art on <a href=""https://www.midjourney.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Midjourney</a>, create storybooks and automate our businesses.</p><p>A few months later, though obsessed with AI developments, the public started worrying about AI taking over their jobs. After that, <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/education/what-is-bitcoin/"">Bitcoin</a> swept dramatically into the crypto market, dressed up for a memorable party and suddenly, cryptocurrencies became the focal point for the media and the public.</p><p>Moreover, in 2023, <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/videos/cryptos-killer-use-case-report-you-have-to-see/"">crypto</a> and AI are merging. Wow! Now, that’s exciting. It’s hard to imagine how far it can go, but some crypto AI projects are already gathering speed and investment and changing how we do things forever.</p><p>We could have called this article the top 100 Exciting AI crypto projects, still, for now, we will look at five projects that caught our eye. We aren’t saying they are the best projects because we aim to present unbiased information so you can decide what AI crypto projects you like. However, we think you’ll enjoy this soiree into the AI crypto world and feel as excited as we do about the future of AI crypto.</p><p><a href=""/deals/trading/kucoin/""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/Kucoin_inline_20ba7688af.jpg"" alt=""Kucoin inline"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_Kucoin_inline_20ba7688af.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_Kucoin_inline_20ba7688af.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_Kucoin_inline_20ba7688af.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_Kucoin_inline_20ba7688af.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a></p><p>To that end, let’s look at the first AI crypto project</p><h2>The Graph (GRT)</h2><figure class=""image""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/the_graph_8e15d38619.jpg"" alt=""What Is The Graph"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_the_graph_8e15d38619.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_the_graph_8e15d38619.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_the_graph_8e15d38619.jpg 750w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/large_the_graph_8e15d38619.jpg 1000w,"" sizes=""100vw""><figcaption>Apis For A Vibrant Decentralized Future: Image Source: <a href=""https://thegraph.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">The Graph</a></figcaption></figure><h3>What Is The Graph?</h3><p><a href=""https://thegraph.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">The Graph</a>&nbsp;is an indexing and querying protocol ranked under the top fifty on <a href=""https://coinmarketcap.com/currencies/the-graph/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coin Market Cap</a>. The Graph is for querying data that supports indexing data from networks such as <a href=""https://ipfs.tech/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">IPFS</a>, <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/education/what-is-ethereum/"">Ethereum</a> and POA with more networks planned.</p><blockquote><p>“Anyone can build and publish open APIs, called subgraphs, making data easily accessible.” (source: <a href=""https://thegraph.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">The Graph</a>)</p></blockquote><p>The Graph has a hosted service for developers to build on the platform. Already developers have deployed more than <a href=""https://thegraph.com/explorer"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">3,000 subgraphs</a> for DApps such as:&nbsp;</p><ul><li><a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/review/aave-lend/"">AAVE</a></li><li>Aragon</li><li>Balancer</li><li><a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/review/decentraland-mana/"">Decentraland</a></li><li>DAOstack</li><li>Gnosis</li><li>Livepeer</li><li>Loopring</li><li>Snapshot</li><li>Sushi – Mainnet</li><li>SushiSwap – Ethereum</li><li>Synthetix</li><li>Uniswap</li></ul><p>The Graph says that usage has averaged growth at over 50% month-on-month with billions of queries. It has a global community of over 2,000 curators and more than 200 Indexer Nodes in the <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/news/ethereum-testing-hard-fork-testnet/"">Testnet</a>. Community members helped raise funds along with many well-known VCs in the blockchain community like:</p><ul><li>Coinbase Ventures</li><li>CoinFund</li><li>DCG</li><li>DTC</li><li>Framework</li><li>ParaFi Capital</li><li>Multicoin</li><li>Reciprocal Ventures</li><li>SPC</li><li>Tally Capital and others</li></ul><p>Feel free to check out our in-depth article covering <a href=""/review/the-graph-grt/"">The Graph</a> in more detail</p><h2>What Makes The Graph Unique?</h2><p>Indexing <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/education/what-is-blockchain-technology/"">blockchain</a> data is challenging. The Graph’s mission is to create reliable decentralised public infrastructure for mainstream adoption. To ensure the network’s data integrity and economic security, participants use GRT (the Graph token), which is “locked up” by delegators, curators, and indexers, providing curating and indexing services on the Graph network.</p><p>The Graph learns what and how to index Ethereum data by its subgraph descriptions (the subgraph manifest):</p><ul><li>Smart contracts of interest for the subgraph</li><li>The events that are important in the contracts</li><li>The event data, which the Graph stores in its database</li></ul><p>Once the subgraph manifest is written, the definition is stored in IPFS using The Graph CLI. After that, it tells the indexer to index data for the specific subgraph.</p><blockquote><p>“A Global GraphQL API: Subgraphs can be composed into a global graph of all the world’s public information. This data can be transformed, organised, and shared across applications for anyone to query with just a few keystrokes.” (source: <a href=""https://thegraph.com/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">The Graph</a>)</p></blockquote><p>The Graph saves the significant engineering requirements of developing and operating proprietary indexing servers by reducing the hardware resources required.</p><p>Developers can now build DApps that provide agency, reliability, interoperability, security, and governance.</p><h2>Who Are the Founders of The Graph?</h2><p>The initial co-founding team includes Brandon Ramirez (research lead), Yaniv Tal (project lead), and Jannis Pohlmann (tech lead).</p><p>The founders are a cohesive team that has worked together for several years, and all have strong engineering backgrounds. Ramirez and Tal worked at MuleSoft (an API developer tools company later acquired by SalesForce).</p><p>The team have focused their careers on optimising the API stack and previously co-founded a developer tools startup where they built a custom framework on Datomic, an immutable database. Their vision was to use the GraphQL language to create immutable APIs and data access.</p><h3>The GRT Token</h3><p>GRT is an ERC-20 token, which is standard on the&nbsp;<a href=""https://ethereum.org/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Ethereum blockchain</a>. GRT has a total supply of 10,623,190,804 tokens.</p><ul><li>Indexers: Earn query fees and indexing rewards</li><li>Curators: Earn a portion of their income from subgraphs query fees they signal on</li><li>Delegators: Delegate to an indexer and receive of portion of their income generated</li></ul><p>Active curators, delegators, and indexers can earn GRT incentives from the Graph network proportional to their GRT stake and how much work they complete. The GRT token is available to purchase and trade on <a href=""https://www.kucoin.com/ucenter/signup?rcode=rJANMGN"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">KuCoin</a> and <a href=""https://accounts.binance.com/en/register?ref=WS9V0N8W"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Binance</a>.</p><h2>Fetch.AI (FET)</h2><figure class=""image""><a href=""https://fetch.ai/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener""><img src=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/fetchai_7227196598.jpg"" alt=""fetch.ai"" srcset=""https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/thumbnail_fetchai_7227196598.jpg 245w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/small_fetchai_7227196598.jpg 500w,https://image.coinbureau.dev/strapi/medium_fetchai_7227196598.jpg 750w,"" sizes=""100vw""></a><figcaption>Infrastructure For Smart, Autonomous Services: Image Source: <a href=""https://fetch.ai/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Fetch.ai</a></figcaption></figure><h3>What is Fetch.AI?</h3><p><a href=""https://fetch.ai/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Fetch AI</a> is an Ethereum layer-1 network founded in 2017. It acts as an interchain gateway to the blockchain universe. The combined features of artificial intelligence (AI) and blockchain form a decentralised, permissionless, machine-learning network. Users can link to and access secure and private datasets and perform tasks autonomously.</p><p>Fetch.ai is an ecosystem influenced by multi-gent Systems AI, adaptable to multiple stakeholder settings. FET is the Fetch project’s native crypto token for users to pay for activities on the Fetch network.</p><p>Fetch.ai optimises transportation networks such as parking, DeFi trading services, travel, and smart energy grids. Indeed, the Fetch protocol will work for any digital system reliant on large-scale datasets.</p><p>We have a dedicated article covering the ins and outs of <a href=""/review/fetch-fet/"">Fetch.AI</a> if you want to learn more about this project.</p><h2>What Makes Fetch.AI Unique?</h2><p>FET holders can create and deploy digital twins on the network, and developers use FET to access machine-learning utilities to deploy collective intelligence and train autonomous digital twins.</p><p>If you’re wondering what a digital twin is, <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_twin"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Wikipedia</a> gives a simple explanation below:</p><blockquote><p>“A digital twin is a digital representation of an intended or actual real-world physical product, system, or process (a physical twin) that serves as the effectively indistinguishable digital counterpart of it for practical purposes, such as simulation, integration, testing, monitoring, and maintenance.” (source: <a href=""https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_twin"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Wikipedia</a>)</p></blockquote><p>Validation nodes are enabled by users staking FET tokens, which helps to maintain network security and reputation.</p><h3>The Fetch.AI technology stack has four elements:</h3><ol><li>The Digital Twin Framework: This framework provides modular components that enable teams to build for digital twins to connect with, such as marketplaces, intelligence, and skills.</li><li>The Open Economic Framework: Enables the search and discovery functions of the digital twins.</li><li>The Digital Twin Metropolis: This is a collection of smart contracts that runs on a WASM (<a href=""https://internetcomputer.org/capabilities/webassembly"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">WebAssembly</a>) virtual machine and maintains the immutable agreement records between digital twins.</li><li>The Fetch.ai Blockchain: Using <a href=""https://plato.stanford.edu/entries/game-theory/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">game theory</a> and multi-party cryptography, the blockchain provides a secure, censorship-resistant consensus that supports smart contracts and rapid chain-syncing for digital twin applications.</li></ol><h2>Who Are the Founders of Fetch.AI?</h2><p>Toby Simpson (advisory board member), Thomas Hain (former COO) and Humayun Sheikh (CEO) and founder of itzME and uVue, founded Fetch.ai.</p><h3>The FET Token</h3><p>FET is the protocol’s utility token. It aims to help businesses and individuals autonomously and securely unlock and monetise their data value with ERC-20 smart contracts, called datasets. Previously, these datasets would be tricky to find and mostly unavailable. However, using the Ocean Protocol, users can buy and sell datasets.</p><p>A datatoken represents each data service, which can wrap a dataset to enable third parties on the platform to access the data without having to leave the security of the publisher’s enclave. You can find out more about this project in our <a href=""/review/ocean-protocol/"">Ocean Protocol Analysis</a>.&nbsp;</p><h2>What Makes Ocean Protocol Unique?</h2><p>The <a href=""/review/ocean-protocol/"">Ocean Protocol</a> gives users access to previously unavailable data. Anyone with datasets can tokenise their data and</p><p>Ocean Protocol unlocks access to data previously unavailable or tricky to access. The protocol allows anyone with datasets to tokenise their data. After that, it can be made available on the Ocean Market for others to access reliable data streams and create an income.</p><p>Businesses can use the Ocean Protocol for building and launching data markets of their own, which can be done by forking the Ocean Protocol or using Ocean Protocol React hooks.</p><h2>Who Are the Founders of Ocean Protocol?</h2><p>The core founding team of entrepreneurs and consultants has extensive experience with high-tech business growth and development.</p><ul><li>Bruce Pon is an international project manager and CEO of BigchainDB.</li><li>Cristina Pon is the marketing director for Ocean Protocol and BigchainDB.</li><li>Trent McConaghy is an AI expert and engineer.</li><li>Razvan Olteanu has over twenty years of management and technical experience in senior roles.</li></ul><p>In addition, the Ocean Protocol has an extensive team of advisors and experts in big data, blockchain, AI and business development.</p><h2>OCEAN: The Utility Token</h2><p>OCEAN tokens enable staking on datasets and gain community governance on data. The OCEAN-datatoken AMM pool establishes the price of datatokens, which adjusts with sales and purchases based on supply and demand.</p><p>OCEAN stakeholders become liquidity providers in the OCEAN-datatoken pool and receive a token stake pro-rata percentage of transaction fees from the pool.</p><p>Ocean Protocol (OCEAN) is in the top 150 cryptocurrencies on <a href=""https://coinmarketcap.com/currencies/ocean-protocol/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coin Market Cap</a> with a total supply of 1,410,000,000. Build a model using the example Python and R scripts. Everything you need to get started in one package.” (source: <a href=""https://numer.ai/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Numeraire</a>)</p></blockquote><p>NumerAI aims to introduce decentralisation to data sciences so developers can compete to create machine-learning prediction models.</p><p>Above all, NumerAI believes it is the first hedge fund to create a <a href=""https://{MIGRATED_DOMAIN}/education/cryptocurrency-beginners-guide/"">cryptocurrency</a> that changes how traditional hedge funds work. NumerAI uses machine learning for investment strategies using predictions and data from NumerAI tournament participants.</p><blockquote><p>“Start with hedge fund quality data. It is clean and regularised, designed to be usable right away. Subsequently, as more people enter and compete in the tournament, the token increases in value.</p><p>It is an innovative approach to stock trading, and Numerai is one of the few hedge funds relying on AI-generated data predictions.</p><h2>Who Are the Founders of Numeraire?</h2><p>Richard Craib is the CEO and founder of Numerai, who was voted Forbes 30 under 30 for his contribution to founding his first company.</p><h2>NMR: The Utility Token</h2><p>The NMR token is the platform’s native cryptocurrency, and NumerAI rewards participants with NMR tokens when their model performs well in competitions.</p><p>NumerAI (NMR) ranks in the top 300 on <a href=""https://coinmarketcap.com/currencies/numeraire/"" target=""_blank"" rel=""noopener"">Coin Market Cap</a> with a total supply of 11,000,000.
